## Phase 6: Auto-Concurrency Runtime

### v64 backend-first commits (Phase 6.3 promoted to v1)

> Graduated from [`brainstorming/archive/v64_backend_first_v1_concurrency.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v64_backend_first_v1_concurrency.md) (2026-05-09). Promotes Phase 6.3 from v1.1 to v1; stages 100K → 250K → 1M+; gates public v1 launch on M3. Spec at [`design.md § v1 Positioning — Backend-First`](../design.md#v1-positioning--backend-first).

- [x] **P0 architectural commit — Pre-implementation design audit shipped 2026-05-17.** All six subsections landed under design.md § Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform: {State-Machine Transform — Network-Boundary Functions, RAII Across Yield Points, Panic During Suspend, Debugger Contract Extension for Parked Tasks, FFI Across Yield Points, RC-Drop Ordering Across Yield Points}. The pre-implementation design surface that runtime engineering on the network event loop / state-machine transform must build against is now fully specified.
  1. [x] **State-machine transform spec — network-boundary functions only shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > State-Machine Transform — Network-Boundary Functions](../design.md#state-machine-transform--network-boundary-functions), plus a wrapper H3 intro that supersedes the "Phase 2 (v1.1)" framing per the v66 graduation and frames the six design audit subsections as a coherent v1 design surface. Spec covers: the lowering shape (state struct `__kara_state_f` + poll function returning `Poll[T, E]`; one state per yield point; captured-locals union packed across non-overlapping live ranges; heap allocation through the existing `allocates(Heap)` budget); yield-points scoped to network-effect call boundaries (not arbitrary statements — predictable small state count, surfaced through `karac explain`); trigger rule (post-inference effect set; private functions lowered without annotation when transitive); monomorphization interaction (transform runs after monomorphization, per-instantiation state struct, counts surfaced through `karac query monomorphization`); effect-polymorphic generics (per-(types, effects) state machine; closure composition extends yield-point set); debug-info preservation (DWARF + source-map fields named for source bindings, switch arms mapped to statement spans, yield points carry call-site + callee name — debugger sees source view identical to thread-blocked syscall); error-path lowering (`?` integrated into state machine; state-struct destructor invokes reverse-construction-order drop before `Err` return; user-visible `?` semantics unchanged); FFI prohibition (forward-declared cross-link to sub-item 5; unsafe escape hatch with `// Safety:` documentation per `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`); cancellation cooperation (poll function checks cancel flag at each yield, unwinds via state-struct destructor); layer classification (state-struct layout / tag encoding / IR shape = Implementation freedom; yield-and-resume value preservation + cancellation observation + match-no-yield call/return semantics = Guaranteed; state-struct field naming through `karac explain` = Reported, evolves with the same discipline as other `karac explain` output). Cross-references to RC-Drop Ordering (sub-item 6), Debugger Contract Extension (sub-item 4), and FFI-Across-Yield (sub-item 5) are forward-declared and resolve as those slices land. Adds one TOC entry between "Runtime Distribution" and "Explicit Concurrency: `par {}` and `spawn()`". Files: `docs/design.md`. **Unblocks** sub-items 2-6 (they all reference the state-machine lowering vocabulary established here — state struct, poll function, yield point, captured locals, state-struct destructor).
  2. [x] **RAII-across-yield as compile error spec shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > RAII Across Yield Points](../design.md#raii-across-yield-points). Spec covers: the rule (network-boundary function cannot hold a non-cancel-safe binding live across any yield point — typechecker check that fires per-yield-point, reusing the existing live-range pass); the `CancelSafe` marker trait (user-extensible `pub marker trait CancelSafe;` per the existing marker-trait infrastructure); semantic contract (a `T : CancelSafe` impl declares that drop-under-cancellation leaves owned resources in a sound state — safety claim, not UB guarantee; wrong impl yields leaks, not undefined behavior); the v1 stdlib `CancelSafe` set (primitives; `String` / collection types when element-type-`CancelSafe`; `Box` / `Arc` / `Rc` when wrapped-type-`CancelSafe`; lock guards; network connection types — `TcpConnection` / `TlsStream` / `HttpConnection`; `par struct` / `par enum` per-field transitively); the v1 stdlib NON-cancel-safe set (`File` before fsync; `BufReader` while buffer non-empty; `BufWriter` while buffer non-empty — released by `flush()`; database transaction handles pre-commit; critical-section guards on embedded profiles; raw pointers; `shared struct` / `shared enum` with `Rc`-rooted reachability); diagnostic shape (`error[E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD]: holding '<name>' (type '<T>') across a suspension point is not cancel-safe` with the binding-construction span, the yield-point span, the cancel-leak `note`, two fix-its in preferred order — release-before-yield then `impl CancelSafe` — and a footnote linking the design.md section); check site (typechecker, after effect inference, before state-machine transform — so the transform never lowers a rejected function); `unsafe` interaction (does NOT bypass the rule — `unsafe` grants unsafe-op capability, not cancellation-contract bypass); orphan rule (user-package author can impl for own types per standard marker-trait orphan rules; stdlib impl additions are additive / non-breaking); layer classification (rule = Guaranteed semantics; stdlib `CancelSafe` set = Reported behavior with version skew tolerated; diagnostic wording = Reported per the general carve-out). Files: `docs/design.md`. **Unblocks** the typechecker implementation of the `E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD` check (Phase 6 codegen-adjacent work; can land at typechecker layer ahead of runtime engineering).
  3. [x] **Panic-during-suspend semantics spec shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > Panic During Suspend](../design.md#panic-during-suspend). Spec covers: the two trigger scenarios (parked task panics on resume; parked task observes sibling fail-fast cancellation); the four-rule cleanup semantics — (a) local cleanup runs via state-struct destructor invoking RC-drops + defer / errdefer in reverse construction order, identical contract to a stack-blocking task panicking at a syscall; (b) parent task observes panic via `WaitTarget` + parent-frame chain walk per the debugger contract — `TaskHandle.join()` returns `Err(panic)` or the enclosing `par {}` routes per dominance rule; (c) sibling tasks in same `par {}` cancel cooperatively at next yield via existing fail-fast — no new mechanism; (d) provider-rooted resources released through normal scope-exit RC-drop path — no new provider release path. Interaction with `catch_panic` — absorbs panics from yield-bearing closures exactly as in synchronous code; the network boundary is NOT an `extern "C"` boundary so the absorbed-panic-to-abort translation does not apply (panic propagates upward through Kāra frames using the normal unwind path). Double-panic during state-struct unwind aborts identically to synchronous double-panic per existing `catch_panic` contract (`panic_kind: "drop_during_unwind"`). Narrow corner case — panic between cancel-flag check and park syscall unwinds the state struct as if cancellation observed; live-range analysis guarantees no torn state. `std.runtime::list_tasks()` safe to call from panic-hook during cascade. Layer classification — four-rule cleanup contract = Guaranteed; stack-frame walking strategy for parent-join surfacing = Implementation freedom; crash-report content follows existing Crash Report Format (Reported behavior). Files: `docs/design.md`. **Unblocks** the runtime engineering work that lowers panic semantics across the state-machine boundary.
  4. [x] **Debugger contract for parked tasks spec shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > Debugger Contract Extension for Parked Tasks](../design.md#debugger-contract-extension-for-parked-tasks). Spec covers: explicit extension of the four existing debugger-contract elements at design.md § 3. Debugger Contract to network-event-loop-parked tasks. Element 1 — SpawnSiteIds inherited from the nearest enclosing par {} / spawn() / TaskGroup site; the event loop itself is not a spawn site. Element 2 — parent-frame reference set at network-boundary function entry, preserved in the state struct's metadata header across yield-and-resume cycles, survives unwind (drives the panic-surfacing rule in Panic During Suspend). Element 3 — typed `WaitTarget` enum with three variants: `NetworkIo { fd: RawFd, direction: IoDirection, timeout: Option[Duration] }` (the v1 network-event-loop contribution — RawFd exposure enables debugger correlation with lsof / netstat), `Timer { deadline: Instant }`, `Channel { receiver_id, side }`. Element 4 — `std.runtime::list_tasks()` returns parked tasks alongside thread-blocking / synchronously-running tasks; each entry carries TaskId, yield-point source location + callee name, WaitTarget variant + payload, effect summary, SpawnSiteId, parent-frame reference. Same data appears in the structured crash report. Profile-gated metadata emission follows the existing rule (default-on dev, default-off release; embedded / isr default off, incompatible with `panics_off`). Stability — `WaitTarget.NetworkIo` payload (`fd` / `direction` / `timeout`) part of the language-level contract, stable within a major version; new variants additive (e.g., GPU-fence wait targets for future GPU backend); existing variants cannot change shape without edition migration. v1 deliverables = metadata emission + typed WaitTarget + list_tasks() extension + profile-gating wiring. Out of scope = gdb / lldb plugins, DAP-server task views, profiler GUIs (downstream consumers). Layer classification — Reported behavior surface (per existing § 3 Debugger Contract rule); NetworkIo variant shape is itself Reported; additive evolution across releases. Files: `docs/design.md`. **Unblocks** the runtime metadata emission engineering (the WaitTarget enum + per-task header layout) and the list_tasks() implementation extension.
  5. [x] **FFI-across-yield spec shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > FFI Across Yield Points](../design.md#ffi-across-yield-points). Spec covers: the rule (network-boundary function cannot make an `extern "C"` or `extern "C-unwind"` call across a yield point; FFI boundary must complete before yield — typechecker check that fires structurally on the call expression + yield-point interleave); the `E_FFI_ACROSS_YIELD` diagnostic shape with both call sites and yield site annotated, and the canonical fix-it (extract cross-yield work into a non-yielding helper); the rationale (foreign code makes synchronous-progress assumption; suspending the C frame requires either non-portable mechanisms — ucontext / fibers, prohibitive cost + edge cases — or abandoning the foreign frame with held heap / fd / lock leaks; FFI boundary is transactional from Kāra's perspective); `extern "C-unwind"` interaction (unwind is a synchronous return, rule's invariant holds identically); `unsafe`-block interaction (does NOT bypass the rule by default; narrow `// Safety:`-documented escape hatch matches the state-machine transform spec's unsafe carve-out for niche cases — custom event-loop adapters, embedded, signal integrations); rationale for hard error vs. warning (yield-interleave at runtime produces torn foreign state → memory corruption / double-frees / fd leaks / silent wrong results — undebuggable; rule pays cost up front to avoid runtime defects); `#[noblock]` case (rule applies uniformly to blocking and non-blocking FFI — helper extraction is cheap, special-casing pure-CPU FFI complicates rule for marginal benefit). Layer classification — rule = Guaranteed; diagnostic wording = Reported; unsafe-block escape hatch = Guaranteed (spec'd exception) but `// Safety:` comment content is uninterpreted by the compiler. Files: `docs/design.md`. **Unblocks** the typechecker implementation of `E_FFI_ACROSS_YIELD` (sits alongside the `E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD` check; both read the same per-yield-point live-range data the state-machine transform's check site already builds).
  6. [x] **RC-drop ordering across yield points spec shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed as design.md § [Network Event Loop and State-Machine Transform > RC-Drop Ordering Across Yield Points](../design.md#rc-drop-ordering-across-yield-points). Spec covers: the rule (state-struct destructor invokes drops on bindings live at the active yield point in source-level reverse construction order — `drop(l_n), drop(l_{n-1}), ..., drop(l_1)` — identical to non-yielding scope-exit drop ordering); rationale for explicit specification (user code relies on resource ordering during cancellation cleanup — e.g., TcpConnection-then-MetricsCounter construction guarantees counter dropped first, connection second, so the metric side-effect is visible before the peer-FIN); worked example with a TcpConnection + MetricsCounter pair making the ordering observable; state-struct field layout independence (transform's overlapping-storage / cache-locality / split-field choices are Implementation freedom; drop order keys off the source-level construction-order metadata the destructor consults, never off physical field layout); `defer` / `errdefer` interleave (existing LIFO scope-exit cleanup rules from Error Handling, interleaved with RC drops per the source-level live-range pass — yielding does not change the interleave); per-yield drop set (drops invoked on cancellation = bindings whose source live range includes the active yield point; bindings constructed after Y or moved out before Y are not in Y's drop set — same live-set machinery the RAII-Across-Yield check consumes); partial-drop guarantee (destructor-panicking-during-unwind aborts process per double-panic prohibition; no drops after the panicking destructor run); RC vs. owned drops (rule applies uniformly — owned values, Rc[T], Arc[T], shared struct, par struct all drop in source-level reverse construction order); cross-package observability (the drop order is part of the language-level contract; library authors with side-effecting Drop impls can rely on the documented order). Layer classification — rule = Guaranteed; state-struct construction-order metadata representation = Implementation freedom; karac explain per-yield-point drop list = Reported behavior. Files: `docs/design.md`. **Final sub-item — closes the design audit.** Sub-items 1+2+3+4+5+6 all shipped; parent line 7 flipped to [x]. The v1 design surface for the network-event-loop story is now consolidated, and runtime engineering on the state-machine transform can begin without re-opening language-level design questions under deadline pressure.

- [x] **P0 — Network event loop runtime (epoll / kqueue / IOCP) substrate shipped 2026-05-17.** Cross-platform fd-readiness abstraction landed at `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` via `mio` 1.x — the canonical Rust crate that wraps epoll (edge-triggered by default on Linux), kqueue (macOS / BSD), and IOCP (Windows) behind a uniform `Poll` / `Token` / `event::Source` API. v1 architecture: single `EventLoop` instance per process, `!Sync` and pinned to its constructing thread (the architectural commitment "single OS thread per event loop in v1"); M2 / M3 multi-loop sharding will re-use the type unchanged. Crate-internal API (no FFI exposure, no public language surface): `IoDirection` (Read / Write / ReadWrite, `repr(u8)` to pin the discriminant for the codegen parking-emit ABI when phase-6 line 17 lands); `RegistrationToken` (opaque handle round-tripped through `Wakeup`); `EventLoop::{new, register, deregister, run_once, handle}`; `EventLoopHandle::{clone, wake}`. Per-fd state (`FdState`) stores the parked-task pointer (`*mut c_void`, type-erased so the codegen parking path owns its concrete representation), I/O direction, and optional deadline — matches the line-15 spec exactly. Cross-thread wakeup goes through `mio::Waker`, which lowers to eventfd on Linux, a pipe pair on BSD / macOS, and a posted IOCP completion packet on Windows — the three OS primitives the line-15 entry calls out by name. 6 unit tests pin the surface: construction succeeds; cross-thread wake unblocks a long `run_once` well under the 2 s safety bound; fd-readiness on a `TcpListener` round-trips the registered parked pointer + direction back through `Wakeup`; deregister removes the entry from internal state; timeout-only `run_once` returns empty wakeups; sequential registrations get distinct tokens; `IoDirection::to_interest()` covers all three arms. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` suite passes with zero regressions (1044 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green). **Verification status:** local development host is macOS (kqueue path through mio) — all 6 unit tests pass. Linux (epoll) and Windows (IOCP) parity is `mio`'s responsibility, not ours, since the same `Poll` / `Waker` / `event::Source` API resolves to the platform-native backend at compile time; CI cross-platform validation will catch any platform-specific regression when the workspace's CI shape evolves to cover those hosts. **Out-of-scope at line 15 substrate (carried under separate tracker entries):** timer-wheel-driven deadline expiry (the `deadline` field is stored per spec; M2 polish layer's timer-wheel implementation reads from it without re-shaping the per-fd state — see the M2 entry below); FFI wrappers (`karac_runtime_event_loop_*`) that codegen calls into (phase-6 line 17 — effect-routed task parking — is the binding pass); multi-loop sharding (M2 / M3). Files: `runtime/Cargo.toml` (mio dep promoted from transitive-via-tokio to direct), `runtime/src/lib.rs` (one-line `pub mod event_loop;`), `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (new — ~320 lines including 6 tests). **Unblocks** phase-6 line 17 (effect-routed task parking) and phase-6 line 18 (state-machine transform codegen — network-boundary functions only) — both consume the `EventLoop::register` + `run_once` shape and the round-tripped parked-pointer.

- [~] **P0 — Effect-routed task parking.** Codegen path: a function call whose target carries `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)` lowers to "register fd with event loop, park current task, yield." On readiness wakeup, the event loop schedules the parked task back onto the work-stealing pool. The routing is automatic from the effect signature — user code stays plain function calls. Distinct from explicit `par {}` block scheduling; complementary to it (a `par {}` block whose branches contain network calls fans out across the event loop).
  1. [x] **Slice 1 — runtime FFI surface shipped 2026-05-17.** Landed in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`. Four `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` entry points the codegen-emitted IR will call into: `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd(raw_fd: i32, direction: u8, parked: *mut c_void) -> u64` (unix, returns a non-zero token on success; 0 = error or invalid direction byte), `karac_runtime_event_loop_deregister_fd(raw_fd: i32, token: u64) -> i32` (unix, 0 = success / -1 = error), `karac_runtime_event_loop_poll(max_wait_nanos: i64, wakeups_out: *mut KaracWakeup, max_wakeups: usize) -> usize` (cross-platform; -1 = block indefinitely, 0 = non-blocking, n > 0 = wait n ns), and `karac_runtime_event_loop_wake() -> i32` (cross-platform). `KaracWakeup` is `#[repr(C)] { token: u64, parked: *mut c_void, direction: u8 }` — the entry written into the caller-allocated buffer by `poll`. Process-global event loop is lazily initialized under `OnceLock<Mutex<EventLoop>>` — v1 prioritizes correctness over throughput (register / deregister / poll serialize through the global lock); M2 polish layer may split into a clonable `mio::Registry` handle + dedicated poller thread without changing the FFI signature. Unix-only on the fd-registration entries (`mio::unix::SourceFd` wraps the raw fd to talk to epoll / kqueue); Windows IOCP integration uses a completion-based model rather than fd-readiness, so its FFI surface looks different and lands separately. **Tests** — one comprehensive integration test (`ffi_round_trip_register_poll_deregister_wake`) exercising the full round trip: bind a `std::net::TcpListener`, register its raw fd; verify invalid-direction-byte path returns 0; connect from another thread to trigger readability; poll into a stack-allocated `[KaracWakeup; 4]` buffer; verify the wakeup carries the registered token + parked pointer + direction byte; deregister; call `wake`; verify the next poll returns immediately and writes zero entries (waker filtered at the `EventLoop` layer); verify non-blocking poll returns 0 in <100 ms. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (1044 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green). `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` updated: 37 → 41 `#[no_mangle]` exports, with the new `event_loop.rs` section documenting C ABI signatures. Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (FFI surface block + integration test added; ~200 lines), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (new section + summary count bump). **Remaining slices under this entry:** scheduler-side glue (event-loop thread drives the work-stealing pool with wakeups → poll function invocations); codegen-side network-effect identification pass (lookup effect signatures at each call site to recognize `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)`); codegen-side lowering at each yield point (depends on phase-6 line 18's state-machine transform — the lowering shape itself); Windows IOCP integration (different model from fd-readiness). **Unblocks** phase-6 line 18 (state-machine transform codegen): the FFI ABI it emits register / poll calls against is now stable.
  2. [x] **Slice 2 — parked-task ABI (`KaracParkedTask` + `KaracPollResult`) shipped 2026-05-17.** Repr-C value types added to `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` that codegen-emitted state machines populate at the network-effect call boundary. `KaracPollResult` is `#[repr(u8)] #[non_exhaustive] { Pending = 0, Ready = 1, Err = 2 }` — discriminants pinned by a test (`karac_poll_result_discriminants_match_codegen_abi`) so accidental reordering breaks compilation; `non_exhaustive` reserves the variant space for future additions like `Cancelled` (cooperative-cancellation lowering) without an ABI-break (existing discriminants stay put). `KaracParkedTask` is `#[repr(C)] { poll_fn: unsafe extern "C" fn(*mut c_void, *const AtomicBool) -> u8, state: *mut c_void }` — mirrors `KaracBranch`'s two-pointer shape exactly so the scheduler integration can share dispatch machinery between branch tasks and parked tasks when it lands. The `*const AtomicBool` cancel arg mirrors `KaracBranch::func`'s convention: the poll function reads it at each yield point to observe cooperative cancellation, unwinding via the state-struct destructor and returning `Err` (or a future `Cancelled` variant) on a true read. Layout pinned by `karac_parked_task_layout_pinned` (`size = 2 * size_of::<usize>()`, `align = align_of::<usize>()`). `Send` impl declared on `KaracParkedTask` — soundness inherited from the cross-task-safe check applied to captured locals when the surrounding network-boundary function is called from `par {}` / `spawn` / `TaskGroup` (per design.md § Structured Concurrency Lifetime Guarantees, already enforced structurally). **End-to-end driver test** (`parked_task_drives_to_completion_through_ffi_surface`, unix-only) hand-rolls a 2-state machine (`HandRolledState { tag, listener_fd, token, ready_observed }`) that simulates what codegen will emit: state 0 calls `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd` and returns `Pending`; state 1 (entered after the driver loop pumps the event loop on `Pending` and re-invokes `poll_fn`) deregisters and returns `Ready`. Test drives the state machine through a tight test-only loop (`poll_fn → if Ready/Err break → else event_loop_poll → loop`, bounded by 8 iterations as a safety bound), connects from a worker thread to trigger listener readability, verifies the state machine reached state 1 with `ready_observed = true`. The driver loop lives in test code — production scheduler integration (event-loop thread + work-stealing pool dispatch) is the still-remaining slice that replaces this with a non-blocking driver. New test-binary-scoped `FFI_TEST_LOCK` (`Mutex<()>`) added to serialize tests that touch the process-global event loop; existing `ffi_round_trip_register_poll_deregister_wake` retrofitted to acquire it, new driver test acquires it. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (1055 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green). No new `#[no_mangle]` exports — slice 2 is a type ABI commitment, not an FFI function expansion; `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` unchanged. Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~180 lines incl. 3 new tests + lock harness). **Unblocks** the codegen-side state-machine transform (phase-6 line 18) which can now emit code that populates `KaracParkedTask` against a stable Rust-side definition. **Remaining slices under this entry:** scheduler-side glue (production driver replacing the test-only loop — event-loop thread enqueues parked tasks back onto the work-stealing pool on wakeup, workers re-poll); codegen network-effect identification (the recognition pass at each call site); codegen lowering at yield points (depends on line 18); Windows IOCP integration.
  3. [x] **Slice 3 — background poller thread + wakeup queue (with `EventLoop` refactor) shipped 2026-05-17.** `EventLoop` refactored to be `Sync` instead of `!Sync` — interior now splits into two independently-locked halves: a `Mutex<EventLoopPoll>` (held for the duration of each blocking `mio::Poll::poll` call) and a `Mutex<EventLoopFds>` (held briefly by register / deregister, and during post-poll wakeup-extraction). Owned `mio::Registry` clone added (mio::Registry is `Sync`, so register / deregister calls hit the OS syscalls without external serialization). Process-global slot changed from `OnceLock<Mutex<EventLoop>>` to `OnceLock<Arc<EventLoop>>`. The lock split is what makes the background poller architecturally sound: the poller thread blocks indefinitely in `run_once` holding the poll Mutex, but concurrent registrations from other threads acquire only the fds Mutex and proceed without contention. The original `OnceLock<Mutex<EventLoop>>` design deadlocked because registration and polling competed for the same lock; this refactor lands alongside the poller for that reason. Three new `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` entry points implement the background-poller surface: `karac_runtime_event_loop_start_background_thread() -> i32` (idempotent thread spawn — second call returns 0 without re-spawn), `karac_runtime_event_loop_take_wakeups(out, max, timeout_nanos) -> usize` (drain queued wakeups into a caller-allocated buffer; -1 = block, 0 = non-blocking, n > 0 = wait n ns; uses an internal `VecDeque<KaracWakeup>` + `Condvar`), `karac_runtime_event_loop_shutdown_background_thread() -> i32` (signal stop, fire the cross-thread waker, notify the queue Condvar, join the thread, clear the global slot — supports re-start after shutdown within the same process; -1 if not running). `karac_runtime_event_loop_poll` now short-circuits to return 0 immediately when the background thread is running so direct FFI poll callers don't contend for the poll Mutex (documented behavior — callers should use `take_wakeups` while the background thread owns polling). `KaracWakeup` declared `unsafe impl Send` since wakeups now cross threads through the queue (the contained `*mut c_void` is opaque to the runtime — pointer-lifetime correctness is the codegen parking path's responsibility). **6 new tests** pin the background-poller surface (all under a per-test `BackgroundPollerTestGuard` that acquires `FFI_TEST_LOCK` + ensures clean teardown via a Drop impl that calls `shutdown_background_thread`): drain via take_wakeups end-to-end (bind listener → register → trigger readability from another thread → take_wakeups → verify round-trip of token/parked/direction), non-blocking take returns 0 on empty queue, take with 100 ms timeout actually waits ~100 ms and returns 0, start is idempotent (second call returns 0), shutdown on already-stopped state returns -1, direct FFI poll short-circuits to 0 in <100 ms when background is running. **The original `EventLoop` API methods** (`register` / `deregister` / `run_once`) changed signature from `&mut self` to `&self` (interior mutability). Existing internal-API tests' `let mut ev = EventLoop::new()` updated to `let ev = EventLoop::new()` (4 sites) — drops the unused `mut` per clippy. `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` updated: 41 → 44 `#[no_mangle]` exports, new event_loop.rs table rows for the three new entries. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (1055 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green; 16 event_loop tests pass, 6 new + 10 pre-existing). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (~520 lines added incl. refactor + background-poller block + 6 tests), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (3 new table rows + summary count bump). **Unblocks** the production scheduler-glue slice: wakeups now flow through a runtime-owned queue that any consumer (the eventual work-stealing pool integration) can drain from. **Remaining slices under this entry:** scheduler glue (drain `take_wakeups` from a worker — each wakeup carries a parked-task pointer the worker can invoke `poll_fn` on); codegen network-effect identification (the recognition pass at each call site); codegen lowering at yield points (depends on line 18); Windows IOCP integration.
  4. [x] **Slice 4 — scheduler dispatcher thread (drains wakeups + re-polls parked tasks) shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the loop from event-loop readiness back to state-machine resume. A background dispatcher thread (separate from the slice-3 poller thread) drains `karac_runtime_event_loop_take_wakeups` in a 100 ms-timeout loop and, for each wakeup, interprets the `parked` field as `*const KaracParkedTask` and invokes `(task.poll_fn)(task.state, &disp.cancel)`. The interpretation convention — `parked = *const KaracParkedTask` — is what codegen (when state-machine lowering lands at phase 6 line 18) will follow when registering fds at network-effect call boundaries. Two new `#[no_mangle] extern "C"` entry points: `karac_runtime_scheduler_start_dispatcher() -> i32` (auto-starts the background poller if not running — `take_wakeups` depends on it; idempotent; returns 0 on success), `karac_runtime_scheduler_shutdown_dispatcher() -> i32` (sets shutdown flag, joins the thread within one 100 ms poll cycle without explicit signaling, clears the global slot — supports re-start; does NOT shut down the background poller, which has its own FFI). Dispatcher state tracks four `AtomicU64` counters (polls, ready_observations, err_observations, pending_observations) for test verification + future diagnostics; counters are `Relaxed`-ordered (monotonic-write visibility is sufficient, no cross-counter ordering needed). Process-global cancel flag is a placeholder for v1 — a single `AtomicBool` that's always `false` — passed to every `poll_fn` invocation. Per-par-block cancel routing (so a parked task inside a fail-fast `par {}` observes its block's cancel flag) is later integration work; the FFI surface stays stable because the cancel pointer for production codegen will come from the task's own `state` struct, not from the dispatcher arg. **Lifetime convention.** Codegen owns the `KaracParkedTask` + `state` struct lifetime from the `register_fd` call until `poll_fn` returns `Ready` or `Err`; the dispatcher never allocates or frees, it only invokes `poll_fn` through the type-erased pointers. NULL `parked` is gracefully skipped (a wakeup with no associated task — e.g., a pre-dispatcher-era test that registered with a raw marker — is silently dropped rather than crashing on a NULL deref). **3 new tests**: `dispatcher_drives_parked_task_to_completion_on_wakeup` (unix-only) hand-rolls a 2-state machine inside a heap-pinned `Box<SchedulerTestState>` (tag 0 → registered, tag 1 → completion signaled via internal `AtomicBool`); the initial poll is invoked by the test thread to transition tag 0 → 1; a connector thread triggers listener readability; the dispatcher's wakeup-drain invokes `poll_fn` (state 1 case) which sets `completed = true`; test spin-waits for the AtomicBool with a 2 s safety bound. `dispatcher_start_is_idempotent` (second start while running returns 0 without re-spawning). `dispatcher_shutdown_returns_minus_one_when_not_running` (shutdown on already-stopped state). All under a per-test `SchedulerTestGuard` that acquires `FFI_TEST_LOCK` + shuts down both dispatcher and poller on Drop. `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` updated: 44 → 46 `#[no_mangle]` exports. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across 40 test binaries (1055 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green; 19 event_loop tests pass — 3 new + 16 pre-existing). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~200 lines: dispatcher block + 3 tests), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (2 new table rows + summary count bump). **The runtime-side scheduler integration for line 17 is now complete:** event loop substrate (line 15) → FFI surface (slice 1) → parked-task ABI (slice 2) → background poller + queue (slice 3) → scheduler dispatcher (slice 4). What remains under line 17 is purely codegen-side: the network-effect identification pass and the lowering at yield points (lowering depends on phase-6 line 18's state-machine transform). **Remaining slices under this entry:** codegen network-effect identification at each call site; codegen lowering at yield points (depends on line 18); Windows IOCP integration.
  5. [x] **Slice 5 — scheduler stats snapshot FFI shipped 2026-05-17.** Exposes the dispatcher's four `AtomicU64` counters (introduced in slice 4 for internal use) through a single FFI entry point: `karac_runtime_scheduler_stats_snapshot(out: *mut KaracSchedulerStats) -> i32` reads the counters with `Relaxed` ordering and writes them into the caller-allocated buffer; returns 0 on success, -1 if the dispatcher is not running. `KaracSchedulerStats` is `#[repr(C)] { polls, ready_observations, err_observations, pending_observations: u64 }` — the counter invariant is `polls == ready + err + pending`, with the caveat that snapshots can transiently violate this invariant by ±1 because the four loads are independent (counters are cross-thread monotonic, but Relaxed ordering doesn't enforce cross-field consistency). Useful for diagnostics, tests, and future profiling integration. **2 new tests**: `scheduler_stats_snapshot_returns_minus_one_when_dispatcher_not_running` (sanity-check of the not-running path) and `scheduler_stats_track_dispatcher_polls` (drive one parked task to completion using the same heap-pinned 2-state machine as slice 4, snapshot before and after, verify polls ≥ 1, ready_observations ≥ 1, and the polls = ready + err + pending invariant holds at the after-snapshot). All clear under clippy + fmt + full LLVM gate (1055 typechecker + 488 codegen E2E + 215 memory_sanitizer + ... all green across 40 binaries; 21 event_loop tests pass — 2 new + 19 pre-existing). `SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` updated: 46 → 47 `#[no_mangle]` exports. Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~120 lines: FFI block + 2 tests), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (1 new table row + summary count bump). **Runtime side of line 17 is now substantively complete** — substrate (line 15) → FFI (slice 1) → ABI (slice 2) → poller + queue (slice 3) → dispatcher (slice 4) → stats observability (slice 5). The two remaining items (codegen integration and Windows IOCP) are tracked as sub-items 6 + 7 below.

[x] **Slice 6 — codegen network-effect identification + lowering at yield points shipped 2026-05-24.** Identification half remained as shipped 2026-05-17 (`Program.callee_network_yield_effect` via `Pipeline::effectcheck`); lowering half ships the `karac_park_on_fd(fd: i32, direction: u8)` compiler-recognised leaf parking primitive. **Design call (resolved this slice):** the v1 convention is one reserved-name leaf primitive that all stdlib network types (`TcpListener.accept`, `TcpStream.read`, …) call from their bodies — fd + direction flow as explicit arguments at the leaf boundary, and effect inference propagates the network-yield classification up the call graph through existing infrastructure. Single special case in codegen (the leaf's poll-fn body); higher-level callers compose through the existing slice 8d/8e caller intercept unchanged. Matches Rust async's `await`-on-leaf-future shape; avoids the "every network-effect call emits register_fd" alternative which had no good fd-extraction story and didn't compose. **Emitted shape (one leaf, hand-rolled):** `karac_park_on_fd`'s state struct gains a trailing `{poll_fn: ptr, state: ptr}` `KaracParkedTask` field (`emit_state_struct_type_for_key`); the constructor `__kara_state_new_karac_park_on_fd` initialises it with `{__kara_poll_karac_park_on_fd, state_ptr_self}` after forward-declaring the poll fn to take its address (the poll-fn pass uses `get_function` to reuse the forward declaration so no duplicate symbol arises). Poll-fn `__kara_poll_karac_park_on_fd` body bypasses the body-split walker (kara-source body is empty — it IS the yield, not a function that contains one) and emits a hand-rolled 2-state machine: entry calls `karac_runtime_event_loop_start_background_thread()` for idempotent bootstrap then switches on the tag; state_0 loads fd (field 1) + direction (field 2), GEPs `&parked_task` (field 3 — under opaque pointers with consecutive same-aligned ptr fields the address equals `&KaracParkedTask`), calls `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd(fd, dir, parked)`, advances tag → 1, returns Pending; state_1 allocas a `{i64, ptr, i8}` `KaracWakeup` buffer, calls `karac_runtime_event_loop_take_wakeups(buf, 1, -1)` blocking, returns Ready (v1 single-task model — the only registered fd is ours so any wakeup is ours; buffer contents discarded). Composition with higher-level callers: the existing caller intercept (slice 8d/8e) routes `karac_park_on_fd(fd, dir)` through `__kara_state_new_karac_park_on_fd` + poll-loop unchanged — `driver()` calling the leaf looks identical in IR to any other network-boundary fn call, Pending propagates up through the spin loop. The standard `cli::build_state_struct_layouts` skips leaf-effect functions whose body has no yield-point sub-call (existing presence rule), so codegen synthesizes the layout for `karac_park_on_fd` locally via `synthesize_park_on_fd_layout` and tail-emits state struct + constructor + poll fn in each of the three emission passes when the function declaration is present. **Runtime FFI declarations** added to `Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd(i32, i8, ptr) -> i64`, `karac_runtime_event_loop_take_wakeups(ptr, i64, i64) -> i64`, `karac_runtime_event_loop_start_background_thread() -> i32` — all three already shipped on the runtime side (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`). **6 IR-grep tests** pin the wiring: state struct carries tag + 2 trailing ptrs; constructor stores poll-fn ptr + self-state ptr into the parked_task fields; poll-fn state_0 calls register_fd with `&parked_task`; poll-fn state_1 calls take_wakeups; poll-fn entry calls start_background_thread; the caller (a `driver(socket_fd: i32) { karac_park_on_fd(socket_fd, 0); }` shape) routes through the slice-8d state-machine constructor + poll-loop intercept. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (782 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1230 typechecker + … all green across 45+ test binaries). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (`Codegen::new` FFI block, +~55 lines), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (`KARAC_PARK_ON_FD` constant + `synthesize_park_on_fd_layout` + state-struct trailing-field push + constructor parked-task init + `emit_park_on_fd_poll_body` helper + tail-emit hooks in the three orchestration passes, +~240 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (+6 tests + `function_body` extraction helper, +~180 lines). **What's deferred to follow-on slices (not gated by Slice 6):** (1) a programmatic end-to-end park-and-wake test that binds a TCP listener from Rust, runs a kara binary that calls `karac_park_on_fd(listener_fd, 0)`, connects from a worker thread to trigger readability, and verifies the binary returns Ready and exits cleanly — IR-grep coverage proves the wiring is correct, but behavioural exercise needs a test harness that's a slice in itself (~1-2 hours); (2) stdlib `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` / `WebSocket` skeleton types that wrap raw fds and call `karac_park_on_fd` from their methods — M1+ stdlib work that builds on the primitive shipped here. **Unblocked:** parent entry's remaining slice is Windows IOCP (Slice 9), correctly blocked by its own "Windows CI infrastructure setup" gate. Slices 7 (programmatic park-and-wake E2E) and 8 (stdlib TcpListener composing through karac_park_on_fd) both ship below.

[x] **Slice 7 — programmatic park-and-wake E2E test shipped 2026-05-24.** Validates the codegen↔runtime bridge for `karac_park_on_fd` under real I/O — Slice 6's IR-grep tests prove the emitted shape is correct, but until this slice the actual end-to-end behaviour (calling convention into `karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd`, `KaracParkedTask` layout under opaque pointers, state_1 blocking `take_wakeups` semantics, parked-pointer round-trip through the event loop's wakeup queue) had never been exercised at runtime. Round-trip works first try after rebase — wiring confirmed sound, no latent bugs in the bridge. **Shape:** a 5-line kara source (declared in `tests/park_and_wake.rs` inline) binds a TCP listener via a new test-only FFI, calls `karac_park_on_fd(fd, 0u8)`, prints `WOKEN` and exits; the Rust harness spawns the binary, reads `BOUND_PORT=<n>` from stdout (same convention as `tests/http_server.rs`), connects to the port from the test thread to trigger readability, then `try_wait`-loops with a 10 s ceiling for the child to exit. End-to-end completion observed at ~4.6 s wall clock (dominated by runtime build + kara compile; the park→wake round trip itself completes in milliseconds once the binary is running). **Test-only FFI:** `karac_runtime_test_bind_and_print_port() -> i32` in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` behind a new `test-helpers` cargo feature (gated by `#[cfg(all(unix, feature = "test-helpers"))]`); binds 127.0.0.1:0, prints `BOUND_PORT=<port>` and flushes stdout, returns the raw fd via `IntoRawFd::into_raw_fd` (no destructor — the fd outlives this call so the parking primitive can register against it). The cargo feature gate keeps the symbol out of production binaries; the test harness's `runtime_path()` builds with `--features test-helpers`. **kara source surface checks (passive):** the test exercises `unsafe extern "C" { fn ...() -> i32; }` block syntax + free-fn FFI calls + `effect resource Network` + body-less function-as-leaf-primitive pattern + `let dir: u8 = 0u8` (typed-literal suffix required: `karac_park_on_fd(fd, 0)` without a suffix fails LLVM verification because integer-literal coercion to narrow-int parameter types isn't implemented; the `0u8` suffix is the existing pattern from `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_print_u8_prints_unsigned`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries (565 unit + 782 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1231 typechecker + 1 new park-and-wake + … all green). Files: `runtime/Cargo.toml` (new `[features] test-helpers = []` block), `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~30 lines: feature-gated FFI fn), `tests/park_and_wake.rs` (new file, +~270 lines: harness + inline kara source). **What's next (not gated by Slice 7):** stdlib `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` / `WebSocket` skeleton types that wrap raw fds and call `karac_park_on_fd` from their methods — M1+ stdlib work that builds on the now-validated primitive; the `tests/park_and_wake.rs` subprocess + port-readback + connect-trigger + exit-with-timeout harness shape is reusable as the basis for the stdlib-era `tests/tcp_listener.rs`. **Follow-on slice surface:** the kara compiler's missing integer-literal-to-narrow-int coercion at call sites (currently requires explicit `0u8` suffix) is a separate small typechecker improvement — not gated by anything here, file under typechecker polish if/when prioritised.

[x] **Slice 8 — stdlib `TcpListener` (bind + accept) composing through `karac_park_on_fd` shipped 2026-05-25.** First M1 stdlib type to wire production-shape `TcpListener.bind(addr) -> TcpListener` + `listener.accept() -> i32` through the leaf parking primitive — proves the "compose at the leaf" architecture (the Slice 6 design call) is real and not just a stipulated convention. The E2E test (`tests/tcp_listener.rs`) exercises the same park-and-wake substrate that Slice 7 validated, but through the stdlib surface that user code will actually call; round-trip works first try at ~0.8 s wall clock (much faster than Slice 7's ~4.6 s because the runtime build is already warm from the prior slice). **Path-A design call (re-confirmed this slice):** picked the "compose at the leaf primitive" architecture over the alternative ("bundle park+accept into a single runtime FFI") — Path B would have been simpler for accept (~10 LOC codegen), but the M1/M2/M3 scaling target requires read/write methods to yield rather than thread-block, and any read/write implementation needs the reusable codegen helper anyway. Building the helper once for accept amortises across the future `TcpStream.read` / `.write` / `WebSocket.recv` / `.send` slices — the cost difference between Path A and Path B for *one* method is illusory once you know read/write will need Path A regardless. **Architectural finding (surfaced this slice):** baked stdlib items (`runtime/stdlib/*.kara`) reach the typechecker via `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` but NOT codegen (`src/codegen/types_lowering.rs:750` — "baked stdlib items aren't fed in"), so a stdlib method that needs real implementation has to be `#[compiler_builtin]` with hand-rolled codegen lowering. Stdlib methods with empty / stub bodies (the `iterator.kara` shape) work because nothing references their bodies; methods with real behaviour follow the `Server.serve_static` precedent of bake-the-signature, override-the-body. **Emitted shape.** `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` declares `struct TcpListener { fd: i32 }` + two `#[compiler_builtin]` methods (`bind` returns `TcpListener { fd: -1 }` stub, `accept` returns `-1` stub). `TcpListener` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` and `tcp.kara` added to `STDLIB_SOURCES`. Codegen lowering lives in new `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (~250 lines): `lower_tcp_listener_bind(addr)` extracts the kara `String`'s `{ptr, len}` from the addr arg and feeds them into a new runtime FFI `karac_runtime_tcp_bind(addr_ptr, addr_len) -> i32`, then packs the returned fd into a fresh `TcpListener { fd }` struct value via `insert_value` on undef. `lower_tcp_listener_accept(self)` extracts `self.fd` (works for both struct-value and ref-self-pointer receiver shapes), invokes the new `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, direction=0u8)` helper for the park step, then calls a second new runtime FFI `karac_runtime_tcp_accept(listener_fd) -> i32` for the raw `accept(2)`. Dispatch wired into `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (TcpListener.bind arm before the Server arms) and `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (TcpListener.accept arm at the top of `compile_method_call`, ahead of the slice 8g network-boundary intercept so the compiler-builtin path takes precedence over the generic state-machine dispatch). **Reusable codegen helper:** `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, direction)` allocates the karac_park_on_fd state struct, stores fd at field 1 + direction at field 2, drives the poll loop with `sched_yield` on Pending, frees the state on Ready. Specialised to the parking primitive's two-arg owned-param shape — no ref/slice handling, ~60 lines vs the slice 8d intercept's ~200 (which has to handle ref T / mut Slice / rvalue parameter shapes). Stays generic for future stdlib yielding methods (`TcpStream.read` / `.write` / `WebSocket.recv` / `.send`) — each new method's codegen call site is one line. **Underlying compiler change:** `synthesize_park_on_fd_layout` in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` was previously gated on the function being declared in user source (`find_function_ast(program, KARAC_PARK_ON_FD)?`); now hardcodes the canonical `{fd: i32, direction: u8}` layout so the symbols emit unconditionally in every kara binary. This is what lets `TcpListener.accept` codegen reach for `state_machine_state_constructors.get(KARAC_PARK_ON_FD)` without requiring user-source to also declare the primitive — stdlib lowering and power-user-source lowering both reference the same emitted symbols. Linker dead-strips the symbols in binaries that don't actually call into them, so the cost is zero for non-network programs. **Runtime FFI declarations** added to `Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_tcp_bind(*const u8, i64) -> i32` and `karac_runtime_tcp_accept(i32) -> i32`. Runtime side (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`): both implementations are ~30 lines each. `karac_runtime_tcp_bind` calls `std::net::TcpListener::bind`, prints `BOUND_PORT=<n>` to stdout when the requested addr ends in `:0` (smoke-test convention matching `Server.serve_static`), returns the raw fd via `IntoRawFd::into_raw_fd`. `karac_runtime_tcp_accept` constructs a borrowed `TcpListener` from the raw fd via `from_raw_fd`, calls `accept()` (raw syscall — no parking, no event-loop interaction — caller is expected to have already parked), returns the new connection fd, releases listener ownership back to the caller via `into_raw_fd` so the listener stays open for further accepts. **E2E test** (`tests/tcp_listener.rs`, +220 lines): mirrors `tests/park_and_wake.rs` harness shape (subprocess + read BOUND_PORT + connect-trigger + try_wait with timeout) but the kara source is now real stdlib — `let listener = TcpListener.bind("127.0.0.1:0"); let conn_fd = listener.accept(); println(conn_fd);` — no inline `extern` block, no power-user declarations. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 782 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1231 typechecker + 1 new park-and-wake + 1 new tcp_listener + … all green across all test binaries). **What's deferred to follow-on slices (not gated by Slice 8):** (1) `TcpStream` wrapper type around accepted fds + `read` / `write` methods (the `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd` helper transplants directly — each method is ~10 lines of codegen on top of two new runtime FFIs); (2) `Result[TcpListener, IoError]` / `Result[i32, IoError]` structured-error wrapping — v1 returns -1 on error matching the raw FFI shape, Result wrapping is a thin layer once a real consumer needs it; (3) close-on-drop for `TcpListener` (and future `TcpStream`) — gated on user-Drop dispatch in the typechecker / codegen, same deferral as `Pool[T]`; (4) `listener.local_addr()` / `.port()` getters — the `BOUND_PORT` stdout convention covers smoke-test readback; programmatic access waits for a real consumer to pin down the `getsockname(2)` FFI shape; (5) `WebSocket.recv` / `.send` — M1+ work; the codegen helper is ready, only the type + runtime FFI implementation is missing. **Slice 6's "every stdlib network type calls karac_park_on_fd from its body" design call is now load-bearing fact** rather than a stipulated convention — TcpListener.accept demonstrates the composition shape end-to-end. Files: `src/prelude.rs` (added `TcpListener` to `PRELUDE_TYPES`, added `tcp.kara` to `STDLIB_SOURCES`), `src/codegen.rs` (mod declaration + 2 FFI declarations in `Codegen::new`, ~30 lines), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (new file, +~260 lines: helper + 2 lowerings), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (+~10 lines: TcpListener.bind dispatch arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (+~15 lines: TcpListener.accept dispatch arm), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (`synthesize_park_on_fd_layout` made unconditional, ~25 lines), `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (new file, +~100 lines with rationale comments), `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~85 lines: 2 new FFI fns with safety docs), `tests/tcp_listener.rs` (new file, +~220 lines).

[x] **Slice 9 — stdlib `TcpStream` (read + write) composing through `karac_park_on_fd` shipped 2026-05-25.** Second M1 stdlib type to wire production-shape read/write methods through the leaf parking primitive — closes the bind → accept → write loop end-to-end through real stdlib surface. Round-trip works first try at ~0.8 s wall clock. **Architectural finding (carries forward from Slice 8):** the `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd` helper transplanted directly — the only new logic is per-method (extract self.fd, extract `buf.{ptr, len}` from Slice[u8], pick direction discriminant, call the raw-syscall FFI). Confirms the Slice 8 design call ("each future method's codegen call site is one line") was accurate: the helper invocation IS one line each, and the per-method lowering boilerplate stayed bounded at ~25 lines for read + ~25 lines for write, sharing the `lower_tcp_stream_io` private helper. **Emitted shape.** `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` gains `struct TcpStream { fd: i32 }` (same single-i32-field layout as TcpListener) + two new `#[compiler_builtin]` methods: `read(ref self, buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> i64 with sends(Network) receives(Network)` returning `-1` stub, `write(ref self, buf: Slice[u8]) -> i64 with sends(Network) receives(Network)` returning `-1` stub. `TcpListener.accept(ref self)` return type changed from `i32` to `TcpStream` and body changed from `-1` to `TcpStream { fd: -1 }` — proper API shape for v1 stdlib. `TcpStream` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` alongside `TcpListener`. Codegen lowerings in `src/codegen/tcp.rs`: new `lower_tcp_stream_read(self_val, buf_val)` and `lower_tcp_stream_write(self_val, buf_val)` both route through the shared private helper `lower_tcp_stream_io(self_val, buf_val, is_write)` that extracts self.fd, extracts Slice's `{ptr, i64 len}` (matches `slice_struct_type()` in `types_lowering.rs:193` — `{ptr, i64}`; `mut Slice[u8]` has the same physical layout, mutability is a type-system concept only), calls `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, direction)` with `direction = 0u8` for read or `1u8` for write, then calls the corresponding `karac_runtime_tcp_read` / `_tcp_write` FFI for the raw syscall. `lower_tcp_listener_accept` updated to wrap the returned i32 fd in a `TcpStream { fd }` struct value via `insert_value` on undef, mirroring `lower_tcp_listener_bind`'s wrapping shape. The fd-extraction logic factored out into `extract_fd_from_tcp_struct(self_val, name_hint)` — handles both struct-value and ref-self-pointer receiver shapes (reused by all three lowerings: accept, read, write). Dispatch wired into `src/codegen/method_call.rs` — same arm block as Slice 8's TcpListener.accept, adds `TcpStream.read` and `TcpStream.write` keys. **Runtime FFI declarations** added to `Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_tcp_read(i32, *mut u8, i64) -> i64` and `karac_runtime_tcp_write(i32, *const u8, i64) -> i64`. Runtime side (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`): both implementations are ~30 lines each, `#[cfg(unix)]`-gated. `karac_runtime_tcp_read` borrows a `std::net::TcpStream` from the raw fd via `from_raw_fd`, calls `read(buf)`, returns byte count (0 on clean EOF, -1 on error), releases ownership via `into_raw_fd`. `karac_runtime_tcp_write` is symmetric — borrows the stream, calls `write(buf)`, returns byte count (-1 on error), releases. Both FFIs are pure-syscall (no parking, no event-loop interaction) — caller (codegen lowering) is responsible for having parked via `karac_park_on_fd(stream_fd, direction)` BEFORE invoking. **E2E test** (`tests/tcp_stream.rs`, +260 lines): mirrors `tests/tcp_listener.rs` harness shape (subprocess + read BOUND_PORT + connect-trigger + try_wait with timeout) but exercises the write direction — kara source binds, accepts, calls `stream.write(msg.bytes())` (where `String.bytes() -> Slice[u8]` is the zero-copy view from design.md § Character type), the Rust harness connects, reads the written bytes from the connection, asserts the payload matches. Read direction wired in codegen + runtime FFI but NOT exercised in this E2E — the user-facing `read(ref self, buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> i64` signature requires the caller to construct a `mut Slice[u8]`, and the buffer-construction shape from user-source baked-stdlib types is best exercised by a real consumer (e.g. an echo-server kara program) that lands when one is needed. Unit-shape correctness of the read lowering is proved by the build + linkage passes; the codegen path is byte-identical to write's modulo the direction discriminant and FFI symbol name. **`tests/tcp_listener.rs` update**: `accept()` now returns `TcpStream` so the kara source changed from `let conn_fd = listener.accept(); println(conn_fd);` to `let _stream = listener.accept(); println(0);` — the round-trip semantics (binary exits 0 after the accept call returns) are unchanged, the test still pins the same park/wake substrate it always did. **`SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md`** updated: 47 → 51 `#[no_mangle]` exports — 2 from Slice 8 (`karac_runtime_tcp_bind` / `_tcp_accept`, which weren't filed at that slice's commit but belong with the runtime FFI surface audit) + 2 new from Slice 9 (`karac_runtime_tcp_read` / `_tcp_write`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 782 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1231 typechecker + 1 park-and-wake + 1 tcp_listener + 1 new tcp_stream + … all green across all test binaries). **What's deferred to follow-on slices (not gated by Slice 9):** (1) E2E exercise of the `read` direction once a real consumer surfaces — needs buffer-construction shape from user-source (e.g. `let mut buf: Array[u8, N] = [0u8; N]; let n = stream.read(buf);`) which is best validated through a real kara program rather than a synthetic harness; (2) `Result[i64, IoError]` structured-error wrapping for read/write — v1 returns -1 on error, Result wrapping is a thin layer once a real consumer needs structured errors (same deferral discipline as bind/accept); (3) `write_all` looping wrapper that absorbs partial writes — v1 issues a single `write(2)` and lets the caller loop if needed; (4) close-on-drop for `TcpStream` (and `TcpListener`) — gated on user-Drop dispatch in the typechecker / codegen, same deferral as `Pool[T]`; (5) `WebSocket.recv` / `.send` — M1+ work; the codegen helper is ready, only the type + runtime FFI implementation is missing. **Slice 6's design call ("compose at the leaf primitive") is now demonstrated across both directions** — TcpListener.accept (read-readiness) and TcpStream.write (write-readiness) both compose through the same `karac_park_on_fd` leaf via the same `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd` helper. The architecture scales as predicted; further stdlib yielding methods slot in with codegen call sites that are literally one line. Files: `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (added `struct TcpStream`, added `impl TcpStream` block with read+write, changed `accept`'s return type from `i32` to `TcpStream`), `src/prelude.rs` (added `TcpStream` to `PRELUDE_TYPES`), `src/codegen.rs` (2 new FFI declarations in `Codegen::new`, ~36 lines), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (refactored `lower_tcp_listener_accept` to wrap fd in TcpStream + 3 new methods `lower_tcp_stream_read` / `_write` / shared `lower_tcp_stream_io` + helper `extract_fd_from_tcp_struct`, +~140 lines net), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (added `TcpStream.read` / `.write` dispatch arms alongside `TcpListener.accept`, +~10 lines), `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~100 lines: 2 new FFI fns with safety docs), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (4 new table rows + summary count bump 47 → 51), `tests/tcp_listener.rs` (kara source updated for new accept return type, +5 / -5 lines), `tests/tcp_stream.rs` (new file, +~260 lines).

[x] **Slice 9a — TcpStream `read` direction E2E shipped 2026-05-25.** Slice 9 wired `TcpStream.read(ref self, buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> i64` end-to-end in codegen + runtime FFI but only exercised the write direction in `tests/tcp_stream.rs`. This slice closes the loop: a kara program binds, accepts, constructs `let mut buf: Array[u8, 64] = [0u8; 64]`, calls `stream.read(mut buf)`, prints the returned byte count; harness connects, writes `b"ping\n"`, asserts the binary exits success with the count line being a positive integer. Round-trip works at ~1.1 s wall clock. **Bug surfaced + fixed mid-slice.** First run paniced at `src/codegen/tcp.rs:321` — `lower_tcp_stream_io` called `buf_val.into_struct_value()` but received `ArrayValue { llvm_type: "[64 x i8]" }` instead of the expected `{ptr, i64}` slice header. Root cause: the TcpStream method-call dispatch in `src/codegen/method_call.rs` compiled the buf argument via `compile_expr` directly, skipping the call-site `Array[T, N]` → `mut Slice[T]` coercion that other slice-taking call paths use. Fix: route through the existing `coerce_to_slice(arg, elem_ty=u8)` helper (defined `src/codegen/expr_ops.rs:1750`) with fallback to `compile_expr` if the arg isn't a recognised sequence source — same shape as the free-function call path at `src/codegen/mono.rs:293` and the impl-call path at `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:381`. Both TcpStream.read and TcpStream.write get the coercion now (write was always passing a `String.bytes()` which already produces a slice struct, so it didn't surface the bug — but the coercion guards against future consumers passing arrays/vecs to write). **Architectural finding.** The compiler-builtin dispatch path I introduced at Slice 9 was a partial reproduction of the standard call-lowering machinery — I extracted self + args via raw `compile_expr` instead of going through the existing coercion helpers. The fix consolidates against the same `coerce_to_slice` helper the rest of the codegen uses, so all four slice-taking call paths (free-fn `compile_call`, impl-method `mono`, generic method dispatch `call_dispatch`, compiler-builtin `method_call::compile_method_call`) now share the same Array/Vec → Slice coercion semantics. Future compiler-builtin methods that take `Slice[T]` / `mut Slice[T]` arguments must route through `coerce_to_slice` — codegen-level lint candidate. **Emitted shape.** Test fn `test_tcp_stream_read_round_trip` in `tests/tcp_stream.rs` reuses `compile_and_link` + `runtime_path` + the test lock from the existing write test, adds a new helper `await_bound_port_collect_lines` that returns the port AND a `JoinHandle<Vec<String>>` exposing every post-BOUND_PORT line (the original helper drops them on the floor, but slice 9a needs them to assert on the `println(n)` count line). Test asserts: exit-success, count line parses as a positive `i64`. The byte-count assertion is the tightest portable invariant — asserting on exact byte values would race against `read(2)`'s partial-read semantics, and slice 9 ships single-syscall reads (no `read_exact` looping wrapper — that's Slice 9c). Positive count proves: (1) parking through `karac_park_on_fd` returned; (2) `karac_runtime_tcp_read` executed the syscall on the borrowed fd; (3) the FFI's i64 return flowed through the codegen lowering into the kara `let n` binding. **Slice 6's design call is now demonstrated across all three stdlib network methods** — TcpListener.accept (read-readiness), TcpStream.write (write-readiness), TcpStream.read (read-readiness with mut Slice arg). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries (565 unit + 785 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1234 typechecker + 2 tcp_stream + 1 tcp_listener + 1 park_and_wake + …). Files: `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (TcpStream.read + TcpStream.write dispatch arms now route buf through `coerce_to_slice`, +6 / -2 lines), `tests/tcp_stream.rs` (file header expanded to mention slice 9a, new `await_bound_port_collect_lines` helper, new `test_tcp_stream_read_round_trip` test, +~190 lines).
