[x] **Slice 9b — `Result[i64, TcpError]` structured-error wrapping for TcpStream read/write shipped 2026-05-25.** Replaces the slice-9 raw `-> i64` (with `-1` sentinel for errors) with `-> Result[i64, TcpError]` so consumers get structured success vs failure and can distinguish retry-now (EINTR) from fatal. **Design call (resolved this slice — diverges from the original filing).** The original tracker entry committed to `Result[i64, IoError]` with five variants (`WouldBlock`, `ConnectionReset`, `BrokenPipe`, `Interrupted`, `Other(i32)`); I scoped down to a dedicated `enum TcpError { Interrupted, Other(i32) }` for two reasons: (1) `IoError`'s existing variant set is filesystem/UTF-8 shaped (`NotFound`, `PermissionDenied`, `InvalidUtf8`) — folding TCP-specific variants in would dilute its semantics. (2) Per the v1-ship-reality discipline, ship the minimum useful variant set — `Interrupted` for EINTR retry detection (needed for slice 9c `write_all`) and `Other(i32)` carrying errno for caller inspection. Richer variants (`WouldBlock`/`ConnectionReset`/`BrokenPipe`) are additive non-breaking changes when a real consumer surfaces the need; the `Other` variant carries the raw errno so callers can match on it inline today. The original "blocked by 9d" cross-reference was wrong — `IoError` and `TcpError` are both just types, neither needs user-Drop dispatch infrastructure. **Emitted shape.** Three surface changes: (1) `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` adds `enum TcpError { Interrupted, Other(i32) }` and flips both method signatures to `Result[i64, TcpError]`; stub bodies return `Result.Err(TcpError.Other(-1))` (never executed — codegen replaces). (2) `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` changes `karac_runtime_tcp_read` / `_tcp_write` to return `-errno` on syscall failure (was: generic `-1`) — uses `std::io::Error::raw_os_error()` to extract the OS errno from the failed `read`/`write` call, negates it. Zero ABI surface change (still `-> i64`); just tighter semantics on the negative-return space. (3) `src/codegen/tcp.rs` adds `wrap_tcp_io_result(n, is_write)` helper called from `lower_tcp_stream_io` after the FFI call. The helper branches on `n >= 0` (success) vs `n < 0` (error). Ok arm: builds `Result.Ok(n)` aggregate (tag at field 0, n at field 1). Err arm: `errno = 0 - n`, classifies via `select` (no extra basic blocks) on `errno == 4` (POSIX EINTR — standardised across Linux/macOS/BSD/Solaris), packs `TcpError.{Interrupted | Other(errno)}` into Result's payload fields 1-2 (TcpError occupies 2 i64 words: tag + payload). Phi-merges Ok and Err arms at the continuation block, returns the `Result[i64, TcpError]` value. **TcpError layout seeding.** Per the `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` convention (mirroring Json's situation in the same file — baked stdlib enums reach the typechecker via `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` but NOT codegen's `declare_enums` which only walks user `program.items`), `TcpError` gets an explicit layout seed in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` alongside `Result`'s seed. Without this the codegen-side variant construction would fall through to the `i64 0` placeholder and break user-side `match Err(TcpError.Other(errno)) => ...` extraction. **Test surface.** `tests/tcp_stream.rs::test_tcp_stream_read_round_trip` updated: kara source now `match stream.read(mut buf) { Ok(n) => println(n), Err(_) => println(-1) }` — exercises the full Ok arm extraction path through `reconstruct_payload_value`. Write test's body still `let _r = stream.write(...)` works unchanged (the binding is unused; the type just changed from `i64` to `Result[i64, TcpError]`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 785 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1234 typechecker + 2 tcp_stream + 1 tcp_listener + 1 park_and_wake + …). Files: `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (added `enum TcpError`, flipped read/write signatures to `-> Result[i64, TcpError]`, +~30 lines), `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (tcp_read + tcp_write return `-errno` on error instead of generic `-1`, +~10 lines / -2 lines), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (`seed_builtin_enum_layouts` adds `TcpError` layout next to `Result`, +~50 lines), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (new `wrap_tcp_io_result` helper, `lower_tcp_stream_io` calls it after FFI, file-header doc updated, +~155 lines / -5 lines), `tests/tcp_stream.rs` (read test source uses `match` on Result, doc updated, +~7 lines / -3 lines).
  12. [x] **Slice 9c — `TcpStream.write_all` looping wrapper for partial writes shipped 2026-05-25.** v1 `write` issues a single `write(2)` syscall and returns the count of bytes actually pushed — callers must loop themselves on partial writes or retry on EINTR. `write_all(ref self, buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]` is the standard wrapper: loops until `buf.len()` bytes are written, advances `chunk_ptr = buf.ptr + written` each iteration, retries on `TcpError.Interrupted` (no progress made; same buffer offset), exits Ok when `written == buf.len()` or Err on the first non-EINTR failure. **Design call resolved this slice.** The original tracker entry committed to "pure kara source (no new codegen / FFI)" — that estimate was wrong because karac's codegen only compiles user `program.items`, NOT stdlib non-`#[compiler_builtin]` method bodies (same gap that forces `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` for stdlib enums). To ship `write_all` as pure-kara stdlib source, the codegen-compiles-stdlib gap would need to close first — that's a multi-day architectural slice. The pragmatic v1 ship: implement `write_all` as a fourth `#[compiler_builtin]` on TcpStream, with the loop expressed in LLVM IR via `lower_tcp_stream_write_all`. The IR is ~200 lines of straightforward state-machine emission (alloca written, loop_head/body/advance/err_check/err_exit/ok_exit blocks, phi-merge at cont) and reuses three existing helpers (`extract_fd_from_tcp_struct`, `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd`, the `Result[i64, TcpError]` build pattern from slice 9b's `wrap_tcp_io_result`). When the codegen-compiles-stdlib gap eventually closes, this lowering can be replaced with the pure-kara while-loop body that's already sketched in the stdlib stub's comment block. **Emitted shape.** `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` adds a fourth method `fn write_all(ref self, buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]` to `impl TcpStream` (stub body returns `Result.Err(TcpError.Other(-1))` — never executes). `src/codegen/method_call.rs` adds a dispatch arm (with `coerce_to_slice` for Array/Vec callers) calling `self.lower_tcp_stream_write_all(...)`. `src/codegen/tcp.rs` adds `lower_tcp_stream_write_all` — the IR builds: (1) `written: i64` alloca initialised to 0; (2) `loop_head` compares `written < buf.len`, exits to `ok_exit` on done; (3) `loop_body` computes `remaining = buf.len - written`, `chunk_ptr = buf.ptr + written` via `in_bounds_gep i8`, parks on write-readiness via `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, 1)`, calls `karac_runtime_tcp_write(fd, chunk_ptr, remaining)`, branches on `n >= 0`; (4) `advance` adds `n` to `written` and loops back; (5) `err_check` computes `errno = -n`, branches: EINTR → loop_head (retry with same `written`), other → `err_exit`; (6) `err_exit` builds `Result.Err(TcpError.Other(errno))` via the slice 9b enum-layout pattern + phi over errno; (7) `ok_exit` builds `Result.Ok(written_final)`; (8) `cont` phi-merges Ok/Err arms. **Test surface.** `tests/tcp_stream.rs::test_tcp_stream_write_all_round_trip` (+~180 lines): 2 KiB payload built in kara source as a repeated 32-byte ASCII pattern (`Aa1Zz9Bb2Yy8Cc3Xx7Dd4Ww6Ee5Vv0!` x 64); harness reads back every byte and asserts (a) exit-success, (b) total byte count equals expected, (c) byte-for-byte content match (catches off-by-one in `chunk_ptr = buf.ptr + written`). Partial-write path (loop count above 1) NOT deterministically reproducible without a blocking peer harness — 2 KiB fits well within the OS socket send buffer so a single syscall pushes the whole payload; the partial-write code path is exercised by reading `lower_tcp_stream_write_all`'s IR and trusting the structural invariants (same approach the codegen E2Es take for branch coverage on tagged loops). **Architectural carryout for the codegen-compiles-stdlib gap.** This slice is the second post-slice-9 entry to hit the gap (slice 9b had to seed `TcpError`'s enum layout for the same reason). When a third or fourth stdlib type wants pure-kara methods, the gap should get its own tracker entry under Phase 7 codegen — the per-method IR-shim pattern doesn't scale to large stdlib surfaces (sorting, parsing, formatting, etc.). For now: file the observation, move on. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 785 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1234 typechecker + 3 tcp_stream + 1 tcp_listener + 1 park_and_wake + …). Files: `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (added `fn write_all` to `impl TcpStream`, +~20 lines), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (added `TcpStream.write_all` dispatch arm with `coerce_to_slice`, +~10 lines), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (added `lower_tcp_stream_write_all` ~200 lines), `tests/tcp_stream.rs` (added `test_tcp_stream_write_all_round_trip`, +~180 lines).
  13. [x] **Slice 9d — close-on-drop for `TcpStream` and `TcpListener` shipped 2026-05-25.** Closes the fd-leak hole the prior entry described. Both stdlib types now register `impl Drop` in `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (compiler-builtin stub bodies), and the codegen hand-rolls `@TcpListener.drop` / `@TcpStream.drop` LLVM bodies that call the new `karac_runtime_tcp_close(self.fd)` runtime FFI — `let l = TcpListener.bind(...)` followed by scope exit now closes the kernel fd. Implementation took path (b) from the prior entry's analysis (hand-rolled LLVM bodies); path (a) — closing the stdlib-bodies-not-compiled gap — remains a separate multi-day slice tracked in phase-7-codegen.md. **Architecture.** The user-Drop dispatch chain (Prereq.1-5) carries TcpListener / TcpStream through transparently once the LLVM symbol exists: typechecker's `drop_method_keys` picks up the stdlib `impl Drop` blocks (Prereq.1 walks `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` alongside user programs); Prereq.2's `emit_user_drop_wrapper` finds `@TcpListener.drop` via `module.get_function` (now exists, hand-rolled); Prereq.3 emits `CleanupAction::UserDrop` at let-binding sites of these types (the let-binding tracking was extended to allow stdlib types — the `struct_types.contains_key` gate now is a fallback for the no-user-Drop case, while `drop_method_keys.contains_key` takes precedence). **Emitted shape.** New helper `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies(program)` in `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` iterates `["TcpListener", "TcpStream"]`, checks each against `program.drop_method_keys`, and emits a 4-instruction body per type: GEP field 0, load `i32`, `call i32 @karac_runtime_tcp_close(i32)`, `ret void`. The body uses an inline `context.struct_type(&[i32_type])` rather than reading `struct_types["TcpListener"]` (stdlib structs aren't in `struct_types` — that map only walks `program.items`); this matches the existing convention in `src/codegen/tcp.rs::lower_tcp_listener_bind`. Runs in `compile_program` between `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` and `emit_user_drop_wrappers` — the wrapper synth then finds the `<Type>.drop` symbol via `get_function` and emits `@karac_drop_<Type>` calling into it. **`karac_runtime_tcp_close(fd: i32) -> i32` FFI** in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` reconstructs a `std::net::TcpStream` from the raw fd via `from_raw_fd` (without `into_raw_fd` — letting the destructor run is the close). `-1` fd is a no-op (matches the per-method "no-fd" sentinel convention used by `bind` / `accept`). `#[cfg(unix)]` gate matches the bind / accept / read / write FFIs; Windows IOCP path lands with slice 10. **3 new IR-grep tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: (1) `@TcpListener.drop`'s emitted body calls `@karac_runtime_tcp_close`; (2) same for `@TcpStream.drop`; (3) `main` of a program creating `TcpListener.bind(...)` contains `call void @karac_drop_TcpListener(...)` at scope exit — pins the full chain from typechecker registration through wrapper synthesis to scope-exit drain. One typechecker test (`drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl`) updated to reflect that stdlib entries are always present in `drop_method_keys`; the assertion is now "no user-defined entries" rather than "empty map". All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 799 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1248 typechecker + 641 interpreter + all binaries green; codegen E2E +3 from 796 → 799, typechecker +1 from 1247 → 1248). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~45 lines: `karac_runtime_tcp_close` FFI), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (1 new table row + summary count bump), `runtime/stdlib/tcp.kara` (+~12 lines: two `impl Drop` blocks; -15 lines: replaced stale "Drop semantics deferred" header comment with the shipped-summary block), `src/codegen.rs` (+13 lines: `karac_runtime_tcp_close` FFI declaration in `Codegen::new` + invocation of `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` in `compile_program`), `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` (+~100 lines: `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` driver + `emit_tcp_drop_body_for` synthesiser), `src/codegen/stmts.rs` (+~10 lines / -2 lines: let-binding tracking now allows stdlib types with user Drop to skip the `struct_types` gate), `tests/codegen.rs` (+~80 lines: 3 new IR-grep tests), `tests/typechecker.rs` (+~10 lines: `drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl` adjusted for stdlib entries). **What still leaks** even with this slice: see the broader move-suppression tracker entry in phase-7-codegen.md (filed by Prereq.5); if a `TcpListener` is moved out of a function via return-by-value, both source and destination scope-exit fire close on the same fd. The second close returns EBADF; in worst case under high concurrency this could land on another process's fd at the same number. Tracking that fix to its own slice. Cross-link to sibling consumer: `Pool[T]` (`runtime/stdlib/pool.kara:25-33`) — same close-on-drop pattern unblocks `PooledConnection[T]`'s auto-return; needs the same hand-rolled `@Pool.drop` / `@PooledConnection.drop` shim or stdlib-bodies-gap closure.

[x] **Slice 9e — `WebSocket.recv` / `.send` stdlib type shipped 2026-05-25 / 2026-05-26.** All four sub-slices landed: 9e.1 framing + 9e.2 HTTP upgrade + 9e.3 control frames + binary (2026-05-25), 9e.4 fragmentation reassembly + client-side masking (2026-05-26). M1 100K-idle-connections demo's WebSocket dependency is now closed; what remains for the demo is the demo program itself (kata-level work, not phase-6).

  **Sub-slice 9e.1 — RFC 6455 framing protocol shipped 2026-05-25.** Lands the wire-format encode/decode for TEXT frames (FIN=1, opcode=0x1, MASK=0 server→client, MASK=1 client→server), server-side convention. Surface: `struct WebSocket { fd: i32 }` (single-i32-field layout matching `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` so it composes with the slice-9d Drop hand-roll), plus three `#[compiler_builtin]` methods — `from_fd(fd: i32) -> WebSocket` (v1 testing entry point; production path lands in 9e.2), `send_text(ref self, msg: Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]`, `recv_text(ref self, buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]`. `impl Drop for WebSocket` wires through the existing user-Drop chain (Prereq.1-5 from phase-7-codegen.md); the `@WebSocket.drop` LLVM body is hand-rolled by `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` extended to include `"WebSocket"` in its type list (mirrors the same path as `@TcpListener.drop` / `@TcpStream.drop`). **Runtime FFIs.** `karac_runtime_ws_send_text(fd, msg_ptr, msg_len) -> i64` encodes the frame header per RFC 6455 §5.2 (7-bit inline length for < 126, 7+16-bit extended for < 65536, 7+64-bit extended otherwise), appends the unmasked payload, writes via `write_all`. Returns `msg_len` on success, `-1` on write error. `karac_runtime_ws_recv_text(fd, out_ptr, out_max_len) -> i64` reads the 2-byte header, validates FIN=1 + RSV=000 + opcode=0x1 + MASK=1, decodes the extended length, reads the 4-byte mask key, reads the payload, unmasks in place via the `payload[i] ^= mask_key[i % 4]` loop. Returns payload byte count on success, `0` on graceful EOF before complete frame, `-1` on any protocol/IO error. v1 limitations rejected as `-1`: FIN=0 fragmented frames, opcode-0 continuation, control frames (close/ping/pong), binary frames, payloads exceeding `out_max_len`. **Codegen lowerings** in `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (alongside the existing TCP lowerings — both types share the single-i32-field layout and the same compose-at-leaf pattern): `lower_websocket_from_fd` packs the i32 fd into a struct via `insert_value`; `lower_websocket_send_text` / `_recv_text` extract `self.fd` + `slice.{ptr, len}`, park via `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, direction)`, call the FFI, wrap the `i64` return through `wrap_tcp_io_result` (which already produces the right `Result[i64, TcpError]` shape — labels show `tcp.write.*` / `tcp.read.*` BB names, mildly imprecise but harmless; a dedicated `wrap_ws_io_result` lands when slice 9e.3 introduces `WsError`). **Dispatch arms** in `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (for `WebSocket.from_fd`) and `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (for `.send_text` / `.recv_text`). **6 RFC 6455 wire-format tests** in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs::tests`: short text-frame send (header + payload), 200-byte payload using extended 2-byte length encoding, masked client-frame recv with unmask validation, unmasked client-frame rejection (RFC 6455 §5.1 protocol violation), binary-opcode rejection (slice 9e.1 text-only scope), full bidirectional round-trip. **4 codegen IR-grep tests** in `tests/ws_framing.rs`: `@karac_drop_WebSocket` wrapper emitted with hand-rolled `@WebSocket.drop` body calling `karac_runtime_tcp_close`; `ws.send_text` dispatches to `karac_runtime_ws_send_text` after parking; `ws.recv_text` dispatches to `karac_runtime_ws_recv_text` after parking; both FFI declarations land in the LLVM module unconditionally. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 803 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1248 typechecker + 4 ws_framing IR-grep + 6 new runtime ws-framing tests in karac-runtime + … all green; codegen E2E +0 because the IR-grep tests landed in a new test file `tests/ws_framing.rs` outside the count). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~220 lines: `ws_read_exact_or_eof` helper + two FFIs + 6 tests), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (2 new rows + summary count bump 52 → 54), `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara` (new file, +~180 lines), `src/prelude.rs` (`WebSocket` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`, `ws.kara` added to `STDLIB_SOURCES`), `src/codegen.rs` (+~40 lines: `karac_runtime_ws_send_text` / `_recv_text` FFI declarations in `Codegen::new`), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (+~120 lines: `lower_websocket_from_fd` / `_send_text` / `_recv_text` / `lower_websocket_io`), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (+12 lines: `WebSocket.from_fd` dispatch arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (+~25 lines: `WebSocket.send_text` / `_recv_text` dispatch arms with `coerce_to_slice`), `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` (+~10 lines: `"WebSocket"` added to `emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies`'s type list), `tests/ws_framing.rs` (new file, +~185 lines), `tests/typechecker.rs` (+~5 lines: `drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl` updated to filter the WebSocket stdlib entry alongside TcpListener/TcpStream).

  **Kara-source E2E gap observed during 9e.1 (filed as orthogonal codegen follow-on).** A natural test for the framing round-trip would be: kara binary binds, accepts, calls `WebSocket.from_fd(stream.fd)` to wrap the connection, then exercises `send_text` / `recv_text`. That test cannot land at slice 9e.1 because `stream.fd` field access on a stdlib struct type returns const 0 at codegen — the codegen's `struct_types` map is populated only for user `program.items`, not stdlib bodies, so the field-access lowering falls back to a zero default. This is a pre-existing gap affecting any `stdlib_value.field` access (not WebSocket-specific). Slice 9e.2's `accept_websocket(listener) -> WebSocket` builder will bypass this by extracting the fd inside the codegen lowering (same path as `lower_tcp_listener_accept`'s `extract_fd_from_tcp_struct`), so kara-source E2E coverage for WebSocket lands with 9e.2. Filed as a tracker entry in phase-7-codegen.md alongside the stdlib-struct-return-ABI gap (same root cause: `struct_types` doesn't include stdlib types). v1 9e.1 correctness is gated on (1) the 6 RFC 6455 wire-format tests in the runtime crate, and (2) the 4 codegen IR-grep tests that pin the dispatch shape; both demonstrate the same FFI ABI the eventual kara-source E2E will exercise.

  **Sub-slice 9e.2 — HTTP-upgrade handshake shipped 2026-05-25.** Server-side WebSocket handshake per RFC 6455 §4.2. `WebSocket.accept(listener: TcpListener) -> WebSocket` parks on listener-readability, accepts a TCP connection, reads the HTTP/1.1 request, computes `Sec-WebSocket-Accept` from the request's `Sec-WebSocket-Key`, writes the 101 Switching Protocols response, returns a `WebSocket` wrapping the upgraded connection (or `WebSocket { fd: -1 }` on any failure — matches the `TcpListener.bind` / `.accept` per-method sentinel convention). **Runtime FFI** `karac_runtime_ws_accept(listener_fd: i32) -> i32` in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` houses the blocking accept + HTTP-upgrade sequence. **SHA-1 + Base64 hand-rolled** in the same file (~80 lines SHA-1 per RFC 3174, ~30 lines Base64 per RFC 4648) — bounded one-call use, well-known algorithms, avoids adding dependency crates. RFC 3174 test vectors (`abc`, empty input) + RFC 4648 §10 Base64 vectors + RFC 6455 §1.3 worked example (`dGhlIHNhbXBsZSBub25jZQ==` → `s3pPLMBiTxaQ9kYGzzhZRbK+xOo=`) pinned in unit tests. **HTTP request parsing** scoped to the handshake's specific shape: read until `\r\n\r\n` (8 KiB cap), find the `Sec-WebSocket-Key` header (case-insensitive per RFC 7230), skip post-colon whitespace, extract the value. Missing key → best-effort 400 Bad Request response + return -1. **Codegen lowering** `lower_websocket_accept` in `src/codegen/tcp.rs` mirrors `lower_tcp_listener_accept`: extract listener.fd via `extract_fd_from_tcp_struct`, park via `emit_state_machine_invocation_for_park_on_fd(fd, direction=0)`, call the FFI, pack returned i32 into a fresh `WebSocket { fd }` struct via `insert_value`. Assoc-call dispatch in `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs`. **By-value listener argument**: convenient for the single-listener M1 demo shape; the listener's close-on-drop fires at the caller's scope exit independently of this call (the FFI uses `from_raw_fd` + `into_raw_fd` to borrow without taking ownership of the listener fd). **3 new tests in runtime** crate (SHA-1 RFC vectors, Base64 RFC vectors, RFC 6455 worked Accept value) + 2 handshake integration tests (full round-trip with hand-crafted browser-shape HTTP/1.1 request validating 101 response + Sec-WebSocket-Accept header, missing-key 400 response) + 2 helper-level tests (case-insensitive Sec-WebSocket-Key extraction, missing-header None return). **2 new codegen IR-grep tests** in `tests/ws_framing.rs` (accept parks before the FFI; ws_accept FFI declaration emitted unconditionally). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 803 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1248 typechecker + 6 ws_framing + 9 runtime ws tests including 3 new handshake — all green). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (+~280 lines: SHA-1 + Base64 + ws_read_http_request + extract_sec_websocket_key + karac_runtime_ws_accept FFI + 5 new tests), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (1 new row + count bump 54 → 55), `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara` (+~35 lines: `WebSocket.accept` method), `src/codegen.rs` (+~18 lines: ws_accept FFI declaration), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (+~45 lines: `lower_websocket_accept`), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (+~9 lines: dispatch arm), `tests/ws_framing.rs` (+~45 lines: 2 new tests). **v1 limitations (filed for 9e.3 or production hardening).** No request validation beyond `Sec-WebSocket-Key` presence (real production would also check `Upgrade: websocket`, `Connection: Upgrade`, `Sec-WebSocket-Version: 13`, `Host:`); no subprotocol/extension negotiation (101 response omits `Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` / `Sec-WebSocket-Extensions`); blocking reads with no handshake timeout (a malicious client that connects but never sends keeps the worker thread tied up until kernel timeout, typically minutes); 8 KiB request size cap. **Unblocks the kara-source E2E test for slice 9e.1's framing round-trip** — `WebSocket.accept(listener)` doesn't pass through `stream.fd` field access (the pre-existing codegen gap that blocked 9e.1's E2E coverage); a follow-on test can now drive the full bind → accept-upgrade → send/recv → drop chain from kara source. Filed as a kata follow-on rather than a 9e.2-blocking test.

  **Sub-slice 9e.3 — control frames + binary shipped 2026-05-25.** Closes the protocol-compliance and binary-payload gaps from slice 9e.1. **Control frames (RFC 6455 §5.5)** are now handled transparently by both `recv_text` and `recv_binary`: ping (0x9) → auto-reply with pong of same payload, continue reading; pong (0xA) → discard, continue; close (0x8) → reply with empty close frame (the §5.5.1 close handshake), return 0 to the caller (matches the EOF return convention so `n == 0` is the universal "connection ended cleanly" signal). The kara caller never sees control frames; they're absorbed inside the FFI's read loop. Control-frame validation: FIN=1 required, payload ≤ 125 bytes per §5.5; violations produce -1. Reserved control opcodes (0xB..0xF) also produce -1. **Binary frames** ship as full-symmetric counterparts to text: `WebSocket.send_binary(ref self, msg: Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]` and `WebSocket.recv_binary(ref self, buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[i64, TcpError]`. Wire shape mirrors text exactly except for the opcode bit (0x2 vs 0x1) the runtime helper encodes/expects. **Internal refactor.** Send paths factor through a new private `ws_write_unmasked_frame(stream, opcode, payload)` helper that's reused by `send_text`, `send_binary`, the auto-pong reply, and the close-response reply — single source of truth for the unmasked-frame encoder. Recv paths factor through `ws_recv_data_frame(fd, out_ptr, out_max_len, accept_opcode)` whose `accept_opcode` parameter dispatches to text (0x1) or binary (0x2); the control-frame loop and shared header decoding live here. **8 new runtime tests + 3 new codegen IR-grep tests.** Runtime: ping auto-response + pong validation, pong frame discarded, close returns 0 + reply observed on wire, oversize control frame rejected, send_binary opcode-2 encoding, recv_binary masked-frame decoding, recv_binary rejects text frames (mirror of slice-9e.1's text-rejects-binary), fragmented data frame (FIN=0) rejected as -1 (refiled gap below). Codegen: send_binary / recv_binary park-then-FFI dispatch shape, both binary FFI declarations land unconditionally. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 803 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1248 typechecker + 9 ws_framing IR-grep + 17 runtime ws tests — all green). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (refactor + control-frame handling + binary FFIs + 8 tests, +~430 lines / -~85 lines net), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (2 new rows + count bump 55 → 57), `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara` (+~25 lines: `send_binary` / `recv_binary` methods on `impl WebSocket`), `src/codegen.rs` (+~28 lines: 2 new FFI declarations), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (+~25 lines: 2 new lowerings + refactor of `lower_websocket_io` to take FFI name parameter), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (+~20 lines: dispatch arms for the new methods), `tests/ws_framing.rs` (+~65 lines: 3 new IR-grep tests).

  **Carryover gap → sub-slice 9e.4 (filed below).** Fragmentation reassembly + client-side masking. Slice 9e.3's recv loop rejects FIN=0 data frames and opcode-0 continuation frames as -1 — fragmentation support requires buffering partial payloads across multiple frames, which has its own design questions (caller-buffer overrun, runtime-side scratch allocation, max-message size policy). Client-side masking on `send_*` requires either a per-WebSocket "is_client" flag (set at construction time) or dedicated `send_text_masked` / `send_binary_masked` companions; the choice has user-API ergonomics implications worth thinking through. Both deferred to 9e.4 — neither blocks the M1 100K-idle-connections demo since the demo uses small unfragmented server→client text frames.

  **Sub-slice 9e.4 — fragmentation reassembly + client-side masking shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the last two RFC 6455 protocol features. **Fragmentation (RFC 6455 §5.4).** `ws_recv_data_frame` now reassembles multi-frame messages: a FIN=0 + opcode=data frame starts a fragmented message; subsequent FIN=0 + opcode=0x0 (continuation) frames extend it; a FIN=1 + opcode=0x0 final continuation closes it. Each fragment's unmasked payload is appended to the caller's buffer at the running `accumulated` offset; the loop returns the total byte count when FIN=1 closes the message. Total reassembled length is bounded by `out_max_len` — exceeding it returns -1. Control frames (ping/pong/close) interleaved between data fragments per §5.4 are handled transparently and don't disrupt reassembly state. Protocol violations rejected as -1: continuation frames outside a fragment, non-continuation data frames mid-fragment. Same behaviour applies symmetrically to `recv_text` (accept_opcode=0x1) and `recv_binary` (accept_opcode=0x2). **Client-side masking (RFC 6455 §5.1).** New dedicated methods `WebSocket.send_text_masked` and `WebSocket.send_binary_masked` for kara binaries acting as WebSocket clients. Default `send_text` / `send_binary` remain server-side (MASK=0); the `_masked` variants build MASK=1 frames with a 4-byte mask key generated per-call via `/dev/urandom` (with a time-derived LCG fallback when `/dev/urandom` is unavailable — defensive, keeps the connection alive in chroot / container environments). Mask key generation pinned by a variance test. Runtime FFIs `karac_runtime_ws_send_text_masked` / `_send_binary_masked` route through a shared `ws_write_masked_frame` helper that mirrors the unmasked encoder's structure + adds the mask-key write + masked-payload write. **8 new runtime tests + 3 new codegen IR-grep tests.** Runtime: orphan continuation rejected; 3-fragment text reassembly; ping interleaved between fragments + pong response observed; oversize fragmented message returns -1; mid-fragment non-continuation rejected; binary fragmentation symmetric; masked text wire format (header + mask key + masked payload, round-trip-unmaskable); masked binary opcode 0x2; mask-key generator produces non-constant output across calls. Codegen: send_text_masked + send_binary_masked dispatch shape; both masked FFI declarations emitted unconditionally. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (565 unit + 803 codegen E2E + 264 memory_sanitizer + 1248 typechecker + 12 ws_framing IR-grep + 25 runtime ws tests — all green). Files: `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (refactor of `ws_recv_data_frame` to handle reassembly + new `ws_generate_mask_key` + `ws_write_masked_frame` + `ws_send_masked_data_frame` + 2 FFIs + 8 tests, +~330 lines / -~40 lines net), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (2 new rows + count bump 57 → 59), `runtime/stdlib/ws.kara` (+~30 lines: `send_text_masked` / `send_binary_masked` methods), `src/codegen.rs` (+~25 lines: 2 new FFI declarations), `src/codegen/tcp.rs` (+~25 lines: 2 new lowerings reusing the shared `lower_websocket_io`), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (+~20 lines: 2 new dispatch arms), `tests/ws_framing.rs` (+~55 lines: 3 new IR-grep tests).

  **What remains gated on M1 demo work** (not on phase-6 slices): the demo program itself (a kara binary that binds, upgrades, and runs the keepalive + echo loop at 100K concurrent connections). All RFC 6455 features that demo needs now ship in stdlib; the kata is purely user-code at this point.

  M1 milestone gate per `Concurrency target staging` (the 100K idle connections demo) — all four 9e sub-slices now landed.
  15. [ ] **Slice 10 — Windows IOCP integration.** Current event loop is `#[cfg(unix)]`-only on the fd-registration FFI (`karac_runtime_event_loop_register_fd` / `_deregister_fd`) because `mio::unix::SourceFd` wraps the cross-Unix raw fd model that doesn't extend to Windows HANDLEs. mio on Windows uses IOCP under the hood, but only for mio-aware source types (`mio::net::TcpStream`, etc.) — not raw HANDLEs. Two design options: (a) accept mio-aware socket types at the FFI boundary instead of raw HANDLEs (forces codegen-side platform branching), or (b) build a completion-handler glue layer that translates IOCP's completion-based model into the fd-readiness shape the current FFI assumes. **Cross-platform CI required** — development on macOS / Linux can't validate Windows paths; needs a Windows runner in CI before merge. **M3 milestone gate** per the v64 staging (`Concurrency target staging` below) — Windows IOCP parity is required for the v1 public launch (1M+ idle connections cross-platform). **Unblocked by:** all six runtime-side slices above (the FFI surface contract that Windows IOCP must satisfy is stable). **Blocked by:** Windows CI infrastructure setup.

- [x] **P0 — State-machine transform codegen — network-boundary functions only — shipped 2026-05-26 (slices 1–42).** Implements the spec from the design audit (1) above. Bounded to functions whose effect set includes `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)`; functions with other `suspends` effects (channel receive, custom suspending) stay thread-blocking at v1. Codegen pass runs after monomorphization — each instantiation gets its own state machine. Test coverage shipped per sub-slice: state-struct shape vs. captured-locals (slice 4 / 5); multi-yield functions (slice 7 / 8); yield-inside-loop / yield-inside-conditional (slice 8t); error-path through yield (slices 8u / 8v / 8w with the per-mono `?`-lowering surface); generics-in-yielding-function (slice 8v Phase 2 per-mono state-machine emission with `type_subst` honored). With slice 8ah (terminal-arm call-returning-value) and slice 8ai (return-type widening) shipped, all parent-level scope items are closed.
  1. [x] **Slice 1 — network-boundary-function identification side-table shipped 2026-05-17.** New `Program.callee_network_yield_effect: HashMap<String, bool>` (`CalleeNetworkYieldEffectTable` alias) populated by `Pipeline::effectcheck` immediately after `Program.callee_effectful` from the same `EffectCheckResult`. A callee classifies as network-boundary iff its inferred or declared effect set contains a `sends(Network)` or `receives(Network)` verb-resource pair — `Suspends`-paired-with-anything is intentionally excluded (Receiver.recv, channel waits, custom user suspending stay thread-blocking at v1 per the line-26 spec). Polymorphic / PolymorphicWithFixed declared-effect callees mark `true` conservatively because a monomorphization may bind their effect parameter to a network-bearing effect; the transform itself reads the resolved monomorphized effect set when deciding to apply, so over-counting here is harmless candidate-pool inclusion. Helper `build_callee_network_yield_effect_table` lives next to `build_callee_effectful_table` in `src/cli.rs` and mirrors its structure exactly. **9 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` pin the filter rule: five unit cases on hand-constructed effect sets (Sends/Network=true, Receives/Network=true, Sends|Receives on Heap/Filesystem/Channel/Database=false, all-other-verbs on Network=false, mixed-set-with-one-qualifying-entry=true) and four integration cases through the full effect-check pipeline (seeded `Client.get`/`Client.post`=true, `Receiver.recv` with `suspends`=false, pure function=false, alloc-only function=false). All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 40 test binaries. Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `CalleeNetworkYieldEffectTable` type alias + `Program.callee_network_yield_effect` field), `src/cli.rs` (new helper fn + Pipeline wiring), `tests/effectchecker.rs` (9 new tests). **Unblocks** subsequent slices: the codegen transform pass and the line-17 sub-item-6 lowering-at-yield-points work both consume this side-table to identify which functions / call sites need the network-event-loop park-and-yield path. **Remaining slices under this entry:** per-function yield-point enumeration (build the list of network-effect call sites within each network-boundary function); state-struct shape synthesis (live-range pass to compute captured-locals union across yield points); actual codegen transform (replace function body with poll function + state struct allocation).
  2. [x] **Slice 2 — yield-point enumeration per network-boundary function shipped 2026-05-17.** New `Program.yield_points: HashMap<String, Vec<YieldPoint>>` (`YieldPointsTable` alias, where `YieldPoint { callee: String, span: Span }`) populated by `Pipeline::effectcheck` immediately after `Program.callee_network_yield_effect`. For each network-boundary function (free fn or impl method classified `true` in slice 1's table), walks the body and records every call site whose resolved callee key is also marked `true` in `callee_network_yield_effect`. Resolution rules: `Call { callee: Identifier(name) }` → key is `name`; `Call { callee: Path { segments } }` → key is `segments.join(".")` (matches `Type.method` shape); `MethodCall { .. }` → key looked up in `TypeCheckResult.method_callee_types` keyed by the call expression's `SpanKey`; all other callee shapes (FieldAccess on closure value, function-pointer indirection) → silently skipped (the codegen lowering pass can't park through an unresolved callee without a stable effect signature). Functions without any yield-point calls are omitted from the table — a function may classify as network-boundary via Polymorphic declared-effect-with-candidate-true while having no concrete sub-call yield points within its body (the FFI-primitive-emitting case). Walker lives in `src/cli.rs` (`build_yield_points_table` + `collect_yield_points_in_block` + `collect_yield_points_in_stmt` + `collect_yield_points_in_expr` + `callee_key_from_call` helper); the expression walker covers all `ExprKind` variants that can contain calls (Call, MethodCall, Binary, Unary, Question, OptionalChain, NilCoalesce, FieldAccess, TupleIndex, Index, Block, Unsafe, Try, Seq, Par, If, IfLet, Match, While, WhileLet, For, Loop, LabeledBlock, Closure, Return, Break, Tuple, ArrayLiteral, PrefixCollectionLiteral, RepeatLiteral, MapLiteral, StructLiteral, Pipe, Cast, Range, Lock, Providers, InterpolatedStringLit; leaf shapes — literals, Identifier, Path, SelfValue/Type, PipePlaceholder, OffsetOf, Error — terminate the recursion). The walker reads the program tree by shared reference, so the assignment routes through a local in `Pipeline::effectcheck` to avoid borrowing `self.parsed.program` mutably and immutably at the same time. **7 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` exercise the table on user-declared `effect resource Network;` + `pub fn f() with sends(Network) ...` source through the full pipeline: single yield-point function (one call site → one entry pointing at the call expression's span), three-call function records three yield points in source order (`fetch → upload → fetch`), yield-inside-conditional (if/else with yield in each arm → two yield points), yield-inside-loop (`while true { fetch(); }` → one yield point), pure functions get no entry, calls to non-network helpers in a network-boundary function are not counted as yield points (only fetch among `pure_helper(1) + fetch() + pure_helper(2)`), and a program without any network-boundary callees has an empty `yield_points` table. Helpers `build_callee_network_yield_effect_table` and `build_yield_points_table` made `pub` in `src/cli.rs` and reachable as `karac::cli::*` for direct test invocation — minimal API surface expansion, simpler than driving the cli `Pipeline` (private) from integration tests. `Program.yield_points` is empty after slice 1's tests because the test pipelines stop at effect-check; slice 2's `pipeline_with_yield_points` helper applies the build-helpers explicitly. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 40 test binaries (234 effectchecker, 488 codegen E2E, 215 memory_sanitizer, 1064 typechecker, ... all green; 7 new + 227 pre-existing effectchecker tests). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `YieldPoint` struct + `YieldPointsTable` alias + `Program.yield_points` field; added `use crate::token::Span;` to the top of the file because the new struct references it), `src/cli.rs` (build_yield_points_table + 3 walker helpers + 1 callee-key extractor + Pipeline wiring; `pub` on both new build-helpers), `tests/effectchecker.rs` (7 new tests + `pipeline_with_yield_points` driver). **Unblocks** the next slice (state-struct shape synthesis: a live-range pass over each network-boundary function's body determines the captured-locals union across the yield-point set; needs the yield-point spans to define the suspension-boundary set). The yield-point spans also serve the codegen lowering pass directly — at each marked call site, codegen emits the parking convention. **Remaining slices under this entry:** state-struct shape synthesis (live-range pass); actual codegen transform (replace function body with poll function + state struct allocation); error-path lowering integration (state-struct destructor invocation through `?`); generics-in-yielding-function support.
  3. [x] **Slice 3 — per-yield-point captured-locals via lexical scope tracking shipped 2026-05-17.** Extends `YieldPoint` with `captured_locals: Vec<String>` — at each yield point, the v1 conservative over-approximation of locals the state-machine transform must preserve across the suspension. Names listed in source-introduction order (params first left-to-right, then per-block let-binding sequence). The walker from slice 2 grew into a stateful struct (`YieldPointWalker`) carrying a flat `scope: Vec<String>` stack alongside the network-yield + method-callee maps; pushes happen on `let` / `let-else` / `if let` / `while let` / `for` / match-arm pattern bindings; pops happen at every block exit via `truncate(scope_mark)` discipline. Function parameters (collected through each `Param.pattern.binding_names()` to handle destructuring `let (a, b): (i64, i64)` shape) plus `self` for methods are pre-pushed onto the scope before the body walk. **Bug fix bundled with the slice:** the slice-2 walker descended into `ExprKind::Closure { body, .. }`, but closures form their own state machine — a network-effect call inside a closure body is the closure's yield, not the enclosing function's. The slice-3 walker no longer enters closure bodies (`ExprKind::Closure { .. } => {}` arm dropped recursion). Two helper methods on the walker (`walk_block_with_pattern`, `walk_expr_with_pattern`) encapsulate the "push pattern bindings → walk → pop" idiom used by `if let` / `while let` / `for` / match-arm-body sites; match-arm guards run under the arm's pattern bindings too (a separate inline push/walk/pop). The let-else handler pushes success-branch pattern bindings AFTER walking the else block, matching the source-level convention that else must diverge and its scope doesn't propagate up. **8 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` pin the capture rule: params appear in the captured set (driver(`url`, `retries`) → both names), lets introduced before yield are captured, captures grow across sequential yields (yield 1 sees `a`, yield 2 sees `a` + `b`), a yield in the RHS of `let _x = { fetch(); 0 }` does NOT include `_x` (binding happens after the value expression), bindings introduced in an inner block are captured at yields inside it but POP at block exit so subsequent outer yields don't include them, for-loop pattern bindings are captured at yields inside the body (driver(`items`) → `for x in items.iter() { fetch(); }` → captures `[items, x]`), methods see `self` in their captured set, and a yield inside a closure body does NOT produce an entry for the enclosing function (closure forms its own state machine). All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 40 test binaries (242 effectchecker, 488 codegen E2E, 215 memory_sanitizer, 1064 typechecker, ... all green; 8 new + 234 pre-existing effectchecker tests). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `captured_locals: Vec<String>` field on `YieldPoint`), `src/cli.rs` (slice-2 walker rewritten as `YieldPointWalker` struct method-style with scope tracking; closure body skip; let-else and pattern-binding scope handling), `tests/effectchecker.rs` (8 new tests). **Unblocks** subsequent slices: the captured-locals lists per yield point give the codegen transform enough data to size the state-struct per-yield-arm storage. The over-approximation (captures everything in lexical scope, not just live-across-yield) keeps v1 correct at the cost of larger state structs; a future live-range pass can refine. **Remaining slices under this entry:** state-struct shape synthesis from the captured-locals set + their typechecker-known types (turn the name list into IR-friendly layout); actual codegen transform (replace function body with poll function + state struct allocation); error-path lowering integration (state-struct destructor invocation through `?`); generics-in-yielding-function support.
  4. [x] **Slice 4 — per-function state-struct layout synthesis shipped 2026-05-17.** Lifts slice 3's per-yield-point captured-local *name* lists into a per-function `StateStructLayout { fields: Vec<StateStructField> }` carrying the **union** of captured locals across every yield point in the function body, paired with each binding's surface type name as recorded by the typechecker's `pattern_binding_types` map (`Some("Vec")` / `Some("Hub")` / `Some("String")` / ... for Named / Str / Shared types; `None` for primitive / anonymous / unrecorded shapes — codegen consuming the layout falls through to its primitive-sizing path on absent entries). New `Program.state_struct_layouts: HashMap<String, StateStructLayout>` (`StateStructLayoutTable` alias) populated by `Pipeline::effectcheck` immediately after `Program.yield_points`. The layout's field order is source-introduction: parameters first left-to-right (with `self` at position 0 in methods, carrying the impl-block target-type name as its `type_name` since there is no pattern span for `self`), then per-block let-binding sequence; first occurrence across yield points fixes position. Same-name bindings introduced at different pattern spans (shadowing) get distinct slots — collision is keyed on the introducing pattern's `SpanKey`, not the binding name, so the v1 layout faithfully reflects source-level binding identity. New parallel walker (`StateStructLayoutWalker` in `src/cli.rs`, sibling to slice 3's `YieldPointWalker`) tracks `Vec<ScopeEntry>` where each `ScopeEntry { name, span_key, type_override }` carries the binding name + introducing-pattern-span (for `pattern_binding_types` lookup) + an explicit type-name override slot (used only for `self`). The walker mirrors slice 3's lexical scope discipline exactly — push on `let` / `let-else` / `if let` / `while let` / `for` / match-arm pattern bindings; truncate on block exit — but at each recognized yield-point call site (Call / MethodCall against a callee marked `true` in `callee_network_yield_effect`) invokes `record_yield_point_capture` to merge the current scope into the function-level union via a `HashSet<ScopeEntryKey>` (variants: `Span(SpanKey)` for ordinary bindings, `Synthetic(String)` for `self`). Walker also flips a `had_yield_point` bool on first capture — drives the table's presence rule (only functions with at least one concrete yield-point call in their body get an entry; matches `YieldPointsTable` exactly). Closures are NOT descended into for the same state-machine-per-closure reason as slice 3. New `Pattern::binding_name_spans() -> Vec<(String, Span)>` sibling helper on `src/ast/patterns.rs` returns each leaf binding's name paired with its introducing pattern's span (for `Binding`, the leaf's own span; for `Struct` shorthand fields, the field's `FieldPattern.span`; for `Slice { rest: Bound(_) }`, the parent slice pattern's span as best-effort proxy since the rest marker has no leaf-span — typechecker's `pattern_binding_types` doesn't key rest bindings either, so the proxy miss yields `type_name: None` consistently). **8 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` pin the layout shape: named-type param surfaces its recorded `type_name` (`fn driver(items: Vec[i64])` → `[StateStructField { name: "items", type_name: Some("Vec") }]`); two sequential yields produce union `[a, b]` with the later-introduced `b` in slot 1; method `self` carries the impl target type name (`Hub.run(self)` → `type_name: Some("Hub")`); primitive-typed binding's `type_name` is `None` (`fn driver(n: i64)`); an inner-block let popped before the yield is excluded from the layout; an inner-block let bound BEFORE a yield inside that block IS included; closures form their own state machine — outer function gets no entry when its body has no own network-effect call; pure-helper function has no entry, mirroring `YieldPointsTable`'s presence rule. All clear under `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo fmt --all -- --check`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 40 test binaries (250 effectchecker, 488 codegen E2E, 1064 typechecker, ... all green; 8 new + 242 pre-existing effectchecker tests). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `StateStructField` + `StateStructLayout` structs + `StateStructLayoutTable` alias + `Program.state_struct_layouts` field), `src/ast/patterns.rs` (new `Pattern::binding_name_spans` helper + `collect_binding_name_spans` recursion mirroring `collect_bindings`), `src/cli.rs` (build_state_struct_layouts + StateStructLayoutWalker + walk helpers; `pub` on the new build helper), `tests/effectchecker.rs` (8 new tests + `pipeline_with_state_struct_layouts` driver). **Unblocks** the next slice (actual codegen transform — replace each network-boundary function body with a poll function operating on a state struct sized from this layout). **Remaining slices under this entry:** actual codegen transform (replace function body with poll function + state struct allocation); error-path lowering integration (state-struct destructor invocation through `?`); generics-in-yielding-function support.
  5. [x] **Slice 5 — state-struct LLVM type emission shipped 2026-05-18.** Lifts slice 4's per-function `StateStructLayout` analysis-side data into actual LLVM struct types at codegen time. New `Codegen.state_struct_types: HashMap<String, StructType<'ctx>>` field populated by `emit_state_struct_types` (in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`), invoked from `compile_program` immediately after `declare_enums` and before `collect_soa_layouts` — so user-named struct types (consumed via `llvm_type_for_name`) are resolvable when the state struct's field types are computed. For each entry in `program.state_struct_layouts`, emits `%kara.state.<fn_key>` as a named opaque struct (`Context::opaque_struct_type` + `set_body`) with field 0 = `i32` yield-point tag and fields 1..=N corresponding 1:1 to `StateStructLayout.fields` in source-introduction order: `Some(name)` → routes through `llvm_type_for_name` (Vec/String expand to the `{ptr, i64, i64}` 3-word struct; user-named shared structs collapse to a pointer-sized handle; user-named regular structs use their `struct_types` entry); `None` → `i64` fallback (over-approximates primitives — i8/i32/bool fit in i64; matches `llvm_type_for_name`'s default arm). [x] **Slice 6 — poll-function stub emission shipped 2026-05-18.** First sub-slice of the codegen state-machine transform: lays down the `KaracParkedTask.poll_fn` ABI (`i8 fn(ptr state, ptr cancel)` per line-17 sub-item-2) as a concrete LLVM function for every entry in `program.state_struct_layouts`, so caller-side allocate-state-struct-then-invoke-poll wiring in subsequent sub-slices can target a stable signature without waiting for the full switch-on-tag transform to land. New `Codegen.state_machine_poll_fns: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` field populated by `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` (in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`), invoked from `compile_program` immediately after `emit_state_struct_types`. For each network-boundary function, declares `define internal i8 @__kara_poll_<fn_key>(ptr, ptr)` with a body that GEPs into `state_struct_types[fn_key]` field 0 (the i32 yield-point tag), loads the tag value, then unconditionally returns Pending (`i8 0` — the discriminant pinned by line-17 slice 2's `karac_poll_result_discriminants_match_codegen_abi` test). Two purposes are served by emitting the stub body rather than a bare declaration: (a) the typed GEP keeps the named `%kara.state.<fn_key>` referenced from a real instruction (independent of the slice-5 anchor global, which stays as belt-and-suspenders until the lowering passes are all in place); (b) the body shape is the load-tag prologue every subsequent sub-slice will keep — slice 7 replaces the unconditional `ret i8 0` with a `switch i32 %tag` against the yield-point arm count, slice 8 fills the per-yield-arm captured-locals reload + actual user-code resume, and slice 9 wires the Ready / Err exit edges. Symbol naming uses `__kara_poll_<fn_key>` with the impl-method `Type.method` shape (`__kara_poll_Hub.run`) inheriting the literal `.` from the function key — matches LLVM's symbol-name acceptance and the parallel `__kara_state_type_anchor_<fn_key>` slice-5 convention. Linkage is `Internal` (module-local, not link-visible) — caller-side wiring in slice 7+ looks up the FunctionValue through the side-table rather than the symbol table. Keys are emitted in sorted order so the IR text is deterministic across runs. **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `__kara_poll_driver` defined with internal linkage and `i8 @__kara_poll_driver(ptr, ptr)` signature for a network-boundary free fn; the stub body GEPs `%kara.state.driver` field 0 + loads i32 (pins the typed-GEP referencing of the state struct); body returns `ret i8 0` (Pending stub); impl-method poll-fn uses the `__kara_poll_Hub.run` name shape (literal `.` in the symbol); pure functions emit no `__kara_poll_*` symbol (presence rule from slice-4 layout propagates). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 41 test binaries (503 codegen E2E, 1072 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 5 new + 498 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `state_machine_poll_fns` field + `HashMap::new()` init + 7-line wiring block in `compile_program` after `emit_state_struct_types`), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` method, ~70 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (5 new tests). **Unblocks** the next sub-slice — the switch-on-tag dispatch that turns the unconditional Pending return into per-yield-arm branching. **Remaining sub-slices under line 26 slice 6+:** switch-on-tag dispatch at entry (replaces the unconditional `ret i8 0` with a `switch i32 %tag` against yield-arm labels); per-yield-arm body emission (captured-locals reload from state struct + actual user-code resume + register_fd call at the yield site + Pending return); Ready / Err exit edges (final-yield arm returns Ready discriminant carrying the function's return value); caller-side allocate-state-struct-then-invoke-poll lowering (replaces direct calls to network-boundary fns with state-struct alloca + initial poll invocation through the line-17 scheduler dispatcher); error-path lowering integration (state-struct destructor through `?`); generics-in-yielding-function support.

[x] **Slice 7 — switch-on-tag dispatch in poll-fn body shipped 2026-05-18.** Replaces slice 6's unconditional `ret i8 0` with `switch i32 %tag, label %tag_unreachable [...]` against N+1 arm labels for N yield points — `state_0` is the initial-call entry state (before any yield in the function body), and `state_i` for `i` in 1..=N is the post-yield resume state for the i-th yield point. Arm count derives from `program.yield_points[fn_key].len()` + 1 (slice 4's presence rule guarantees yield_points is non-empty when state_struct_layouts has an entry, so N ≥ 1 in practice). The default arm goes to a `tag_unreachable` block holding a single `unreachable` instruction — the runtime never invokes the poll-fn with an out-of-range tag (state-struct initializer pins tag=0 at allocation; tag transitions are codegen-controlled), and the `unreachable` hint unlocks downstream optimization of the switch (jump-table compaction, dead-arm dropping). Per-arm bodies are still Pending-return stubs at slice 7 — the observable per-arm behavior matches slice 6 — so the switch shape lands without depending on the per-yield-arm logic that lives in slice 8. The IR shape after slice 7:
     ```llvm
     define internal i8 @__kara_poll_driver(ptr %0, ptr %1) {
     entry:
       %tag_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.driver, ptr %0, i32 0, i32 0
       %tag = load i32, ptr %tag_ptr
       switch i32 %tag, label %tag_unreachable [
         i32 0, label %state_0
         i32 1, label %state_1
       ]
     state_0:                                          ; first invocation
       ret i8 0                                        ;   ↳ slice 8: run body until yield 1
     state_1:                                          ; post-yield-1 resume
       ret i8 0                                        ;   ↳ slice 8: reload captures, continue body
     tag_unreachable:
       unreachable
     }
     ```
     **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `switch i32 %tag` appears in the poll-fn body; arm count is N+1 for N yield points (1-yield case has `state_0` and `state_1`, no `state_2`); default arm is `tag_unreachable:` with the `unreachable` instruction; multi-yield case (3 yields → 4 arms `state_0` through `state_3`, no `state_4`). New helper `extract_fn_ir(ir, fn_name)` in the test module carves the textual IR for a single function out of the module dump, so per-function assertions don't trip over arm-label collisions if another function happens to share state-block names. All 5 slice-6 tests continue to pass — the Pending-return assertion (`ret i8 0`) now matches multiple sites inside the per-arm bodies, but the existing `body.contains("ret i8 0")` substring check stays green. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 42 test binaries (507 codegen E2E, 1072 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 503 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-7 dispatch block in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, ~50 lines: arm/default-block creation + `build_switch` call + per-arm Pending returns + `build_unreachable` for the default), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests + `extract_fn_ir` test helper). **Unblocks** slice 8 — the per-yield-arm body emission that replaces each arm's stub `ret i8 0` with captured-locals reload from the state struct, user-code resume from the corresponding yield point, register_fd call at the yield boundary, and the Pending return at the suspension site.

[x] **Slice 8a — captured-locals reload prologue shipped 2026-05-18.** First sub-slice of the per-arm body work: each `state_i` arm (i in 0..=N for N yield points) now emits a uniform reload prologue ahead of its terminating `ret i8 0`. For every captured local in `program.state_struct_layouts[fn_key].fields`, the prologue emits a four-instruction sequence — `getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.<fn_key>, ptr %state, i32 0, i32 <field_idx+1>` to step from the struct base to the captured-local field (`+1` to skip the i32 tag at field 0), `load <field_ty>` to read the value, `alloca <field_ty>` to reserve a stack slot for it, and `store <field_ty>` to deposit the reloaded value into the slot. SSA names use the source binding's name as the prefix (`%items.field_ptr`, `%items.reload`, `%items.slot`) so subsequent sub-slices that walk the slot via the existing `variables` registry resolve through the same name. Field types come from `state_struct.get_field_type_at_index(idx+1)` (slice 5's struct shape) — `Vec[T]` / `String` expand to the inline `{ ptr, i64, i64 }` 3-word load; user-named shared structs collapse to a pointer-sized load; primitives use the i64 fallback. The prologue runs uniformly across every state arm (state_0 through state_N), not just resume arms (state_1..=N) — for state_0 (initial call) some fields may be uninitialized in the caller-side state-struct allocator, but slice 8b's body-splitting will not reference the not-yet-bound locals at state_0 so the load-of-zero is harmless and the uniform per-arm shape keeps the codegen contained. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: GEP+load+alloca+store quadruple appears for a `Vec[i64]` captured local with the expected inline-Vec types; reload prologue appears in every state arm (2 GEPs to field 1 for a 1-yield function with 1 captured local = one per arm); multi-field layout (2 captured locals × 3 arms = 3 GEPs to field 1 + 3 GEPs to field 2 in a 2-yield function); empty layout (no params, no in-scope lets at yield) emits arms with only the tag GEP at field 0, no captured-local GEPs. All 9 prior slice-6 / slice-7 tests stay green — the new reload prologue precedes the `ret i8 0` in each arm, so the existing per-arm Pending-return assertions continue to match. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 42 test binaries (511 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 507 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8a reload block inside the per-arm loop in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, ~30 lines: layout lookup + per-field GEP/load/alloca/store quadruple), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** slice 8b — body-splitting at yield-point spans: take the user's AST body, slice it at `program.yield_points[fn_key]` spans, emit each segment into the corresponding state arm with the reloaded slots from this slice serving as the local-variable backing store.

[x] **Slice 8b — state-transition skeleton shipped 2026-05-18.** Lays down the state-machine state-transition mechanic on top of slice 8a's reload prologue: non-terminal state arms (`state_i` for i in 0..N-1, where N = yield-point count) write the next tag value `i+1` into state struct field 0 via `getelementptr inbounds + store i32` before returning Pending, so the next poll-fn invocation routes to `state_{i+1}` via slice 7's switch dispatch. The terminal arm (`state_N`) returns Ready (`i8 1`) instead of Pending — the function has completed and the caller can observe the result. Tag-store GEP names use the per-arm form `%state_<arm_idx>.next_tag_ptr` for IR readability; SSA renaming is deterministic across runs given slice 6's sorted-key emission order. The slice forms a minimal but real state machine: a function with N yield points can now (after caller-side state-struct allocation in slice 8e+) loop through tag transitions 0 → 1 → ... → N → Ready over N+1 poll-fn invocations, even though the arms still contain no user-code lowering. Slice 8c+ adds the actual user-code body between slice-8a's reload prologue and slice-8b's tag-store / Ready return. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: non-terminal arm `state_0` stores `i32 1` to state struct field 0 (next tag for the 1-yield case); terminal arm returns `ret i8 1` (Ready); multi-yield case (2 yields → 3 arms) has tag transitions 1 in state_0 and 2 in state_1 with no tag-store in terminal state_2; 3-yield case (4 arms) has exactly one `ret i8 1` (terminal) and three `ret i8 0` (non-terminal Pending). All 13 prior slice-6 / slice-7 / slice-8a tests stay green — slice-8b adds new instructions to each arm but doesn't remove any existing shape. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 42 test binaries (515 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 511 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8b state-transition block inside the per-arm loop in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, ~30 lines: arm-index branch on `arm_idx < yield_count` → tag-GEP/store + Pending return; else → Ready return), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** slice 8c — the user-code lowering between reload prologue and tag-store. For the "trivial" case (functions where every yield-point call sits at the top level of the function body, no nested-in-if/loop yields), slice 8c can emit each AST sub-segment between yield-points into the corresponding state arm using the slice-8a reloaded slots as the variable-lookup backing store.

[x] **Slice 8c — state-struct constructor helper shipped 2026-05-18.** For each network-boundary function, codegen emits a no-arg helper `define internal ptr @__kara_state_new_<fn_key>()` that mallocs a fresh state struct of the right size, initializes the i32 yield-point tag at field 0 to 0 (so the next poll-fn invocation routes to the entry arm `state_0` via slice 7's switch dispatch), and returns the heap pointer. Body uses inkwell's `state_struct.size_of()` to compute the LLVM-canonical size constant, then `call ptr @malloc(i64 <size>)` (the existing `Codegen.malloc_fn` declared at module-build time), then `getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.<fn_key>, ptr <alloc>, i32 0, i32 0` + `store i32 0` for the tag init, and `ret ptr <alloc>`. Captured-local fields (state struct fields 1..N) are intentionally left uninitialized — slice 8a's reload prologue will load `poison`/`undef` from them, but slice 8b's terminal-vs-non-terminal arm logic doesn't reference the loaded values, so the loads are harmless at this slice. Slice 8d+ will either (a) thread the function's parameters into the caller-side state-struct initialization before invoking the poll-fn, or (b) extend the constructor to memset the whole struct — the choice depends on whether caller-side param-storage is needed before or after the constructor call. Stored in a new `Codegen.state_machine_state_constructors: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` side-table populated by `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` (in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`), invoked from `compile_program` immediately after `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`. Internal linkage; deterministic emission via sorted keys (matches slice 6's convention). **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: constructor defined with internal linkage and `ptr @__kara_state_new_driver()` signature for a network-boundary fn; body calls `@malloc` and binds the result to `%state.alloc`; body initializes the tag via `store i32 0, ptr %tag_init_ptr` with a typed GEP into the state struct; pure functions emit no constructor (presence rule from slice 4 propagates). All 17 prior poll-fn tests stay green — the constructor emit is additive. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 43 test binaries (519 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 515 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `state_machine_state_constructors` field + `HashMap::new()` init + 5-line wiring block in `compile_program` after `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` method, ~60 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** slice 8d — caller-side wiring that replaces each direct call to a network-boundary function with `call ptr @__kara_state_new_<callee>()` followed by `call i8 @__kara_poll_<callee>(<state>, ptr null)`, observing the discriminant and either retaining the state-struct pointer for the next invocation (Pending) or `free`ing it and continuing (Ready/Err). Slice 8e+ extends the wiring to actually loop until Ready, integrating the line-17 runtime scheduler dispatcher for cooperative cancellation + event-loop yielding.
