[x] **Slice 8d — caller-side network-boundary intercept shipped 2026-05-18.** Hook in `compile_call` (immediately after the closure-call check, before the module symbol lookup) that intercepts calls to any callee in `state_machine_state_constructors` (slice 8c's table). The intercept emits the state-machine invocation shape:
       ```llvm
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_<name>()
       br label %kara.poll_loop
     kara.poll_loop:
       %kara.poll_result = call i8 @__kara_poll_<name>(ptr %kara.state, ptr null)
       %kara.is_pending = icmp eq i8 %kara.poll_result, 0
       br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_loop, label %kara.poll_done
     kara.poll_done:
       call void @free(ptr %kara.state)
       ; subsequent IR continues here
       ```
       The synchronous spin-loop is a v1 placeholder — slice 8e+ replaces it with a yield to the line-17 scheduler dispatcher so that a Pending observation parks the parent task until the event loop signals readiness. v1 args are silently dropped (test programs use no-arg shapes); a follow-on slice threads call-args through state-struct captured-local fields at constructor invocation time. The intercept fires only when the callee resolves to an `Identifier(name)` or single-segment `Path` whose name is in `state_machine_state_constructors` — generic / closure / `Type.assoc` shapes route through their existing paths, and the slice-4 presence rule guarantees network-boundary fns aren't generic at v1. Cancel arg is `ptr null` for now (line-17 slice 4's process-global cancel placeholder); future slice routes the dispatcher's cancel flag through here for cooperative cancellation propagation. Return value is `i64 0` — v1 network-boundary fns return unit; non-unit returns land via state-struct terminal field in a later slice. LLVM auto-disambiguates `kara.poll_loop` / `kara.poll_done` labels across multiple call sites in the same caller (appends `1`, `2`, … suffixes). **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: a caller (`main`) calling a network-boundary `driver()` emits the state-constructor call (not the direct `call void @driver()`); the intercept emits `kara.poll_loop:` block with the poll-fn call carrying state-ptr + null cancel and the `icmp eq i8 ..., 0` Pending compare; the `kara.poll_done:` block calls `@free` on the state struct; pure-helper calls in the same caller still lower to direct calls (intercept fires only for network-boundary callees); two call sites in the same caller produce two distinct ctor invocations + at least two poll-loop label occurrences. All 21 prior poll-fn / state-constructor tests stay green — slice 8d only adds caller-side IR, doesn't change the state-machine helpers themselves. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 43 test binaries (524 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 5 new + 519 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8d intercept block before module symbol lookup, ~80 lines: state-constructor call + loop/done block creation + poll-fn invoke + Pending compare + free), `tests/codegen.rs` (5 new tests). **The end-to-end state-machine ABI is now wired:** caller invokes constructor → state machine loops through tag transitions via poll-fn → terminal arm returns Ready → caller frees state struct. The user code inside each state arm is still a stub (slice 7's switch + slice 8a's reload + slice 8b's tag-store, no actual user statements between), and the loop is synchronous. **Unblocks** slice 8e — replace the synchronous spin-loop with a runtime-scheduler yield on Pending observation so the parent task parks instead of busy-waiting, integrating with the line-17 dispatcher + event loop for cooperative cancellation and event-loop-driven resumption.
  12. [x] **Slice 8e — cooperative yield on Pending shipped 2026-05-18.** Replaces slice 8d's busy-spin Pending-branch-to-loop with a third block that calls `sched_yield` before re-entering the poll loop. New `Codegen.sched_yield_fn: FunctionValue<'ctx>` field declared at module-build time alongside malloc / free / memcmp: `let sched_yield_type = i32_type.fn_type(&[], false); let sched_yield_fn = module.add_function("sched_yield", sched_yield_type, Some(Linkage::External));`. The intercept restructure splits the Pending path:
       ```llvm
       kara.poll_loop:
         %kara.poll_result = call i8 @__kara_poll_<name>(ptr %kara.state, ptr null)
         %kara.is_pending = icmp eq i8 %kara.poll_result, 0
         br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_yield, label %kara.poll_done
       kara.poll_yield:
         %kara.yield_result = call i32 @sched_yield()
         br label %kara.poll_loop
       kara.poll_done:
         call void @free(ptr %kara.state)
         ; subsequent IR continues here
       ```
       The cooperative yield matters because without it the parent thread busy-spins on poll-fn invocations, starving the line-17 dispatcher thread (and any other tasks on the same scheduler) of cycles to process event-loop readiness wakeups. With the yield, the OS scheduler gives other threads a quantum on every Pending observation — the dispatcher can run its `take_wakeups` drain, the event-loop poll can process fd readiness, and parked tasks can be resumed in their own time. The `sched_yield` return value (`i32` non-zero on catastrophic OS failure) is discarded — the linked libc on Linux / macOS always returns 0 in practice, and the not-recoverable failure path isn't actionable from the IR. Windows IOCP support (line 17 sub-item 7) will need a `SwitchToThread` analog; v1 targets Linux / macOS where sched_yield is available. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `kara.poll_yield:` block appears in the caller's IR; module declares `declare i32 @sched_yield()` extern AND the yield block invokes it via `call i32 @sched_yield()`; the Pending branch routes through `kara.poll_yield` (literal `br i1 %kara.is_pending, label %kara.poll_yield, label %kara.poll_done`); the yield block branches back to `kara.poll_loop`. All 5 slice-8d tests stay green — the new yield block is additive; the slice-8d Pending-loopback test was checking presence of the loop label, not the branch target. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 45 test binaries (528 codegen E2E, 1078 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, 8 raii_check, ... all green; 4 new + 524 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `sched_yield_fn` field + extern declaration in `Codegen::new` alongside malloc / free / memcmp + struct init wiring), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8e restructure of the intercept block: split Pending branch into `kara.poll_yield` indirection, ~15 added lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** future slices — the cooperative yield gives the runtime dispatcher real cycles to drive parked tasks. Next sub-slices under line 26: thread call-args through state-struct captured-local fields at constructor invocation time; emit user-code statements between yield-points in each state arm (the body-splitting work deferred from earlier sub-slice discussions); error-path lowering integration through `?`; generics-in-yielding-function support.
  13. [x] **Slice 8f — caller-side arg-storing into state struct shipped 2026-05-18.** Threads call args into the state struct's captured-local fields ahead of the first poll-fn invocation. Without this, slice 8d's intercept silently dropped args — `driver(my_vec)` invoked the constructor + poll loop but `my_vec` never reached the callee. Slice 8f closes the loop: in the compile_call intercept, after the `__kara_state_new_<name>()` call, iterate `args[]` with index `i`, compile each arg expression via the existing `compile_expr` machinery, GEP into state struct field `i+1` (skipping the i32 tag at field 0), and store the compiled value. The mapping is direct because slice 4's layout puts parameters first in field order: layout slot `i` ↔ state struct field `i+1` ↔ call arg `i`. Slice-4 let-binding slots (positions K..N for the K-param case) stay uninitialized at construction — they're populated by the state-machine transform itself when execution reaches the let-site (future slice). The arg-store sites appear textually before the `br label %kara.poll_loop` entry branch, guaranteeing args are in place by the time the first poll-fn invocation runs. The IR shape after slice 8f for `fn driver(n: i64)` called via `main() { driver(42); }`:
       ```llvm
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_driver()
       %kara.arg0.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.driver, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 1
       store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr
       br label %kara.poll_loop
       ```
       v1 scope restrictions: free-function calls only (method-call intercept lands alongside the method-call intercept itself in a follow-on slice); owned-arg semantics — `ref` / `mut ref` flagging through the state struct is deferred to the slice that handles cross-yield-point borrows; non-`Vec` complex types are passed as opaque LLVM values via the standard `compile_expr` + `build_store` pair, matching the slice-5 state struct's field types. **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: single-arg primitive `driver(42)` GEPs into field 1 and stores `i64 42`; two-arg `driver(1, 2)` GEPs into fields 1 + 2 and stores both literals; no-arg call emits no `kara.argN.field_ptr` sites; identifier arg `driver(x)` where `x: i64` is let-bound stores a loaded SSA value (not a literal) into field 1; arg-store sites appear textually before the `br label %kara.poll_loop` entry branch. All 9 prior caller-side / slice-8e tests stay green — slice 8f only adds IR between the constructor call and the poll-loop entry. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 45 test binaries (533 codegen E2E, ... all green; 5 new + 528 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8f arg-store loop in the intercept block, ~20 lines: state struct lookup + per-arg compile + GEP + store), `tests/codegen.rs` (5 new tests). **Unblocks** the user-code body-splitting work (the next major slice under line 26) — with args reachable in the state struct from arm 0 onward, the per-arm body lowering can reference the slice-8a reloaded slots as the canonical variable-lookup backing store for both parameters and let-bindings.

[x] **Slice 8g — method-call network-boundary intercept shipped 2026-05-18.** Mirrors slice 8d's free-function intercept (`compile_call`) for the `obj.method(args)` shape in `compile_method_call`. Hook fires ahead of every other method-call dispatch path (Option/Result `unwrap`-style shortcuts, indexed-receiver, field-receiver, entry-chain, clone-on-collection) so a network-boundary method's resolved `Type.method` key is never lost to a receiver-shape shortcut emitting an inappropriate direct call. The hook reads the slice-2-of-line-26 `method_callee_types` side-table for the resolved `Type.method` key and, when that key is in `state_machine_state_constructors`, emits the full state-machine invocation shape: compile receiver via `compile_expr`; call `__kara_state_new_<Type.method>()`; store the receiver SSA value into state struct field 1 (`self` is at slice 4's layout position 0, mapping to field 1 after the i32 tag at field 0); store each method arg into fields 2..=K via the existing slice-8f-style per-arg compile + GEP + store loop; emit the slice-8e poll loop with cooperative `sched_yield` on Pending; `free` the state struct on done. The IR shape after slice 8g for `impl Hub { fn run(self, n: i64) { ... } }` called via `main() { h.run(42); }`:
       ```llvm
       %recv = ...
       %kara.state = call ptr @__kara_state_new_Hub.run()
       %kara.self.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.Hub.run, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 1
       store %Hub %recv, ptr %kara.self.field_ptr
       %kara.arg0.field_ptr = getelementptr inbounds %kara.state.Hub.run, ptr %kara.state, i32 0, i32 2
       store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr
       br label %kara.poll_loop
       ; ... slice-8d/8e poll-loop + yield + done blocks ...
       ```
       v1 scope: regular structs only — `shared struct` receivers are rejected by line 31 slice 1 (`E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD`) before the codegen sees them; line 31 slice 2's `CancelSafe` marker will eventually allow user-extensible opt-in. Owned-receiver semantics — `ref self` / `mut ref self` receivers through the state struct are deferred to the same slice that adds ref-passing through arg-storing. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: method intercept emits state constructor + poll-loop block + poll-fn invocation for `h.run()` on a `struct Hub`; receiver stores into state struct field 1 via `%kara.self.field_ptr`; non-network methods (`h.pure_count()`) still use direct dispatch (`@__kara_state_new_Hub.pure_count` absent); multi-arg method `h.run(42)` stores receiver into field 1 + arg into field 2. All 15 prior caller-side / slice-8f tests stay green — slice 8g is purely additive for method-call paths. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (537 codegen E2E, ... all green; 4 new + 533 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (slice-8g intercept block at the top of `compile_method_call` after the cancel-check, ~110 lines: state-machine helper lookups + receiver compile + ctor call + receiver-store into field 1 + per-arg compile/GEP/store loop into fields 2..=K + poll loop + cooperative yield + done + free), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **End-to-end state-machine ABI now spans both free-function and method-call dispatch surfaces.** Next sub-slices under line 26: user-code body-splitting between yields (the big remaining piece); non-unit return values through the state-struct terminal field; error-path lowering through `?`; generics-in-yielding-function support; ref-passing for both arg-storing and method receivers.
  15. [x] **Slice 8h — body-splitting for void calls between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** First cut of the user-code lowering between yield points in each state arm. The poll-fn body now walks the user function's body AST, partitions statements at yield-point spans (via the slice-2-of-line-26 `yield_points` table), and emits `call void @<name>()` for each non-yield arg-less `Call(Identifier)` statement with a void-returning callee in the corresponding state arm. The call emission lands between the slice-8a reload prologue and the slice-8b tag-store / Ready return, so a `fn driver() { helper(); fetch(); }` now produces a `__kara_poll_driver` whose state_0 body is: reload prologue → `call void @helper()` → tag-store(1) → Pending return; state_1 (terminal): reload prologue → Ready return. v1 scope restrictions: only `Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier(name), []))` shapes emit; method calls, args-bearing free-fn calls, let bindings, control flow (`if`/`while`/`match`/`for`), and non-void returns are silently skipped — the supported-statement set grows in subsequent slices as receiver-storing / arg-passing / typed-return / control-flow handling lands. **Compilation-order shift required for slice 8h to work:** the `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` call moved from its early position (alongside slice 5's `emit_state_struct_types`, line ~1688) to just before user body compilation (line ~1866, after `declare_function` for all user free fns and impl methods + `emit_provider_vtables` + `pre_emit_hot_swap_table`). The move was necessary because the poll-fn body emission now calls `self.module.get_function(callee_name)` to look up the LLVM `FunctionValue` for non-yield user-code callees — that symbol must be declared first. `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` stayed at the early position because it only references `state_struct_types` + `malloc` (both available early), not user fns. New module-level `find_function_ast` helper in `declarations.rs` resolves an `fn_key` (`"name"` for free fns, `"Type.method"` for impl methods) to its `&Function` AST node by scanning `program.items`. The walker categorises each top-level `Stmt::Expr(ExprKind::Call { callee, args })`: if `expr.span` matches the next pending `yield_points[fn_key][cur_arm].span` (yield_points entries are recorded in source order by slice 2's walker), the statement is a yield-point that advances `cur_arm += 1` without queuing; otherwise, if it's an arg-less bare-identifier call, queue the name into `per_arm_calls[cur_arm]`. Inside the per-arm loop, after the reload prologue, iterate the queued names and emit `call void @<name>()` for each callee that's declared with a void return type — non-void returns are skipped at v1 (a non-void call without a named SSA binding would produce malformed IR, and threading return values through the state struct's terminal field is a separate slice). **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: pre-yield `helper()` call appears in state_0 before the tag-store; post-yield `helper()` call appears in the terminal arm before `ret i8 1`; multi-yield case `{ a(); fetch(); b(); fetch(); c(); }` emits a/b/c in state_0/state_1/state_2 in the right order; trivial yield-only body (`fn driver() { fetch(); }`) emits no extra calls. All 17 prior poll-fn tests stay green — the move doesn't change the emission shape, and slice 8h's body-splitting only ADDS calls between the existing reload and tag-store / Ready return. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 47 test binaries (543 codegen E2E, ... all green; 4 new + 539 pre-existing codegen tests). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (move `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` call from line ~1688 to ~1866), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8h body-splitting block in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` + new `find_function_ast` module-level helper, ~90 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansion: handling method-call statements between yields (mirrors slice 8h's free-function path but with receiver compilation); handling args-bearing calls (compile args + emit non-void calls); handling let-bindings (introduce local allocas in the appropriate state arm with proper scope tracking); handling control flow (`if` / `while` / `for` need per-arm-internal CFG construction); non-unit returns (terminal arm writes return value into a state-struct terminal field, caller-side loads after Ready observation).
  16. [x] **Slice 8i — non-unit return value through state struct terminal field shipped 2026-05-18.** Adds v1 support for network-boundary functions returning `i64`. Each affected fn's state struct gains a terminal `i64` field appended after the captured-local fields; the poll-fn's terminal arm writes a placeholder `i64 0` into that field before returning Ready; caller-side intercepts (free-function + method-call) load the terminal field after the `kara.poll_done` block and use that value as the call's return value, replacing the unconditional `i64 0` from earlier slices. New `Codegen.state_machine_return_types: HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>` side-table maps each fn_key whose return type matches the v1 supported set (`i64` only) to its LLVM type — populated by `emit_state_struct_types` (slice 5) while walking the user `Function` AST via the slice-8h `find_function_ast` helper. New module-level `is_i64_return_type` helper in `declarations.rs` matches `TypeKind::Path` whose single segment is `"i64"`. The terminal field's index in the state struct is `1 + N` (after the i32 tag at 0 and the N captured-local fields), so terminal arm and caller-side intercepts both compute `state_struct.count_fields() - 1` to find it. The load-before-free ordering on the caller side is load-critical: GEP-then-load runs in the `kara.poll_done` block, then `@free` releases the heap allocation — reversing the order would dereference freed memory. **Body-splitting handoff:** the terminal arm stores a constant `i64 0` placeholder rather than the user's actual final-expression value because the body-splitting work for non-trivial final exprs (anything beyond a literal — identifier references, binary ops, function calls returning values) requires variables-scope plumbing that the line-26 sub-slices haven't reached. The end-to-end shape is wired and tested with the placeholder; a follow-on slice replaces the placeholder with the actual return-expression value once body-splitting supports expressions that reach the function's final position. v1 scope: `i64` returns only; `i32` / `u32` / `bool` / `f64` / Vec / String / shared structs / user structs etc. stay on the unit-return path until follow-on slices widen the supported set. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: state struct for `fn driver() -> i64 with sends(Network) ...` shape is `{ i32, i64 }` (tag + terminal); poll-fn terminal arm stores `i64 0` into `%kara.return.field_ptr` before `ret i8 1`; caller-side intercept loads the terminal field via the named GEP before `@free`, with load-before-free ordering preserved; unit-returning callees keep existing behavior (no terminal field in state struct, no caller-side load). All 45 prior caller-side / poll-fn / state-constructor / body-splitting / method-intercept tests stay green. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `state_machine_return_types` field + `HashMap::new()` init), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `is_i64_return_type` helper + slice-8i terminal-field append in `emit_state_struct_types` + terminal-arm placeholder store in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (slice-8d intercept loads terminal field before `@free`), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (slice-8g intercept mirror), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the user-level final-expression body-splitting: once a future slice handles expression statements + variable scope inside arm bodies, the terminal arm's placeholder `i64 0` becomes the user's actual final-expression value (tracked as slice 8ah). Also unblocks widening the supported return-type set (i32/bool/Vec/String/structs) — the slice-5/8b/8d/8g touch points are already structured for type-keyed dispatch through `state_machine_return_types` (tracked as slice 8ai).

[x] **Slice 8j — method-call body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.**  Extends slice 8h's free-function body-splitting (`Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier, []))`) to also cover `Stmt::Expr(MethodCall { object, args: [], .. })` where the receiver is a captured layout-field (`SelfValue` → field `"self"` for impl methods, or `Identifier(name)` where `name` resolves to a slice-4 layout field) and the resolved `Type.method` LLVM function returns void. Per-arm queueing now uses a `BodySplitStmt` enum with two variants (`FreeFnCall(name)` for slice 8h shape, `MethodCall { receiver_field, callee_key }` for slice 8j) so a single walker handles both. Resolution of the `Type.method` callee key reads from `program.method_callee_types[(span.offset, span.length)]` — the same typechecker side-table the slice-2 yield-point walker uses, populated during `infer_method_call`. The first-param ABI dispatch mirrors `compile_method_call`'s existing user-side discipline (`src/codegen/method_call.rs:543-548`), keeping the slice 8j path consistent with how methods are called everywhere else in the codegen. **v1 scope restrictions (carried forward from slice 8h):** receiver must be `SelfValue` or a captured-layout `Identifier`; args list must be empty; method must return void; non-yield method calls only (yield-point method calls advance the arm via the existing slice-8h span comparison). Method calls with non-captured receivers (chained `m.first().second()`, field-access receivers `obj.inner.method()`, literal receivers, etc.) are silently skipped at v1 — the body-splitting walker's coverage grows incrementally as receiver shapes get threaded through. **Tests use free-fn drivers with let-bound identifier receivers (`fn driver() { let h = Hub { count: 0 }; h.helper(); fetch(); }`) rather than impl-method bodies with `self.method()`,** because the codegen's user-side `compile_method_call` doesn't yet resolve `SelfValue` receivers via `inferred_receiver_type` (an existing limitation that's orthogonal to slice 8j — the body-splitting walker handles `SelfValue` correctly; the test source just can't trigger that path without first fixing user-side self-method dispatch). **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: pre-yield `h.helper()` emits `call void @Hub.helper(...)` in state_0 before the tag-store to state_1; post-yield `h.helper()` emits in the terminal arm before the Ready return; multi-yield case `let h = ...; h.a(); fetch(); h.b(); fetch(); h.c();` emits a/b/c in state_0/state_1/state_2 in the right order; pins that the receiver argument is the slice-8a `%h.slot` pointer (regression pin that the slot mechanic actually wires through). All 17 prior poll-fn / slice-8h body-splitting / slice-8i return-value tests stay green — slice 8j is additive to the per-arm emission loop, the existing `FreeFnCall` branch keeps its slice-8h shape exactly. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 47 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodySplitStmt` enum + walker classification arm for `MethodCall` + slot-map collection during reload prologue + per-arm emission dispatch on the enum, ~70 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: args-bearing method/free-fn calls between yields (the per-arm slot map gives the body-splitting walker the variable-lookup backing store it needs to compile arg expressions referencing captured locals); let-bindings introducing arm-local allocas (the slot map is the foundation; let-introduced names join via the same per-arm dispatch); control flow inside arms (`if`/`while`/`match`/`for` need per-arm CFG construction but can re-use the slot map for any captured-local read inside the branch bodies); user's actual final-expression value through the slice-8i terminal-arm placeholder (once expression statements are supported, the placeholder `i64 0` becomes the user's actual return).
