[x] **Slice 8k — args-bearing free-fn body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** Extends slice 8h's free-function body-splitting (`Stmt::Expr(Call(Identifier, []))`) to accept zero-or-more args per call, where each arg is in a recognised v1 shape (`ExprKind::Integer(n, _)` → emitted as `i64` const; `ExprKind::Identifier(name)` where `name` resolves to a slice-4 layout field → loaded from the slice-8a reload-prologue slot). Any unrecognised arg shape (binary expressions, method-call args, field accesses, struct literals, etc.) causes the WHOLE call to be silently skipped — same conservative "non-emittable shape dropped" rule slice 8h established, mirrored at arg granularity. `BodySplitStmt::FreeFnCall` widened from `(String)` to `{ name: String, args: Vec<BodyArg> }`; new sibling enum `BodyArg { IntLit(i64), Slot(String) }` captures the recognised shapes; new module-level `recognize_body_arg(expr, layout_field_names) -> Option<BodyArg>` runs at walker time per arg. Per-arm emission compiles each `BodyArg` into a `BasicMetadataValueEnum`: `IntLit(v)` → `context.i64_type().const_int(v as u64, true)`; `Slot(name)` → looks up `slot_map[name]` (the per-arm `(slot_ty, slot_ptr)` map from slice 8j), emits `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.arg")` to pass the slot's stored value by value; vector is then handed to `build_call(callee_fn, &compiled, "")`. Defensive: if `slot_map` lookup fails for a `Slot(name)` arg despite the walker having pre-checked `layout_field_names`, the call is skipped via an `arg_ok = false` continue — guards against any future divergence between the walker's pre-classification and the emission-time slot map. **v1 type lowering is conservative `i64` for integer literals** (matches the state-struct primitive fallback in slice 5); narrower / signed-unsigned distinctions stay deferred until the typechecker's recorded callee param type starts flowing into the walker — a fine extension because most user network-boundary calls in v1 carry `i64` / `String` / `Vec[T]` shapes whose ABI is uniform at the slot level. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: integer literal arg `take(42)` emits `call void @take(i64 42)` before the state_0 tag-store; identifier arg `take(n)` (where `n` is a captured param) emits `load i64, ptr %n.slot` then `call void @take(i64 %n.arg)`; multi-arg `mix(n, 7)` mixes slot-loaded + literal in source order (`call void @mix(i64 %n.arg, i64 7)`); unrecognised arg `take(n + 1)` (binary op) is silently dropped — no `call void @take` in the poll-fn. All 21 prior poll-fn / slice-8h void-call / slice-8j method-call tests stay green; the `FreeFnCall { name, args: vec![] }` shape produced by an arg-less call still emits `call void @<name>()` exactly as slice 8h tests expect. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodyArg` enum + `recognize_body_arg` helper + widened `BodySplitStmt::FreeFnCall` + per-arm emission arg-compile loop, ~50 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: args-bearing method calls between yields (mirror of slice 8j with the slice-8k arg-compile loop applied to `MethodCall.args`); typed-aware arg lowering (consume the typechecker's recorded param types so `i32` / `u32` / `bool` / pointer-typed args don't silently lower to `i64`); let-bindings introducing arm-local allocas (the slot map is already arm-scoped, so a let inside an arm just needs to register its alloca into the same map under the binding name).
  19. [x] **Slice 8l — args-bearing method-call body-splitting between yields shipped 2026-05-18.** Mirrors slice 8k's `BodyArg`-driven arg-compile loop onto `BodySplitStmt::MethodCall`. The MethodCall variant widens from `{ receiver_field, callee_key }` to `{ receiver_field, callee_key, args: Vec<BodyArg> }`; the walker drops slice 8j's `args.is_empty()` guard and runs `recognize_body_arg` on every arg, dropping the whole MethodCall if any arg falls outside the recognised set (same conservative skip rule as slice 8k for free-fn calls). Per-arm emission compiles the receiver via the slice-8j ABI dispatch (pointer-typed first param → pass slot_ptr; value-typed → load slot), then iterates the new `args` field with the slice-8k `IntLit` / `Slot` cases — `IntLit` emits an `i64` const, `Slot` emits `build_load(arg_slot_ty, arg_slot_ptr, "<name>.marg")` from the per-arm slot map (the `.marg` SSA suffix distinguishes method-call arg loads from free-fn `.arg` loads, easing IR-grep tests). The receiver claims call position 0; method args follow at positions 1..=N in source order. Defensive: if `slot_map[arg_field]` lookup fails for a `Slot` arg, the whole call is skipped via `arg_ok = false` continue, mirroring slice 8k's defensive bail. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `h.take(42)` lowers to `call void @Hub.take(ptr %h.slot, i64 42)`; `h.take(n)` where `n` is a captured param emits `load i64, ptr %n.slot` then `call void @Hub.take(ptr %h.slot, i64 %n.marg)`; multi-arg `h.mix(n, 7)` orders receiver + slot-load + literal as `call void @Hub.mix(ptr %h.slot, i64 %n.marg, i64 7)`; unrecognised arg `h.take(n + 1)` (binary op) silently skips the whole call. All 25 prior poll-fn / slice-8h void-call / slice-8j no-arg method / slice-8k free-fn-arg tests stay green; the slice-8j no-arg method-call shape produces `args: vec![]` and emits exactly the same single-receiver `call` as before. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (widened `MethodCall` variant + walker arg-classification + emission arg-compile loop, ~40 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: typed-aware arg lowering for both free-fn and method calls (consume `param_types` so `i32` / `bool` / `ptr` args don't silently lower to `i64`); let-bindings introducing arm-local allocas (slot map is already arm-scoped; let inside an arm registers a new entry under the binding name); control flow inside arms (`if` / `while` / `for` need per-arm CFG construction but inherit the slot map for captured-local reads inside branch bodies); user's actual final-expression value through the slice-8i terminal-arm placeholder.
  20. [x] **Slice 8m — arm-local let-bindings inside arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** First slice that adds first-class scope INSIDE per-arm emission (slices 8h-8l only handled statement-level call shapes; everything else was silently dropped). New `BodySplitStmt::Let { name, rhs: BodyArg }` variant. Walker arm: classify `StmtKind::Let { value, pattern, .. }` where `pattern.kind == PatternKind::Binding(name)` and `recognize_body_arg(value, &current_names)` returns `Some(rhs)`. Non-binding patterns (destructuring, struct patterns, etc.) and unrecognised RHS shapes are silently skipped — same conservative rule the call-classification arms established. **New `current_names: HashSet<String>` tracks visible bindings dynamically** through the walker: starts at `layout_names` (slice-4 captured-locals union), grows as let-statements introduce arm-local bindings, RESETS to `layout_names` at every yield boundary. The reset is correct because slice-8a's reload prologue reconstitutes all captured-locals at the start of every arm — but arm-local lets from prior arms aren't reflected in any reload (no state-struct field), so they must drop. `recognize_body_arg`'s signature widens from `&HashSet<&str>` to `&HashSet<String>` so the same call shape works for both static (layout-derived) and dynamic (let-extended) name sets. Per-arm emission: when `BodySplitStmt::Let { name, rhs }` is processed, alloca a fresh `i64` slot named `<name>.slot`, compute the RHS value (`IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)`; `Slot(src)` → `build_load(src_ty, src_ptr, "<src>.let_rhs")`), store the value into the slot, and `slot_map.insert(name, (i64.into(), slot))` so subsequent calls/lets in the same arm can reference the binding. **v1 type lowering: every let-binding slot is `i64`** — matches the state-struct primitive fallback, but means struct/Vec/String let-bindings can't flow through slice 8m yet (struct-literal RHS isn't in `BodyArg` recognised set, so the let is dropped; downstream method-call receivers on the would-be binding silently fall through). Cross-yield let preservation also stays deferred: a let introduced in arm 0 that's referenced in arm 1 would need state-struct write-back before the yield, which is a follow-on slice. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: terminal-arm `let x = 42; take(x);` emits `%x.slot = alloca i64`, `store i64 42, ptr %x.slot`, and `call void @take(i64 %x.arg)` in source order; identifier-RHS `let y = n;` loads `n` from its captured-local slot via `%n.let_rhs`, stores into `%y.slot`, and subsequent `take(y)` uses the new slot; struct-literal RHS (`let h = Hub { count: 0 }`) is silently dropped, and the downstream `h.helper()` also drops because `h` isn't in the slot map (regression pin for the v1 limitation); let-chains `let a = 7; let b = a; take(b);` flow through both lets, with `b.slot` carrying `a`'s loaded value. All 20 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8m is purely additive (a new BodySplitStmt variant + a new walker arm + a new emission arm), the existing FreeFnCall / MethodCall paths are unchanged. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodySplitStmt::Let` variant + `current_names: HashSet<String>` tracking + walker `Let` arm + reset-on-yield + emission `Let` arm + widened `recognize_body_arg` signature, ~80 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the next slice expansions: cross-yield let-preservation (write-back to state-struct field before the yield when the let-binding is in slice-4's capture set; the slot map + slot pointer are already arm-scoped); typed-aware let lowering (consume the typechecker's recorded binding type so non-i64 lets actually have the right LLVM slot type); struct-literal / call-result RHS shapes (extend `BodyArg` with `StructLit` / `CallResult` variants for richer RHS coverage); control flow inside arms (`if` / `while` / `for` would build per-arm CFGs but inherit the same slot map for captured-local reads inside branch bodies).
  21. [x] **Slice 8n — cross-yield captured-local writeback before each yield shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes the slice-8m correctness gap: an arm-local `let x = ...` that shadows a captured-local slot pointer in `slot_map` now actually survives across yields. Before each non-terminal arm's tag-store + Pending return, the poll-fn writes each captured-local's CURRENT slot value (which may be the slice-8a reload's original load, OR a slice-8m let-shadowed value) back into the corresponding state-struct field. Slice 8a's reload prologue in the next arm then reads the post-arm-body value rather than the stale field. **Where:** the writeback block lands inside the `if arm_idx < yield_count` branch of `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, ahead of the slice-8b tag-store. Walks `layout.fields` (the slice-4 capture set) in order; for each field with name `field.name`, looks up `slot_map[&field.name]` (which is guaranteed to be `Some(_)` because slice-8a populated it during reload prologue, but the lookup uses `let-else continue` defensively against future divergence). `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.writeback")` reads the slot; `build_struct_gep` into field `field_idx + 1` (the same "skip i32 tag at 0" offset slice 8a uses); `build_store` writes the value back. SSA names: `<name>.writeback` for the load result and `<name>.writeback_field_ptr` for the GEP — LLVM auto-suffixes for repeat writeback sites across multi-yield arms (e.g. `%n.writeback4`), so tests that count writeback sites use the named-GEP substring rather than exact SSA names. **Terminal arm intentionally skips writeback** — it returns Ready and the caller's `@free` releases the state struct immediately after; persisting state into about-to-be-freed memory would be wasted work. **For captured locals untouched inside the arm body**, the writeback loads the slice-8a reload's stored value and stores the SAME bytes back into the same field — a value-equivalent no-op that LLVM's store-after-load redundant-store elimination optimizes away. The IR overhead is minimal (3 instructions per captured local per non-terminal arm), well worth the simplification of NOT having to track which slot_map entries were modified by slice 8m. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: writeback load + GEP + store appears in state_0 with `%n.writeback` / `%n.writeback_field_ptr` and precedes the tag-store; writeback skipped in terminal arm (single yield → exactly one writeback occurrence); slice-8m let-shadowed local (`let n = 99; fetch();`) has the let-store followed by writeback that loads from the shadowed slot — the runtime value 99 lands in the state-struct field, not the original `n` param; multi-yield case (two yields → two non-terminal arms) emits exactly two writeback sites (counted via the named-GEP `writeback_field_ptr` substring divided by 2 because LLVM emits the name in both the GEP-define and the store-use lines). All 20 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8n adds IR ahead of the tag-store but doesn't remove or reorder any existing shape. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (slice-8n writeback block inside the non-terminal arm branch, ~35 lines), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the broader cross-yield correctness story: slice-8m lets that participate in slice-4's capture set (introduced before the last yield) now survive each suspension boundary; subsequent slices that mutate captured locals via `=` / `+=` / method calls will hook the same writeback path. The writeback also creates a natural integration point for the future "typed-aware lowering" slice — when a let's LLVM type stops being i64-conservative, the writeback already loads/stores via `slot_ty` from the slot map, so widening flows through with no IR-shape changes here.
  22. [x] **Slice 8o — terminal-arm final-expression value through state-struct terminal field shipped 2026-05-18.** Replaces slice 8i's `i64 0` placeholder with the user's actual final-expression value when the trailing expression on the function body block is in the recognised `BodyArg` set. Body grammar: each `Block` carries `stmts: Vec<Stmt>` plus an optional `final_expr: Option<Box<Expr>>` (the trailing-expression-without-semicolon position). The walker, after processing all statements in source order, inspects `fn_ast.body.final_expr` via `recognize_body_arg(final_expr, &current_names)` — using the TERMINAL arm's `current_names` state (post-yield-reset, plus any terminal-arm-local let bindings introduced before the final expression), so a `let r = X; r` final shape sees `r` in scope. The recognised value lands in a new walker-scoped `terminal_return: Option<BodyArg>` field; terminal-arm emission consults it before falling back to slice 8i's `i64 0`. Emission: `IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)` stored into the terminal field; `Slot(name)` → `build_load(slot_ty, slot_ptr, "<name>.return")` from `slot_map`, then `store` into the terminal field. **Slice 8m + 8n compose cleanly:** a `let r = computed_value; r` terminal pattern (slice 8m emits the let-alloca + store, slice 8n is a no-op in the terminal arm) reads the let-stored value via slot map and stores into the terminal field — the end-to-end return path works for the entire integer-let-then-return shape. **v1 scope (carried forward from slice 8k):** only integer-literal and captured-local-identifier final exprs lower; binary operations, calls, struct literals, method-call results, etc. fall back to the slice-8i `i64 0` placeholder. Wider final-expr shapes will arrive when typed-aware lowering threads expression evaluation through the body-splitting walker. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: integer-literal final `fn driver() -> i64 ... { fetch(); 42 }` emits `store i64 42, ptr %kara.return.field_ptr`; captured-local final `fn driver(n: i64) -> i64 ... { fetch(); n }` loads `%n.return = load i64, ptr %n.slot` then stores it; arm-local let final `let r = 99; r` loads `%r.return` (the slice-8m let-alloca's stored value); unrecognised final `n + 1` (binary op) falls back to `store i64 0, ptr %kara.return.field_ptr`. The four existing slice-8i tests stay green — the placeholder-fallback path is preserved verbatim for unrecognised final-expr shapes, and the existing `0`-literal test program emits `store i64 0` because `0` is now recognised as `IntLit(0)` (value-equivalent to the old placeholder). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `terminal_return: Option<BodyArg>` walker field + final-expr classification at end of walker + terminal-arm emission dispatch on `terminal_return`, ~40 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the final remaining v1 functional gap on line 26: typed-aware lowering for primitive let-bindings, args, and final-expressions (currently every i64-sized slot is i64-typed; widening to i32 / u32 / bool / f64 would require slot-type lookup against `pattern_binding_types` + per-slot LLVM-type-aware load/store/const calls — the `slot_ty` plumbing through `slot_map` and `terminal_return` is already there waiting). After typed-aware lowering, the remaining line-26 surface is control flow inside arms (if/while/for with possibly-nested yields), error-path lowering through `?` (state-struct destructor invocation), and generics-in-yielding-function support.
  23. [x] **Slice 8p — assignment statements (`name = value`) inside arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Pairs with slice 8m + 8n to make captured locals genuinely mutable across yields. New `BodySplitStmt::Assign { name, value: BodyArg }` variant. Walker arm: classify `StmtKind::Assign { target, value }` where `target.kind == ExprKind::Identifier(name)`, `current_names.contains(name)`, and `recognize_body_arg(value, &current_names)` returns `Some(body_value)`. Non-identifier targets (`obj.field = x`, `arr[i] = x`, etc.) and unrecognised RHS shapes silently drop — same conservative rule the call / let arms established. Per-arm emission: look up the binding's slot in `slot_map` (which slice 8a pre-populated for captured locals AND slice 8m extends with arm-local lets), compute the new value via the same `BodyArg`-driven dispatch as let RHS (`IntLit(v)` → `i64.const_int(v)`; `Slot(src)` → `build_load(src_ty, src_ptr, "<src>.assign_rhs")`), and `build_store` into the existing slot — does NOT alloca. The pre-existing slot is the key: the assignment's LHS already has memory backing from either slice 8a (param/captured-local-reload) or slice 8m (let-alloca), so slice 8p just overwrites the value. **Composition with slice 8n is what makes this load-bearing for cross-yield mutation:** an assignment to a captured local in a non-terminal arm leaves the new value in the slot; slice 8n's pre-yield writeback then transfers the slot's post-arm value to the state-struct field; arm K+1's reload prologue reads the updated value. Without slice 8n, the assignment would be invisible across the yield. The integration test for this — `fn driver(n: i64) with sends(Network) { n = 99; fetch(); ... }` — verifies the assignment-then-writeback sequence in IR. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: literal-to-captured assignment (`n = 99`) stores into existing `n.slot`, and slice 8n's `%n.writeback` follows in source order; captured-to-captured assignment (`b = a`) emits `%a.assign_rhs = load i64, ptr %a.slot` then `store i64 %a.assign_rhs, ptr %b.slot`; terminal-arm assignment (no following yield, no writeback) updates the slot which the slice-8o `%n.return` final-expression read then sees; field-assign target (`h.count = 7`) silently drops — non-identifier target rule. All 24 prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8p is purely additive (new BodySplitStmt variant + walker arm + emission arm), no existing path changes. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries. Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodySplitStmt::Assign` variant + walker `Assign` arm + emission `Assign` arm, ~55 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **Unblocks** the broader "mutable state across yields" story: compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=` ...) maps directly to assign-after-binop and can land in a follow-on slice once `BodyArg` widens to recognise binary expressions; field-assign / index-assign require the walker to thread receiver/index resolution, which sits alongside the future struct-literal / call-result `BodyArg` extensions; typed-aware lowering is now the most strategically valuable next slice because all four mutation paths (let-init, let-shadow, assign, writeback) currently hardcode i64 — widening to consult `pattern_binding_types` and `state_struct_layouts[fn_key].fields[i].type_name` unlocks bool / i32 / f64 / Vec / String mutation through the same slot-and-writeback machinery.
  24. [x] **Slice 8q — `BodyArg::Binary` for integer arithmetic in arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Widens the body-splitting walker's `BodyArg` set to accept arithmetic binary expressions (`+` / `-` / `*` / `/` / `%`) in any position the prior slices reached: let-RHS (slice 8m), assign-RHS (slice 8p), free-fn call args (slice 8k), method-call args (slice 8l), and terminal-arm final expression (slice 8o). Picks the simpler of slice 8p's two named follow-on directions — compound-assign mechanically lowers to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` once parser/walker threads the `+=` surface through, so this slice lays the binary-expression foundation that the compound-assign slice then composes onto. Typed-aware lowering (the other direction) stays deferred — slice 8q remains i64-conservative throughout. **Two coupled additions in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`:** (1) new `BodyArg::Binary { op: BinaryArithOp, lhs: Box<BodyArg>, rhs: Box<BodyArg> }` variant with companion `BinaryArithOp` enum (`Add` / `Sub` / `Mul` / `Div` / `Mod`); (2) new `Codegen::materialize_body_arg(arg, slot_map, name_hint) -> Option<BasicValueEnum>` helper that handles all three `BodyArg` variants in one place and is now the single materialisation point — the five emission sites (FreeFnCall args, MethodCall args, Let RHS, Assign RHS, terminal-return) collapsed from per-site `match arg` blocks into uniform `materialize_body_arg(...)` calls, deduplicating ~80 lines of repeated IntLit + Slot handling. **Recognition path matches the lowered shape, not the surface AST:** the `karac` lowering pass (`src/lowering.rs::rewrite_binary`) rewrites every primitive `Binary { Add, n, 1 }` into `Call { callee: Path { segments: ["i64", "add"] }, args: [n, 1] }` before codegen runs, so the walker matches on the two-segment-`Path`-callee Call form (segments[0] in `{i8, i16, i32, i64, u8, u16, u32, u64, usize, isize}`; segments[1] in `{add, sub, mul, div, rem}`). Comparison (`eq` / `ne` / `lt` / `le` / `gt` / `ge`), bitwise (`bitand` / `bitor` / `bitxor` / `shl` / `shr`), and float arithmetic stay outside the recognised set — `recognize_body_arg` returns `None` for those and the walker drops the whole statement, mirroring the conservative-skip rule the prior slices established. **Materialisation lowers to LLVM int arithmetic:** `BinaryArithOp::Add` → `build_int_add`; `Sub` → `build_int_sub`; `Mul` → `build_int_mul`; `Div` → `build_int_signed_div`; `Mod` → `build_int_signed_rem`. Operands recurse through `materialize_body_arg`; the helper bails (`None`) if either operand resolves to a non-`IntValue` (defensive against future `Slot` entries whose type isn't i64) so the caller skips emission rather than emitting ill-typed IR. The `name_hint` parameter — the suffix already in use by the per-site loads (`.arg` / `.marg` / `.let_rhs` / `.assign_rhs` / `.return`) — flows through unchanged: slot loads remain named `<slot>.<suffix>` (preserves existing test patterns), binary results name as `binop<suffix>`, and LLVM auto-suffixes for nested binaries (`%binop.assign_rhs1` for the outer of a nested binop). **7 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: let-RHS binary (`let m = n + 1`) emits `%n.let_rhs` load + `%binop.let_rhs = add i64 %n.let_rhs, 1` + store into `%m.slot`; assign-RHS binary (`n = n + 1`) emits `%binop.assign_rhs` and slice-8n's writeback follows in source order; call-arg binary (`helper(n + 1)`) threads `%binop.arg` into `call void @helper(i64 %binop.arg)`; terminal-return binary (`fn driver(n: i64) -> i64 { fetch(); n + 99 }`) stores `%binop.return` into `%kara.return.field_ptr`; all-five-ops sweep pins each LLVM int-arith op string (`add i64`, `sub i64`, `mul i64`, `sdiv i64`, `srem i64`); nested binary (`a = (a + b) * 2`) pins the recursive emission with the inner add and outer mul; unrecognised-binop-skips uses a comparison (`let cmp = a == b` post-yield) to confirm `==` stays unrecognised and the walker drops the let entirely. **3 prior tests updated** — `test_body_splitting_8k_skips_unrecognised_arg_shape`, `test_body_splitting_8l_skips_method_with_unrecognised_arg`, and `test_terminal_return_8o_unrecognised_final_expr_keeps_zero_fallback` originally used `n + 1` as their "unrecognised shape" example; slice 8q now recognises that shape, so the tests switched to a user-fn call shape (`ident(n)` with `fn ident(x: i64) -> i64 { x }`) which has an `ExprKind::Identifier` callee that doesn't match the `Path` recognition rule and stays outside the recognised set. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (597 codegen, all prior 590 + 7 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `BodyArg::Binary` variant + `BinaryArithOp` enum + `recognize_body_arg` Call arm + `materialize_body_arg` helper + 5 emission sites converted to call the helper, ~130 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (7 new tests + 3 updated). **Unblocks** compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=` / `/=` / `%=`) — the parser already produces `CompoundAssign { target, op, value }`; the body-splitting walker can lower it to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` and reuse slice 8p + 8q emission verbatim. Typed-aware lowering (the other slice 8p hint) remains the next strategically valuable target — all four mutation paths still hardcode i64, but `materialize_body_arg`'s defensive `IntValue`-check on `Binary` operands means the helper is already structurally ready for the widening; only the `IntLit` arm and the `slot_ty.into()` insert in the Let path need to thread the actual binding type to unlock bool / i32 / f64 / Vec / String mutation.
  25. [x] **Slice 8r — compound-assign (`+= -= *= /= %=`) in arm bodies shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes out the user-visible "mutate captured locals across yields" surface for v1 integer arithmetic. The parser already produces `StmtKind::CompoundAssign { target, op, value }` end-to-end; the body-splitting walker now desugars this in-place to `Assign { name, value: Binary { op, lhs: Slot(name), rhs: <recognised> } }` so slice 8p's Assign emission + slice 8q's Binary materialisation handle the actual codegen unchanged. No new `BodySplitStmt` variant, no new emission path, no new helper — pure walker desugaring. **Walker arm** (in `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`): a new `if let StmtKind::CompoundAssign { target, op, value }` branch immediately after the slice-8p `StmtKind::Assign` branch. Target restriction is identical to slice 8p (`ExprKind::Identifier(name)` already in `current_names`); non-identifier targets (`h.count += 1`, `arr[i] += 1`) silently drop. `CompoundOp` mapping picks up the same five arithmetic arms `BinaryArithOp` already lowers (`Add`/`Sub`/`Mul`/`Div`/`Mod`); the five bitwise / shift arms (`BitAnd`/`BitOr`/`BitXor`/`Shl`/`Shr`) return `None` and the walker drops the statement, mirroring slice 8q's "comparison / bitwise stay outside the recognised set" rule. RHS goes through `recognize_body_arg` like every other slice — IntLit / Slot / Binary recurse, anything else drops. **The lhs is always `BodyArg::Slot(name.clone())`** by construction: compound-assign's defining property is that the target is also the lhs of the binop, so the walker hands the binding's slot to the materialiser as the binary's left operand and the helper emits the slot load + int-arith op + store into the same slot. Composition with slice 8n's pre-yield writeback closes the cross-yield-mutation loop: `n += 1; fetch();` reaches the next arm's reload prologue with the post-op value, because the writeback loads the slot (now holding `n + 1`) and writes that into the state-struct field before the tag-store. **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `n += 1` desugars to `add i64 %n.assign_rhs, 1` + writeback observes the post-op value (assign_pos < writeback_pos); all-five-ops sweep pins `+= -= *= /= %=` against `add/sub/mul/sdiv/srem i64`; terminal-arm `n += 41; n` updates the slot which the slice-8o `%n.return` load then reads (no writeback because terminal); bitwise `n &= 1` silently drops (no `and i64` IR, no `%binop.assign_rhs`); field-target `h.count += 1` silently drops (non-identifier target); captured-to-captured `a += b` materialises both slot loads + an `add i64 %a.assign_rhs, %b.assign_rhs`. All prior body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8r is purely additive at the walker (new arm before the `StmtKind::Expr` fall-through), no existing code path changes. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (603 codegen, all prior 597 + 6 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new walker arm for `StmtKind::CompoundAssign`, ~35 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests). **What slice 8r does NOT cover** (intentional v1 scope boundaries, carried under future slices): bitwise / shift compound-assign (`&=` / `|=` / `^=` / `<<=` / `>>=`) — needs `BinaryArithOp` widened with the matching LLVM `build_int_and` / `or` / `xor` / `shl` / `ashr` arms and `recognize_body_arg`'s Call recognition extended for `bitand` / `bitor` / `bitxor` / `shl` / `shr` method names; field-target / index-target compound-assign (`h.count += 1`, `arr[i] += 1`) — requires the walker to thread receiver / index resolution, same shape as the field-assign / index-assign carve-out from slice 8p. **Unblocks** the typed-aware lowering slice (now the only remaining slice 8p / 8q hint not yet shipped) — all four mutation paths (let-init, let-shadow, assign, compound-assign) now share the same `Binary` materialisation surface, so widening the `IntLit` / slot type from i64 to per-binding LLVM type at one site (`materialize_body_arg`'s `IntLit` arm + `BodySplitStmt::Let`'s slot alloca + `slot_map` insert) flows through every captured-local-mutation path in one slice. After typed-aware lowering, the remaining line-26 surface is control flow inside arms (if / while / for with possibly-nested yields), error-path lowering through `?` (state-struct destructor invocation on Err), and generics-in-yielding-function support.
  26. [x] **Slice 8s — typed-aware arm-local let slot lowering shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes the latent miscompile slice 8r flagged as the "only remaining slice 8p / 8q hint not yet shipped". `BodySplitStmt::Let` emission now derives the slot alloca type from the materialised value's `BasicValueEnum::get_type()` rather than hardcoding `self.context.i64_type()`. Single-site change in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`: the `Let` arm under the per-arm body walk swaps `let i64_ty = self.context.i64_type(); build_alloca(i64_ty, …); slot_map.insert(name, (i64_ty.into(), slot))` for `let slot_ty = value.get_type(); build_alloca(slot_ty, …); slot_map.insert(name, (slot_ty, slot))`. Captured-local slots (slice 8a reload prologue) are unaffected — they already thread their state-struct field type from slice 5's typed `llvm_type_for_name` emission, so `let v = items;` with `items: Vec[i64]` reads the inline `{ ptr, i64, i64 }` shape correctly, and slice 8s now lands the matching width into the destination slot. **The latent bug being fixed:** prior to slice 8s, `let v = items;` (with `items` a captured `Vec[i64]`) would `alloca i64` for `v.slot` (8 bytes) and `store { ptr, i64, i64 }` (24 bytes of Vec data) — opaque pointers let LLVM IR accept this without a verifier error, but the result was a stack-smashing miscompile that overwrote 16 bytes past the alloca's intended footprint. Subsequent `let w = v;` reads compounded the corruption (slot_map["v"] said i64, so `build_load(i64, v.slot)` read 8 bytes of the half-overwritten Vec data as if it were an int). The reload-prologue test (`test_poll_fn_reload_prologue_multi_field_layout`) used exactly this `let b: Vec[i64] = a;` shape and passed because it only counted reload-GEPs, not let-emission IR — slice 8s makes the let-emission soundness explicit at the test layer. **Why value-driven is the right primitive (vs. consulting `pattern_binding_types`):** the materialised value's LLVM type is always exactly the width that gets stored, so the alloca-store pair is type-coherent by construction. `pattern_binding_types` records `Some("Vec")` / `Some("Hub")` / `None` (None for unrecorded primitives — i64/i32/bool/f64), so threading it would still need a fallback for the None case, and the fallback would need to consult the RHS value type anyway. The value-driven approach skips the indirection. **What slice 8s does NOT widen:** the `materialize_body_arg::IntLit` arm stays `i64` (integer literals default to i64 in Kara, which is what the type system assumes for unannotated int contexts); the `BodySplitStmt::Assign` arm still uses the pre-existing `slot_ty` from `slot_map` (captured or arm-local — the slot's width was set correctly by either slice 8a or slice 8s, so no further coercion is needed). **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `let v = items` with Vec captured local alloca's `{ ptr, i64, i64 }` (not i64) + the `.let_rhs` load + store both Vec-typed; same shape for `let s = name` with String captured local; `let r = h` with shared-struct captured local alloca's `ptr` (single-word handle); regression guards — `let x = 42` still alloca's i64 (IntLit is i64-typed), `let m = n + 1` still alloca's i64 (Binary result is i64-typed); chained `let v = items; let w = v;` propagates the Vec type through both slots — `v.slot` and `w.slot` are both `{ ptr, i64, i64 }`, and the chained `.let_rhs` load reads Vec width from `v.slot`. All prior 41 body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8s is a one-site type widening that affects no IR shape integer-typed lets already produced. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (609 codegen, all prior 603 + 6 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (~5 lines net — single-site change in the `Let` emission arm), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests). **What slice 8s does NOT cover** (deferred to future slices): bool / f64 / i32 width-precise IntLit lowering (today's literals stay i64; mismatched-width assignment paths like `n = 0` where n is bool are out of scope because `pattern_binding_types` doesn't record bool / int-narrowing and the layout's captured-local-field stays i64-widened); MethodCall return as `BodyArg` (would let `let s = name.clone()` work); StructLit as `BodyArg` (would let `let h = Hub { count: 0 }` work — currently silently dropped, see `test_body_splitting_8m_let_then_method_call_on_local`). **Unblocks** the remaining line-26 surface — typed-aware lowering is now closed, so the next strategic slice is one of: control flow inside arms (`if` / `while` / `for` with possibly-nested yields — requires the walker to handle nested blocks and the codegen to thread arm IDs across control-flow boundaries); error-path lowering through `?` (state-struct destructor invocation on Err — requires Drop-on-state-struct emission and Pending vs Err discriminant routing); generics-in-yielding-function support (per-monomorphization state-struct + poll-fn emission, currently the slice 4 walker handles concrete types only).
  27. [x] **Slice 8t — control-flow-aware `cur_arm` advancement in the body-splitting walker shipped 2026-05-18.** Closes the "post-CF stmts land in the wrong arm" half of the CF-inside-arms story (the half that doesn't need IR-shape changes). Walker change only — no codegen change. **Problem:** today's body-splitting walker (`emit_state_machine_poll_fns` in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`) iterates flat-block statements and advances `cur_arm` only when a top-level `StmtKind::Expr(Call/MethodCall)`'s span exactly matches `yield_points[cur_arm].span`. A stmt like `if cond { fetch(); }` has the `if`-expression span as its top-level — fetch's span is *inside* but doesn't equal it — so the walker drops the if-stmt silently and `cur_arm` doesn't advance. Any *post-CF* statement in the function body then incorrectly lands in `per_arm_stmts[0]` (the entry arm) instead of `per_arm_stmts[1]` (the post-yield arm). State_0 emits the post-CF call before its state-transition + Pending; state_1 is empty. **Fix:** a span-containment count helper `count_yields_inside_span(stmt_span, yield_points, start_idx)` returns how many `yield_points` starting from `start_idx` have spans contained in `stmt_span`. Slice 2's `YieldPointWalker` records yields in source order, so once a yield's offset is past the stmt's end the `take_while` short-circuits. The walker invokes the helper after each of the four stmt-kind processing branches (`Let`, `Assign`, `CompoundAssign`, the `Expr` arm's `_ => {}` fall-through) and advances `cur_arm` by the returned count, also resetting `current_names` to `layout_names` once per advance to match the top-level yield-match's arm-boundary discipline. **What slice 8t does NOT change:** the CF expression itself is still dropped from the IR — `if cond { fetch(); }` produces the same state-transition + Pending that today's silent-drop produces, regardless of `cond`'s runtime value (the function still suspends-then-resumes unconditionally). A follow-on slice rebuilds the CF in IR via branching codegen that routes between state-machine arm blocks at yield points. **What slice 8t covers vs. doesn't:** the descent fires for stmt-position CF (`if` / `while` / `for` / `match` / `loop` / labeled-block / etc. as the top-level expr of a `StmtKind::Expr`) and for yields nested in `Let` / `Assign` / `CompoundAssign` RHS expressions; it does NOT fire for yields nested in non-yield top-level Call/MethodCall args (e.g. `outer(fetch())`) because those paths take the enqueue arms — a future slice can extend the descent into argument expressions if the pattern arises in practice. **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs`: `if cond { fetch(); } take(42);` puts take in state_1 (verified by IR-position: take's offset > state_0's transition store); same shape for `while` / `for` / `match`; multi-yield-multi-CF (`if a { fetch(); } if b { fetch(); } take(99);` → take in state_2, both state_0 and state_1 emit transitions); nested CF (`if a { if b { fetch(); } } take(5);` → descent recurses, take in state_1). All prior 47 body-splitting tests stay green — slice 8t is purely additive to the walker; the helper is a free function near `recognize_body_arg`. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (615 codegen, all prior 609 + 6 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `count_yields_inside_span` helper + 4 descent call sites, ~50 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests). **Unblocks** the CF-preservation slice — `cur_arm` is now correctly advanced for nested yields, so the conditional-emission slice can focus solely on the IR-shape change (branch on cond into state-transition-bb vs no-yield-bb) without worrying about arm classification. **Test coverage from the line-26 spec:** yield-inside-loop, yield-inside-conditional (both shipped — the post-CF stmt classification is correct; the CF's runtime semantics still need the follow-on slice).
  28. [x] **Slice 8u — state-struct destructor primitive (unified unwind for `?`-Err-propagation and cooperative-cancel) shipped 2026-05-19.** Lands the per-state-struct destructor function — the load-bearing primitive both the future `?`-Err-propagation use site (post-yield arm Err-route) and the cooperative-cancel use site (`*cancel == true` check at arm boundaries) invoke — *without* yet wiring either use site. Picks shape (a) from the spec hint: a single `define internal void @__kara_state_drop_<fn_key>(ptr %state)` per heap-bearing state-struct, rather than (b)'s inline-drop-sequence-per-Err-arm (which would duplicate the captured-local field walk at every future `?` and every per-arm cancel-check). The single-fn shape also matches the slice 6 design audit's "state-struct destructor invocation through `?`" framing and gives a stable callable for a future user-Drop hook on state-structs. **Use-site recognition deferred** — slice 8u v1 lands the primitive and stops there because (i) the `?`-operator recognition in the body-splitting walker requires the yield-call result-slot mechanism (which would let the post-yield arm read the resumed call's `Result` tag and branch on Err) — that slot doesn't exist yet, so emitting a vapor "is-this-yield-erred" check would be promise-not-reality; (ii) the cooperative-cancel use site requires threading the `cancel: ptr` poll-fn parameter into a per-arm prologue load + branch, which is its own slice-shaped change. Both follow-ons consume *this* destructor unchanged. **Per-state-struct destructor body shape.** For each entry in `state_struct_layouts` whose captured-local field set has at least one heap-bearing field, codegen emits a single function: load the state-ptr from `param 0`; walk `layout.fields` in source-introduction order; for each field, dispatch on its recorded `type_name` to one of three emission arms: (i) `Vec` / `String` / `VecDeque` / `str` → the `cap > 0 ? free(data)` pattern — GEP into the state-struct field at offset `field_idx + 1` (tag at 0), GEP into the field's Vec struct field 2 (cap), load i64, `icmp ugt 0`, conditional branch to a `<name>.drop.free` BB that GEPs field 0 (data ptr), loads it, calls `free(data)`, and falls through to a `<name>.drop.skip` continuation BB. IR shape is bit-identical to `emit_struct_drop_synthesis`'s `FieldDrop::VecOrString` arm and `CleanupAction::FreeVecBuffer`'s scope-cleanup emission, so optimizer recognition / coverage parity holds across all three drop surfaces. (ii) Shared-struct field (the field's `type_name` resolves through `shared_types`) → load the heap handle as `ptr`, null-guard via `icmp eq ptr %handle, null` (slice-8a's reload-over-uninitialized-state-struct-fields concern means the destructor may be invoked when not all fields have meaningful values yet — the null guard prevents a dec-on-null trap before the runtime err-signal plumbing lands), then dispatch through `emit_refcount_dec` so the recursive drop chain (`rc_drop_fns`) fires on transitively-owned shared refs the same way ordinary scope-exit cleanup does. (iii) Any other field (`Option[shared T]`, value-type struct with heap fields, enum with heap payload, `Map[K, V]` / `Set[T]`, primitives, unrecorded `None` type_name) → silently skipped at v1, mirroring the body-splitting walker's conservative coverage rule. Field positions still GEP'd in strict source order so a future slice extending the recognized set drops in additional emission arms without re-ordering anything. Body terminates with `ret void`. **Caller-allocates / caller-frees discipline.** The state struct's own heap allocation is the *caller's* responsibility to `free` after invoking the destructor — matches the constructor's discipline (slice 8c). The runtime's parked-task release path already has the state pointer at hand and pairs the destructor call with the `free` in one place, rather than baking the free into every destructor body and forcing the caller to remember not to free again. Test pins the absence of `call void @free(ptr %state)` from the destructor body. **Skip-when-empty rule.** When every captured-local field classifies as `Skip`, slice 8u emits *no* destructor at all — the function would be an `entry: ret void` body that IR consumers would treat as dead code, and the sparse `state_machine_state_destructors` map gives the future use sites a fast "is there cleanup to do?" predicate without calling an empty function. Test pins this for both the primitive-only-captures shape and the pure-function-no-state-struct shape. **Cross-coordination with phase-7 line 67 slice 1a (Result-slot ABI + Err-triggers-cancel, on main).** Slice 1a established the par-block Result-slot write convention and the cancel-atomic flip on Err for sibling-task cooperative cancellation. The future use sites of slice 8u's destructor align with that ABI: when a yielding-fn's `?`-propagation use site lands, the post-yield arm reads the resumed call's Result tag from a state-struct Result slot (extending the slice-1a Result-slot concept to yielding-fn calls), branches on Err, invokes the destructor, writes the Err value into the state-struct terminal-result field, and returns `i8 2` (`KaracPollResult::Err` per `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`'s `assert_eq!(KaracPollResult::Err as u8, 2)` — the original slice 8u spec text said `i8 1`, which is `KaracPollResult::Ready`; the runtime's actual disc value is `2`, mirrored across both the par-task and network-yield-task "task returned Err" branches of the dispatcher). **Implementation discipline.** `emit_state_machine_state_destructors` runs immediately after `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` (line 1736 of `src/codegen.rs`) so all three state-machine helpers (poll-fn, constructor, destructor) land in one orchestration block. Independent of user-function declarations — only consults `state_struct_layouts`, `state_struct_types`, `shared_types`, and the runtime intrinsic `free_fn` / RC helpers. Save / restore of `self.current_fn` (needed by `emit_refcount_dec`'s `current_fn.unwrap()`) mirrors `emit_struct_drop_synthesis`'s discipline so the outer caller's builder state stays untouched. **7 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under the new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8u: state-struct destructor helper` section: destructor emitted with correct `void @__kara_state_drop_driver(ptr ...)` signature for a `Vec[i64]` captured-local; `cap > 0 ? free` pattern emits the canonical IR (cap load, ugt-0 compare, free-branch with data load + `call void @free`); shared-struct captured-local emits handle load + null-guard + `emit_rc_dec`'s `%rc_dec = sub i64 %rc, 1` shape; primitive-only captures emit no destructor (skip-when-empty); pure functions emit no destructor (no state-struct entry); multi-field heap captures walk in source order (`%items.drop.*` precedes `%name.drop.*` for `(items: Vec, name: String)`); destructor terminator is `ret void` and never frees the state ptr (caller-frees discipline). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 636, all prior 629 + 7 new). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `state_machine_state_destructors` field + initializer + emission-call wire-up, ~25 lines net), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `emit_state_machine_state_destructors` method, ~210 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (7 new tests). **What slice 8u does NOT cover** (carried explicitly as named follow-on slices): (1) `?`-operator recognition in the body-splitting walker (requires the yield-call result-slot mechanism — store the resumed call's Result into a state-struct field, post-yield arm reads the tag, branches on Err to a per-arm `err_unwind` BB that invokes the destructor + writes Err to the terminal-result field + returns `i8 2`); (2) cooperative-cancel per-arm prologue check (load the `cancel: ptr` poll-fn param's `AtomicBool`, branch on `*cancel == true` to the same `err_unwind` BB shape); (3) `Option[shared T]` / value-type-struct-with-heap-fields / enum-with-heap-payload / `Map`/`Set` captured-local field destructor arms (today's `FieldDrop::Skip` cases — each adds an emission arm to `emit_state_machine_state_destructors` parallel to the existing Vec / Shared arms once the relevant type-info pathways are threaded); (4) reverse-construction-order field walk (today's destructor walks source-introduction order — matches `pattern_binding_types` recording order, which is what the v1 spec audit hint phrased; a future user-Drop hook may want strict-reverse-order for symmetric construction/destruction, at which point the iteration flips to `.rev()` and the multi-field source-order test updates to multi-field reverse-order). **Test coverage from the line-26 spec:** error-path through yield — destructor primitive shipped; use-site recognition follows.
  29. [x] **Slice 8v — generics-in-yielding-function support (per-monomorphization state-struct + poll-fn emission).** Probe (2026-05-19) revealed the original spec's claim "doesn't get its state struct + poll-fn emitted" was almost right — the analysis-side tables DO record polymorphic yielding fns under their base name (build_state_struct_layouts at `src/cli.rs:1367` iterates `program.items` without filtering on `generic_params.is_some()`, and `callee_network_yield_effect` conservatively flags `DeclaredEffects::Polymorphic` / `PolymorphicWithFixed` as network-yield candidates at `src/cli.rs:903`), so slices 5 / 6 / 8c / 8u WERE emitting state-struct LLVM types / poll-fns / constructors / destructors under the polymorphic base name (`%kara.state.driver`, `__kara_poll_driver`, etc.) — but with the WRONG field types (`llvm_type_for_name("T")` falls through to the i64 default when no `type_subst` is active, so a `T`-typed captured local lowered to i64 regardless of whether the eventual monomorphization is `i64` or `Vec[i64]` or `String`). The dead-IR was unreachable in any case because `compile_call`'s generic-dispatch arm (`src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:193`) short-circuits through `compile_generic_call` BEFORE reaching the slice-8d state-machine intercept at line 230 — so every call site emitted `call void @"driver$<mono>"(args)` direct, bypassing the polymorphic-keyed helpers entirely. Slice 8v Phase 1 ships the **dead-IR cleanup** (skip generics from all four base-name emission passes) shipped 2026-05-19; Phase 2 ships **per-mono emission + caller-side intercept routing** as a follow-on slice once the four emit fns are refactored into per-key helpers callable from `compile_generic_call`. **Slice 8v Phase 1 — base-name dead-IR cleanup shipped 2026-05-19.** Adds `is_generic_fn_key(program, fn_key) -> bool` next to `find_function_ast` in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` — returns `true` when the AST node has `generic_params.is_some()` (free fns or impl methods; same key-shape resolution as `find_function_ast`, so `"Hub.run"` resolves to the impl method's generic-params check). Each of the four base-name iteration passes (`emit_state_struct_types`, `emit_state_machine_poll_fns`, `emit_state_machine_state_constructors`, `emit_state_machine_state_destructors`) now skips entries where `is_generic_fn_key(program, fn_key) == true` before any LLVM type lookup / emission work. Effect: zero IR change for non-generic fns; for polymorphic yielding fns, the previously-emitted-and-unreachable `%kara.state.<base>`, `__kara_state_type_anchor_<base>`, `__kara_poll_<base>`, `__kara_state_new_<base>`, `__kara_state_drop_<base>` all disappear from the module. **What Phase 1 does NOT do** (carried into Phase 2): per-mono emission of the four helpers at the mangled key (e.g., `%kara.state.driver$i64`, `__kara_poll_driver$i64`, etc.); per-mono caller-side intercept routing in `compile_generic_call` (today the call site still emits direct `call @<mangled>(args)` which is semantically wrong for a network-yielding fn — it skips the parking/scheduling machinery — but it's the same wrongness that existed pre-Phase-1; Phase 1 doesn't worsen the user-visible behavior, only removes the dead helpers that misleadingly suggested support existed). **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8v Phase 1: skip generics from base-name emission` section: polymorphic free fn `driver[T]` produces no `%kara.state.driver` type and no `__kara_state_type_anchor_driver` anchor; no `__kara_poll_driver` poll-fn; no `__kara_state_new_driver` constructor; no `__kara_state_drop_driver` destructor even when the captured-local's `type_name` would classify as heap-bearing (`Vec[T]`); non-generic concrete fn `caller()` still emits its state struct / poll-fn / constructor (sanity guard — the filter is generic-only, not blanket-skip); polymorphic impl method `Hub.run[T]` on a non-generic impl block also skips emission (`is_generic_fn_key` resolves `"Hub.run"` to the method AST correctly). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 636 → 642 — the 6 new Phase 1 tests). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (new `is_generic_fn_key` helper + 4 skip-checks at the top of each base-name iteration loop, ~35 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests). **Phase 2 follow-on plan** (separate future slice once the refactor lands): (a) extract per-key emission helpers from each of the four base-name passes — `emit_state_struct_type_for_key(ast_key, emit_key, layout)`, `emit_state_machine_state_constructor_for_key(emit_key, state_struct)`, `emit_state_machine_state_destructor_for_key(ast_key, emit_key, layout)`, `emit_state_machine_poll_fn_for_key(ast_key, emit_key, layout)` — so both the base-name iteration and the per-mono path share one emission source; (b) hook a per-mono orchestrator into `compile_generic_call` immediately after `declare_mono_function` so each new mono gets its four helpers emitted under the mangled key, with `type_subst` active so `llvm_type_for_name("T")` resolves correctly to the per-mono field types; (c) replace the direct `call @<mangled>(args)` at the end of `compile_generic_call` with a state-machine intercept (state_new + arg-store + poll-loop + state_drop + free) gated on `state_machine_state_constructors.contains_key(mangled)` — mirrors the slice 8d shape inline. Scope option from the original spec stands: confine v1 to the trivially-monomorphic case (polymorphic source has no `with` clause that mentions an effect parameter — all monos share the same concrete effect set); defer the per-mono resolved-effect-set case (where a `Polymorphic` declared effect resolves to network-yield at one mono and non-network at another) to a later slice that threads the resolved-per-mono effect set through `callee_network_yield_effect`. **Slice 8v Phase 2 — per-mono state-machine emission + caller-side intercept routing shipped 2026-05-19.** Lands the three-step refactor + wire-up Phase 1 had named as a follow-on. **Step (a) — per-key emission helpers extracted from all four base-name passes.** Each of `emit_state_struct_types` / `emit_state_machine_poll_fns` / `emit_state_machine_state_constructors` / `emit_state_machine_state_destructors` becomes a thin iterator that filters generics via `is_generic_fn_key` and calls a per-key helper: `emit_state_struct_type_for_key(program, ast_key, emit_key, layout)`, `emit_state_machine_state_constructor_for_key(emit_key)`, `emit_state_machine_state_destructor_for_key(emit_key, layout)`, `emit_state_machine_poll_fn_for_key(program, ast_key, emit_key)`. The two-key signature (`ast_key` for layout / yield-points / AST lookups vs. `emit_key` for LLVM symbol names + map insertions) is what enables a single per-mono call to emit under the mangled key while consulting the polymorphic base's AST. Inside each helper, all references to the iteration variable `fn_key` got mechanically rewritten to either `ast_key` or `emit_key` based on which lookup-vs-emission discipline applies (layout reads via `ast_key`, LLVM symbol names + map keys via `emit_key`, `state_machine_return_types.contains_key` switched to `emit_key` so the slice-8i terminal-field shape per-mono'es correctly). The refactor is zero-IR-change for non-generic fns — verified by the full 648-test codegen suite passing unchanged after the extraction. **Step (b) — per-mono orchestrator + `compile_generic_call` hook.** New `emit_state_machine_helpers_for_mono(&mut self, base_key, mono_key)` method in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` runs all four per-key helpers with the polymorphic base as `ast_key` and the mangled name as `emit_key`. Idempotent (early-return if `state_machine_poll_fns[mono_key]` is already populated). No-op when `base_key` isn't in `state_struct_layouts` (non-yielding generic fn — the common case; one HashMap lookup is the entire cost). Hooked into `compile_generic_call` (`src/codegen/mono.rs`) immediately after `compile_mono_function` and BEFORE the `type_subst` restore steps — so `llvm_type_for_name("T")` inside the helpers resolves to the per-mono concrete LLVM type. Accessing the polymorphic source's `state_struct_layouts` / `yield_points` / AST without threading `&Program` through `compile_expr` → `compile_call` → `compile_generic_call` required a new `Codegen.program_snapshot: Option<Rc<Program>>` field: one full `Program` clone at the top of `compile_program` (under an `Rc`), cheap reference-bumping clones to per-mono callers as they fire. Wrapping in `Rc` sidesteps the `&self` (snapshot read) vs. `&mut self` (per-key emission) borrow conflict that a bare `Option<Program>` would create. **Step (c) — per-mono caller-side intercept.** In `compile_generic_call`, the final `call @<mangled>(args)` emit is now gated: when `state_machine_state_constructors.contains_key(&mangled)` (the per-mono helpers were emitted in step b), the direct call is replaced with the slice-8d-shaped state-machine invocation, keyed on the mangled name: `state = __kara_state_new_<mangled>()` + arg-store-into-captured-local-fields + `kara.poll_loop` BB with `__kara_poll_<mangled>(ptr %state, ptr null)` + Pending-branch-to-`kara.poll_yield` + `sched_yield()` + back to loop + done-branch loads the terminal field (when `state_machine_return_types[mangled]` is `Some`) + `free(state)`. Non-yielding generic calls (the common case) fall through to the unchanged direct-call path. **Generic-typed param resolution fix.** During Phase 2 implementation, a probe revealed the typechecker's `pattern_binding_types` recorder emits `type_name: None` for type-parameter-typed parameters (e.g. `item: T`'s pattern binding has no surface name recorded). The existing per-key state-struct-type emission then fell back to `i64` for those fields — wrong for any non-i64-shaped mono. Fix: when `field.type_name == None`, the per-key emission now consults a new free function `lookup_param_type_expr(fn_ast, field_name) -> Option<TypeExpr>` that walks `fn_ast.params` matching pattern-binding names, and threads the parameter's `TypeExpr` through `llvm_type_for_type_expr` (which honors `type_subst`). For a polymorphic `fn driver[T](item: T)` instantiated with `T = i32`, the i32 mono's state struct now correctly lowers to `{ i32, i32 }` instead of the i64-fallback `{ i32, i64 }`. The fallback path stays for arm-local let-bindings of generic type (no parameter lookup hits) — a follow-on slice can extend the lookup to walk the body's let-bindings; for v1 the parameter-only path covers the dominant generic-yielding-fn shape. **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8v Phase 2: per-mono state-machine emission + caller intercept` section: per-mono state-struct type emitted with the concrete field type (`%"kara.state.driver$i64" = type { i32, i64 }` for `T = i64`); per-mono poll-fn + constructor emitted at mangled keys (`@"__kara_poll_driver$i64"` / `@"__kara_state_new_driver$i64"`) + per-mono destructor correctly skipped for primitive-only captures; per-mono caller intercept routes through state-machine (no `call void @"driver$i64"(args)` direct-call survives, `kara.poll_loop` block + `call ptr @"__kara_state_new_driver$i64"()` + `call i8 @"__kara_poll_driver$i64"(ptr %kara.state, ptr null)` + `call void @free(ptr %kara.state)` all present); arg-into-state-struct-field threading emits the canonical `%kara.arg0.field_ptr` GEP + `store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr`; two distinct monos of the same polymorphic fn (i64 + i32) each get their own state-struct + poll-fn + constructor with the right per-mono concrete field types (`{ i32, i64 }` vs. `{ i32, i32 }`); non-yielding generic fn (`fn identity[T](x: T) -> T { x }`) skips per-mono emission entirely and falls through to the direct-call path (sanity guard — the orchestrator's gating predicate must miss for non-yielding generics, otherwise we'd pay state-machine cost on every generic call). Phase 1's 6 tests still pass after substring-match tightening (the previously-loose checks like `@__kara_state_new_driver` would now also catch `@"__kara_state_new_driver$i64"`; tightened to `@__kara_state_new_driver(` so per-mono variants don't trip the base-name filter). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 642 → 654 across both Phase 1 and Phase 2 additions). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (new `program_snapshot: Option<Rc<Program>>` field + initializer + populator at top of `compile_program`, ~25 lines net), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (per-key helper refactor of all four base-name passes + `emit_state_machine_helpers_for_mono` orchestrator + `lookup_param_type_expr` helper + None-fallback param-type lookup in the state-struct type emission, ~150 lines net), `src/codegen/mono.rs` (orchestrator hook + per-mono caller-side intercept replacing the direct call, ~120 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new Phase 2 tests + Phase 1 substring-match tightening). **What Phase 2 does NOT cover** (carried as named follow-on slices): (1) destructor-emitting per-mono case (e.g. `fn driver[T](items: Vec[T])` with `T = i64`) — the `Vec[T]` parameter's `type_name` is recorded as `Some("Vec")` regardless of `T`, so `FieldDrop::VecOrString` classification works; but the broader case where `T` itself is a heap-bearing type (e.g. `fn driver[T](item: T)` with `T = String`) needs the destructor classification to look up the parameter's TypeExpr through `type_subst` to determine heap-bearingness — today's classification only inspects `field.type_name` directly. (2) Generic-typed arm-local let-bindings (`fn driver[T](item: T) { fetch(); let copy = item; }`) — the parameter-only `lookup_param_type_expr` doesn't reach these; a body-walk extension is the natural next step. (3) Polymorphic-effect monomorphizations (where `with` clause mentions an effect parameter and different monos resolve to different effect sets — `network-yield` at one mono, `non-yield` at another) — `callee_network_yield_effect` conservatively flags `Polymorphic` candidates as network-yield, so the per-mono path always fires its state-machine emission even for monos that resolve to non-network; a stricter slice would consult the resolved-per-mono effect set to gate the orchestrator. (4) Args-pass-by-ref for per-mono intercepts — the intercept currently mirrors slice 8d's `fn_param_ref` / `fn_param_slice_elem` handling implicitly (the direct-call path passes through arg lowering correctly for non-yielding generics; the state-machine intercept stores the compiled `arg_vals[i]` LLVM value directly into the state-struct field, matching slice 8f's discipline — but ref / slice-elem param shapes haven't been exercised by tests yet, so this is "untested" rather than "broken"). **Test coverage from the line-26 spec:** generics-in-yielding-function — both Phase 1's cleanup boundary AND Phase 2's per-mono emission + intercept routing verified end-to-end through 12 tests across both sections; the polymorphic source `fn driver[T](item: T) { fetch(); }` now goes from "dead-and-broken base-name IR" (pre-slice-8v) to "no per-mono helpers but no dead IR either" (Phase 1) to "per-mono helpers correctly emitted, caller routes through state machine" (Phase 2) — the actual functional shape that lets generic yielding fns compose with the slice-1a Result-slot ABI and the future scheduler-yield wiring. Four named follow-on slices (8w / 8x / 8y / 8z below) extend the per-mono path to the heap-bearing-`T`, body-let, polymorphic-effect, and ref-param surfaces respectively — each carries an independent scope so they sequence cleanly.

[x] **Slice 8w — destructor classification via `type_subst` for `T`-typed captured locals (Vec-shape scope) shipped 2026-05-19.** Closes the cancel-leak path slice 8v Phase 2 surfaced: with the per-mono state-machine helpers now emitted for polymorphic yielding fns, a heap-bearing mono like `fn driver[T](item: T)` instantiated with `T = String` was still skipping the destructor — the classification arm in `emit_state_machine_state_destructor_for_key` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs`) inspected `field.type_name` directly, which the typechecker records as `None` for type-parameter-typed bindings. The mono's destructor stayed absent (silently via slice 8u's skip-when-empty rule), leaving the captured `item: String`'s heap buffer un-freed when the runtime parks-then-cancels a `driver$String` task before the user's binding goes out of scope. **Fix:** the per-key destructor helper now takes `program + ast_key` (matching the state-struct-type and poll-fn helpers' signatures), so when `field.type_name == None` it can route through `lookup_param_type_expr(fn_ast, field_name)` (introduced by slice 8v Phase 2 for the layout side), resolve the parameter's declared `TypeExpr` against the active `type_subst` via `llvm_type_for_type_expr`, and classify the resulting LLVM type. The Vec-struct identity check uses the existing `llvm_ty_is_vec_struct(ty)` helper — context-uniqued struct equality against `vec_struct_type()`. **Three shapes** classify as `FieldDrop::VecOrString` after the fix: `T = String` (lowered to `vec_struct_type`), `T = Vec[U]`, `T = VecDeque[U]`. All emit the canonical `cap > 0 ? free(data)` pattern under the mangled destructor key. **What 8w does NOT cover (carried as a named follow-on):** shared-`T` (e.g. `T = SharedNode` where `SharedNode` is a `shared struct`) — `infer_type_args` binds `T → ptr_type` when the arg is a shared-struct handle, losing the surface name needed to recover `shared_types[N].heap_type` for `emit_refcount_dec`'s reverse-lookup. The destructor classification falls through to `Skip` for shared-`T`, matching v1 conservatism. Recovering the surface name needs a parallel name-tracking table in `infer_type_args` / `unify_type_expr` — deferred as a follow-on. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8w: destructor classification via type_subst` section: `fn driver[T](item: T)` with `T = String` emits `@"__kara_state_drop_driver$struct"` with the `cap > 0 ? free` IR shape (`%item.drop.cap = load i64`, `%item.drop.is_heap = icmp ugt i64 %item.drop.cap, 0`, `call void @free(ptr %item.drop.data)`); same fn with `T = i64` emits no destructor (skip-when-empty regression guard); both `T = i64` and `T = String` instantiated in the same caller body emit asymmetrically — only the String mono gets a destructor; non-generic `fn driver(items: Vec[i64])` still classifies via the existing `Some("Vec")` arm and emits unchanged (regression guard — the None-fallback path doesn't fire for recorded `type_name`s). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 654 → 658). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (destructor helper signature extended with `program: &Program` + `ast_key: &str` + reuses `lookup_param_type_expr`; the orchestrator caller in `emit_state_machine_helpers_for_mono` passes through; the base-name pass passes `fn_key` for both keys, ~30 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests).
