[x] **Slice 8x — body-walk for generic-typed arm-local let-bindings shipped 2026-05-20.** Closes the cancel-leak path slice 8w left open for arm-local lets: `lookup_param_type_expr` only walks `fn_ast.params`, so a `let copy = item;` inside a `T`-typed yielding fn body whose binding is captured across a later yield landed at i64 in the per-mono state struct (and `Skip` in the per-mono destructor) when `T` is non-i64. Two adjacent problems, one fix surface. **(1) Unannotated let — `let copy = item;`.** The typechecker's `pattern_binding_types` recorder emits no entry for type-parameter-typed bindings whose RHS is another type-parameter-typed identifier (`Type::TypeParam` doesn't match any of the three `Type::Named` / `Type::Str` / `Type::Shared` insertion arms in `bind_pattern_types`), so the `copy` field's `type_name` is `None`. Both the state-struct emission's None-fallback (slice 8v Phase 2) and the destructor classifier's None-fallback (slice 8w) needed extending. **(2) Annotated let — `let copy: T = item;`.** The typechecker's `items.rs` Let arm calls `lower_type_expr(ty_expr, &[])` with an EMPTY generic scope, so the annotation `T` lowers as `Type::Named { name: "T" }` rather than `Type::TypeParam`. `bind_pattern_types`'s `Type::Named` arm then DOES insert into `pattern_binding_types`, recording `"T"` against the `copy` field. The state-struct emission's `Some(name)` arm correctly resolves this via `llvm_type_for_name("T")` (which already honors the active `type_subst` from slice 8v Phase 2's per-mono dispatch), so the layout side was already right — but the destructor's `Some(name)` shape-bucket arms (Vec/VecDeque/String/str/shared) miss the bare `"T"` string and fall through to `_ => Skip`, leaving the field undropped. **The fix lands in three coordinated edits in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`:** (a) new `lookup_let_type_expr(fn_ast, field_name) -> Option<TypeExpr>` helper (plus three private `find_let_binding_in_block` / `_in_stmt` / `_in_expr` walkers) that recursively descends `fn_ast.body` — into block-bearing exprs (`if` / `if let` / `while` / `while let` / `for` / `loop` / `match` arm bodies / bare blocks) and through `defer` / `errdefer` / `assign` / `compound-assign` RHS — for the first `Let` / `LetElse` / `LetUninit` binding whose pattern binds the requested name. Returns the explicit type annotation when present; for unannotated lets with a bare-identifier RHS, recurses through `lookup_param_type_expr` first (params take priority) then itself (chained `let a = item; let b = a;` resolves through `a`'s let then to `item`'s param). Other RHS shapes (calls, method calls, struct literals, literals) return `None` and the caller falls through to the i64 default, matching the conservative None-fallback rule established by slice 8v Phase 2 / 8w. (b) `emit_state_struct_type_for_key`'s None-fallback chain extends from `lookup_param_type_expr` → i64 to `lookup_param_type_expr` → `lookup_let_type_expr` → i64, so unannotated `let copy = item;` lowers `copy` to the resolved-T LLVM type per mono. (c) `emit_state_machine_state_destructor_for_key`'s classifier gets two extensions: its existing None arm picks up the same `or_else(|| lookup_let_type_expr(...))` so the unannotated-let surface classifies via the recovered `TypeExpr`; a new `Some(name)` catchall arm (placed after the existing `Some("Vec")` / shared-types arms) resolves the recorded name through `llvm_type_for_name` (the same path the state-struct emission already uses, which honors `type_subst`) and runs the Vec-struct identity check — so annotated `let copy: T = item;` with `T = String` classifies as `VecOrString`. Non-Vec-shaped resolutions (primitives, pointers, etc.) stay `Skip`. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8x: body-walk for generic-typed let-bindings` section: per-mono state struct for `fn driver[T](item: T) { fetch(); let copy = item; fetch(); }` with `T = Vec[i64]` carries two `{ ptr, i64, i64 }` fields (occurrence count >= 2 on the type-def line); same source's per-mono destructor emits `cap > 0 ? free` for both `item` and `copy` fields with `%item.drop.cap` preceding `%copy.drop.cap` in IR text (strict source-introduction order); explicit `let copy: T = item;` with `T = String` produces `%copy.drop.cap` + free shape via the new `Some(name)` arm; `T = i64` mono regression guard — primitive-T let-binding mono emits no destructor (skip-when-empty per slice 8u). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 676 → 680, all prior + 4 new). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (~145 lines net — `lookup_let_type_expr` + 3 walker helpers + state-struct + destructor wire-ups + new `Some(name)` arm), `tests/codegen.rs` (4 new tests). **What slice 8x does NOT cover** (carried as follow-on surface): (1) MethodCall / Call / StructLit / Index / FieldAccess RHS shapes for unannotated lets (`let copy = items.clone();` / `let h = Hub { count: 0 };` / etc.) — needs the typechecker's `expr_types` sibling table threaded through to recover the recorded expression type; deferred until that infrastructure lands or a use case forces it. (2) Multi-binding patterns (tuple / struct destructure) inside a let — the helper finds the binding name via `pattern.binding_names()` but only returns the let's whole-type annotation; component types of a destructure would need per-field resolution. (3) The underlying typechecker issue (`lower_type_expr(ty_expr, &[])` passes empty generic scope, mis-classifying `T` as `Type::Named`) — slice 8x masks the symptom at codegen, but a follow-on typechecker fix would record `Type::TypeParam` correctly and make the destructor's new `Some(name)` arm exercise a strictly smaller surface. **Test coverage from the line-26 spec:** the spec's primary test case — `fn driver[T](item: T) { fetch(); let copy = item; fetch(); }` with `T = Vec[i64]` lowering both fields to Vec struct shape with destructor `cap > 0 ? free` for both — now passes end-to-end.
  32. [x] **Slice 8y — polymorphic-effect monomorphizations (caller-side intercept gating) shipped 2026-05-20.** Lands the per-call-site state-machine-intercept gate the spec named as the slice 8y optimization, threaded end-to-end from the effect checker through cli.rs to the codegen monomorphization path. **Scope correction vs. the original spec:** the spec called for gating the per-mono `emit_state_machine_helpers_for_mono` *emission* on resolved-per-call effects, on the premise that a polymorphic `fn driver[T, E: Effect](item: T) with E` would otherwise pay state-machine emission cost at every mono including non-network ones. That premise turns out to not fire under the current `state_struct_layouts` architecture: a callee enters `state_struct_layouts` only when its body contains static yield points (per `build_state_struct_layouts`'s coupling to `build_yield_points_table`'s non-empty filter), so a callee that is *only* network-yielding through `E` has no `state_struct_layouts` entry and never paid the emission cost the spec was optimizing away. The actual reachable optimization at v1 is gating the *caller-side state-machine intercept* — when a purely-polymorphic-effect callee's body has static yield points BUT a given call site resolves `E` to a non-network effect set, the caller can take a direct mango-keyed call instead of state-struct alloc + poll loop + scheduler yield + free. Slice 8y ships this gate. **Implementation details:** New `Program.callee_purely_polymorphic_effects: HashSet<String>` records callees whose `DeclaredEffects` is `Polymorphic` only (no `Explicit` / `PolymorphicWithFixed` fixed portion); `PolymorphicWithFixed` is intentionally excluded because the fixed portion may carry `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)` regardless of `E`. New `build_callee_purely_polymorphic_effects_set` builder in `src/cli.rs` mirrors `build_callee_network_yield_effect_table`'s sourcing of `declared_effects`. Pipeline wires the set into `Program.callee_purely_polymorphic_effects` alongside the existing `call_effect_subs` threading. New `Codegen.call_uses_state_machine(call_span, base_key)` predicate in `src/codegen/mono.rs` consults `program_snapshot.state_struct_layouts`, `callee_purely_polymorphic_effects`, and `call_effect_subs` to decide between state-machine and direct-call paths per call site. `compile_call` in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` and `compile_generic_call` in `src/codegen/mono.rs` now accept a `call_span: &Span` parameter (threaded from `ExprKind::Call` lowering in `src/codegen/exprs.rs`), so the gating predicate has access to the call-expression span used as the `call_effect_subs` key. The per-mono helpers stay emitted unconditionally (idempotent across call sites; a later call site whose `E` resolves to network-yield may still need them); only the caller-side intercept is gated. **What slice 8y does NOT do** (carried as follow-on architectural work): broadens `state_struct_layouts` population to also include purely-polymorphic-effect callees WITHOUT body yield points — the case the original spec envisioned as the primary optimization opportunity. Decoupling `state_struct_layouts` population from the `yield_points` non-empty filter is bigger-scope than slice 8y and would lever the slice 8y gate to fire on a much larger surface (every monomorphization of `fn driver[T, with E](item: T) with E` would then pay the emission cost today and be optimized away per call site). **Soundness caveat (documented in `call_uses_state_machine`):** for a private fn whose body has static yield points AND is declared purely polymorphic (`fn op[T, with E](cb: Fn() with E) with E { fetch(); cb(); }`), the body parks at `fetch()` regardless of `E` resolution; the slice 8y skip would technically be unsound (the direct-call path bypasses the event-loop driver that the body's internal `fetch()` requires). The v1 test-harness `fetch` stubs are empty-bodied so the skip is harmless in tests; production correctness awaits the same follow-on slice that decouples `state_struct_layouts` from body-yield-points. **4 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8y: caller-side state-machine intercept gating` section: purely-polymorphic callee is in the marker set (`fn op[T, with E](cb: Fn() with E) with E { cb(); }` lands in `callee_purely_polymorphic_effects`); `PolymorphicWithFixed` callee is excluded (`with reads(Db) E` is NOT in the set — fixed portion may carry network-yield); `Explicit` callee is excluded (`fn driver[T](item: T) { fetch(); }` whose effects come from body inference, NOT a `with E` annotation, is NOT in the set); non-polymorphic-effect callee still takes the state-machine intercept (regression coverage — `driver$i64` mono still emits `call ptr @__kara_state_new_driver$i64()` + `kara.poll_loop` block, demonstrating slice 8y is a strict no-op for callees outside the marker set). **`ir_for_with_state_struct_layouts` helper** (in `tests/codegen.rs`) was extended to also populate `call_effect_subs` and `callee_purely_polymorphic_effects` so test fixtures see the same program shape the cli pipeline produces — empty for legacy fixtures (degrades to pre-8y conservative behavior). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 692 → 696 — the 4 new tests). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `CalleePurelyPolymorphicEffectsSet` type alias + `Program.callee_purely_polymorphic_effects` field, ~28 lines including doc-comments), `src/cli.rs` (new `build_callee_purely_polymorphic_effects_set` builder + pipeline wire-up, ~28 lines), `src/codegen/exprs.rs` (1-line span pass-through), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (`compile_call` accepts `call_span` + 2 forwarding sites to `compile_generic_call`), `src/codegen/mono.rs` (new `call_uses_state_machine` predicate + intercept gate, ~85 lines net), `tests/codegen.rs` (helper extension + 4 new tests). **Unblocks:** none — slice 8y was the last entry under the line 26 sub-slice queue that depended on slice 8ac. The line-26 sub-slice tracker (entries 28-32, 34-36) is now fully resolved.
  33. [x] **Slice 8z — ref / slice-elem param shapes through the per-mono caller intercept shipped 2026-05-20.** Closes the cancel-leak path that slice 8v Phase 2 left open for ref / slice-elem params: the per-mono intercept in `compile_generic_call` (`src/codegen/mono.rs`) stored compiled `arg_vals[i]` LLVM values directly into state-struct captured-local fields (slice-8f shape). For owned-value params (`fn driver[T](item: T)`) that's correct; for `ref T` / `mut ref T` / `mut Slice[T]` the loaded value (Vec struct, i64, etc.) is the wrong shape to land in a `ptr` / `{ ptr, i64 }` state-struct field. Empirical probe (2026-05-20) on the pre-fix `T = Vec[i64]` shape confirmed: the per-mono intercept emitted `store { ptr, i64, i64 } %v, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr` against a ptr-typed state-struct field — opaque pointers accepted the IR but semantically the 24-byte Vec struct overflowed the 8-byte field into adjacent state-struct bytes. **Three coordinated changes:** (1) `declare_mono_function` (`src/codegen/mono.rs`) now mirrors `declare_one_function` for the mangled per-mono key — populates `fn_param_ref` / `fn_param_slice_elem` with the polymorphic source's per-param ref-flags and slice-element types respectively. Type-parameter-typed ref (`ref T`) keeps `ref_flag: true` regardless of T's resolution because `TypeKind::Ref(_)` lowers uniformly to ptr; `mut Slice[T]`'s element type resolves through `extract_slice_elem_type` → `llvm_type_for_type_expr`, which honors the active `type_subst`. (2) The per-mono intercept's arg-storing loop in `compile_generic_call` consults the new mangled-key tables and dispatches: for `ref` params with `ExprKind::Identifier` args, `get_data_ptr(var_name)` returns the caller-side variable's data ptr; for `ref` params with rvalue args (literals, function returns, arithmetic), a new `materialize_rvalue_for_ref_arg` helper allocas an entry-block stack temp, stores `arg_vals[i]` into it, registers Vec-struct-shaped temporaries with `track_vec_var` for scope-exit `FreeVecBuffer` cleanup (mirroring slice 8d's `compile_call::ref_rvalue_arg{i}` discipline), and returns the temp's ptr; for slice-elem params, `coerce_to_slice(arg, elem_ty)` synthesizes the `{ptr, i64}` slice header at the call site. (3) The same probe surfaced a latent companion bug in `llvm_type_for_name`: the typechecker's `record_pattern_inner_type` arm records the canonical `"Slice"` surface name in `pattern_binding_types` for `Type::Slice` bindings, but `llvm_type_for_name`'s match arms didn't recognise "Slice" — the lookup fell through to the i64 default. So even when the intercept stored the correct slice header value, the state-struct field's layout was 8 bytes for a 16-byte slice header. The new `"Slice" => slice_struct_type()` arm mirrors the identical recognition in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` (line 67-69's `TypeKind::Path("Slice")`). **3 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8z` section: `fn driver[T](item: ref T)` with `T = Vec[i64]` — state-struct field lowers to `{ i32, ptr }`; caller emits `store ptr %v, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr` (data ptr, not loaded Vec); regression-guards on no `store { ptr, i64, i64 } %v, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr`. `fn driver[T](items: mut Slice[T])` with `T = i64` — state-struct field lowers to `{ i32, { ptr, i64 } }`; caller emits `store { ptr, i64 } %slice.<...>, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr` (synthesized header); same regression guard. Owned `T` param regression guard — `fn driver[T](item: T)` with `T = i64` still emits `store i64 42, ptr %kara.arg0.field_ptr`, confirming the extension is gated on the ref/slice tables and doesn't perturb the owned-value path. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 680 → 683, lib 565 / lib serial 565, integration 28 — all green). Files: `src/codegen/mono.rs` (~95 lines net — `materialize_rvalue_for_ref_arg` helper + per-mono intercept arg-store extension + `declare_mono_function` table population), `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (~12 lines net — new `"Slice"` arm in `llvm_type_for_name`), `tests/codegen.rs` (3 new tests). **What slice 8z does NOT cover** (carried as follow-on entries): see entries 37 (non-generic state-machine intercept ref/slice gap, `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:271-286`), 38 (method-call state-machine intercept ref/slice gap, `src/codegen/method_call.rs:103`), and 39 (`mut ref T` + type-param-typed slice with non-i64 element verification gaps). Critical correction to slice 8z's spec: the 2026-05-20 probe verified that the claim "the slice 8d intercept handles ref/slice correctly for non-generic yielding fns" is incorrect — the slice 8d intercept handles ref/slice in `compile_call`'s general path but explicitly defers it in the state-machine intercept (see in-code comment at `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs:262-265`: "ref-passing through the state struct lands alongside the method-call intercept"). Entries 37 and 38 ship the identical fix shape (consult `fn_param_ref` / `fn_param_slice_elem` in each intercept's arg-storing loop, dispatch by mode) and may share a helper via a refactor — see entry 37 for the consolidation plan.

[x] **Slice 8aa — `call_effect_subs` side-table populated from existing per-call effect-variable resolution shipped 2026-05-20.** **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** the pre-ship plan assumed Kāra's effect model was "caller-context-flows-DOWN" (caller's `with` clause broadcast into the callee's named effect variable `E`). Empirical scout 2026-05-20 found this is wrong — the model is callee-effects-flow-UP. The named effect variable `E` is resolved per call site by unioning effects across Fn-arg slot positions that reference `E` in the callee's signature; if `E` has no Fn-arg references, it resolves to ⊥ (empty). This resolution already exists in `src/effectchecker.rs::compute_call_var_bindings` (line 1031), called from `check_call_args_subtyping` (`src/effectchecker/subtyping.rs:110`). What was missing was the **persistence** of those bindings in a side-table so downstream consumers (slice 8ab → codegen → slice 8y) can read them. **Fix:** new `call_effect_subs: HashMap<SpanKey, HashMap<String, HashSet<Effect>>>` field on both `EffectChecker` (working state) and `EffectCheckResult` (public output). Populated in `check_call_args_subtyping` immediately after `compute_call_var_bindings` returns — only recorded when the binding map is non-empty (the absence of an entry signals "no polymorphic-effect to resolve" downstream, distinct from "resolved to ⊥"). Two existing literal `EffectCheckResult { ... }` construction sites updated to include the new field (`src/concurrency_report.rs::empty_effects`, `tests/missing_track_caller_lint.rs::empty_effects`). **3 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8aa` section: polymorphic-effect call with a `reads(Db)` closure records `E → {reads(Db)}` at the call-site span; non-polymorphic-effect program leaves the table empty (absence semantics); two distinct call sites to the same polymorphic-effect callee record two entries (one with `reads(Db)`, one empty) — pins the per-call-site granularity that slice 8y needs. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 46 test binaries (codegen 690 / 690, effectchecker 270 → 273, lib 565 / lib serial 565, integration 28). [x] **Slice 8ac — `E: Effect` bound syntax (effect-parameter trait bounds) shipped 2026-05-20.** Closes the parser/AST gap so design.md line 736's `fn handle[E: Effect](...)` spelling parses to the same shape as the positional `[with E]` form. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** the plan envisioned resolver bound-validation (rejecting `[T, E: NonEffect]`) and effect-checker bound-enforcement at call sites. Empirical scout 2026-05-20 found both are no-ops for v1: with the parser-side classification key (first bound is `Effect`, structural), `[T, E: NonEffect]` parses as a TYPE param with bound `NonEffect` — no special diagnostic needed; the unknown-trait path fires naturally. The `Effect` marker is the universal effect-trait, so every effect set trivially satisfies it — no call-site validation work to do. v1 enforcement of granular bounds (`E: Effect + UserExt`, `E: no writes(R)`) is deferred to a future slice per design.md line 3150's Phase 7 P0 reservation. **Fix:** parser-side classification in `src/parser/generics.rs` — after parsing an identifier + optional `: bound-list`, if the FIRST bound's single-segment path is exactly `Effect` (no generic args), reclassify the param into `effect_params` rather than `params`. AST change: `GenericParams.effect_params: Vec<String>` → `Vec<EffectParam>` where `EffectParam { name, bounds, span }` carries the parsed bound list. Positional `with E` continues to produce `EffectParam` with empty `bounds`; the new `E: Effect` form produces `EffectParam` with a single-`Effect` bound. The bound list is preserved verbatim for future granularity. **6 new tests** in `tests/parser.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ac` section: bound-form parses with correct AST shape (`name="E"`, bounds path `["Effect"]`, no generic args, effect-clause still resolves `Variable("E")`); equivalence to `[T, with E]` (same param count, same name, marker bound on the bounded form, no bound on positional); coexistence with `with` block (`[T, E: Effect, with F]` collects both); extra bounds preserved (`E: Effect + Foo` stores both, still classifies as effect-param); non-Effect bound stays type-param (`T: Ord` regression guard); `Effect[args]` stays type-param (v1 only matches bare `Effect`). **3 new tests** in `tests/effectchecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ac` section: bound-form `pub fn identity[T, E: Effect]` polymorphic classification (mirrors `test_effect_variable_makes_function_polymorphic`); bound-form compound polymorphism end-to-end (closure with concrete effects binds `E` at call site; caller effects include closure's effects); bound-form `apply` round-trip (mirrors `test_polymorphic_returning_with_E_does_not_emit_missing_effects`). **2 new tests** in `tests/resolver.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ac` section: bound-form fn resolves clean; impl-level effect-var rejection (`ImplLevelEffectVarNotAllowed`) still fires for `impl[E: Effect] Sink for LogSink` (the bound form does not bypass slice 4's impl-level rule; diagnostic still names `E`). [x] **Slice 8ae — method-call state-machine intercept's ref / slice-elem gap shipped 2026-05-20.** Closes the parallel of slice 8z (per-mono intercept) and slice 8ad (non-generic free-fn intercept) on the method-call side. Both dispatch through `fn_param_ref` / `fn_param_slice_elem` keyed on the impl-method's dotted name (e.g. `"Container.run"`) — populated by `declare_function` against the synthesized impl-method function whose `params[0]` is self after `make_impl_method_function` promotes `SelfParam` into a real `Param`. So `ref_flags[0]` covers self, `ref_flags[1..]` covers method args at param indices `i + 1`. Self uses `usize::MAX` as the arg_idx sentinel when calling `materialize_rvalue_for_ref_arg` (the helper's `arg{i}` name suffix won't collide with method arg slots). **Empirical probe finding 2026-05-20:** the original spec-suggested test source used `shared struct Hub`, but a probe revealed the method-call intercept's `callee_key` (from `method_callee_types`) is `None` for shared-struct method calls — `method_callee_types` doesn't populate the call-site span for shared-struct receivers. [x] **Slice 8ag — typechecker `mut ref T` call-site unification with mut-marker auto-ref-take shipped 2026-05-20.** Closes the typechecker gap surfaced by slice 8af's verification probe. **Root cause:** pre-slice-8ag, `is_subtype` / `types_compatible` / `unify_types` had no `owned-source → mut ref T` coercion arm — only the corresponding `mut Slice[T]` coercion existed. Both shapes participate in the same call-boundary contract (owned source + `mut` marker → mutable borrow at the callee), so the asymmetry was a real bug affecting **every** `mut ref T` slot, not just the type-parameter-typed case. The non-generic case (`set_at(mut v, …)` against `fn set_at(v: mut ref Vec[i64], …)`) was masked because the `test_e2e_vec_indexed_write_through_mut_ref_param` e2e harness uses `run_program`, which does not assert `typed.errors.is_empty()` — the type error was emitted but ignored, and codegen tolerated the shape mismatch via runtime layout. Slice 8ag's verification probe (typechecker direct, not e2e) confirmed both cases failed: `expected 'mut ref T', found 'i64'` (generic) and `expected 'mut ref Vec<i64>', found 'Vec<i64>'` (concrete). **Fix:** add the `MutRef → owned` coercion arms to `is_subtype`, `types_compatible`, and `unify_types`, mirroring the existing `mut Slice[T] → Vec[T] / Array[T, N]` coercion pattern in `types_compatible`. The `Ref` / `MutRef` (and `Weak` in unify_types) exclusion blocks the `ref T → mut ref T` loss-of-mutability cross. The `unify_types` arm recurses into the inner so generic resolution pins `T` against the owned source's type (e.g. `driver[T](item: mut ref T)` called with owned `i64` solves `T = i64`). The `mut` call-site marker is enforced separately by `check_call_site_marker` (unchanged), so `MissingMutMarker` still fires when the caller forgets `mut`, and `InvalidMutMarker` still fires when the param shape is non-mutating. **5 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ag` section: type-param `mut ref T` accepts owned + mut marker; non-generic `mut ref Vec[i64]` accepts owned + mut marker; missing marker on owned source still fires `MissingMutMarker` (for both concrete and type-param param shapes); `ref T → mut ref T` cross still rejected (loss-of-mutability guard). **1 new test** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ag` section: re-enables the carved-out `mut ref T` per-mono intercept probe from slice 8af — verifies the state-struct field for type-param `mut ref T` lowers to `ptr` and the caller stores the address-of source binding (regression guard against storing the loaded i64 value). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (typechecker 1170 → 1175, codegen 691 → 692, lib 565 / lib serial 565, integration 28). Files: `src/typechecker/types.rs` (~25 lines net — new `MutRef → non-Ref` arms in `is_subtype` and `types_compatible`, with comment cross-referencing the existing `Slice{mutable:true}` pattern), `src/typechecker/inference.rs` (~12 lines net — new `MutRef → non-Ref/Weak` arm in `unify_types`), `tests/typechecker.rs` (5 new tests + section comment documenting the root-cause analysis), `tests/codegen.rs` (1 new test). **What slice 8ag does NOT cover:** the broader typechecker invariant that `mut ref T` at any non-call-arg position (e.g. `let x: mut ref T = owned_val`) is now accepted at the type level — this mirrors the existing `mut Slice[T]` behaviour and is consistent with the design's "marker enforces at call sites, types are permissive" pattern. Ownership-checking is the layer that ultimately rejects ill-formed mut-ref bindings; no audit of every non-call site was performed in this slice. If a regression surfaces from a non-call mut-ref shape that should remain rejected, the right fix is in ownership analysis, not by tightening the type-level arm.

[x] **Slice 8ah — terminal-arm placeholder replacement (user-level final-expression body-splitting) shipped 2026-05-26.** Slice 8i (line 127) shipped the end-to-end state-struct return-field ABI with a constant `i64 0` placeholder stored into `%kara.return.field_ptr` from the terminal poll-fn arm. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** the plan's (a)+(b) — "extend the arm-body emitter so it compiles the user's final expression with the state-struct field map as the variables-in-scope source" — turned out to already be done. Slices 8o (final-expression `BodyArg` capture) and 8q (lowered binary arithmetic) had already widened the terminal-arm path to materialise `IntLit` / `Slot` / `Binary` through `materialize_body_arg` against the per-arm slot map. Of the three classes called out in 8i's note, identifier reference and binary op were covered (`test_terminal_return_8o_uses_captured_local_final_expr`, `test_terminal_return_8o_uses_arm_local_let_final_expr`, `test_body_splitting_8q_binary_in_terminal_return`). Only **call-returning-i64** remained — `recognize_body_arg`'s `Call { callee: Path }` arm matched the lowered integer-arithmetic surface but didn't recognise bare-identifier user free-fn calls like `other_fn()`. **Fix:** new `BodyArg::Call { name, args }` variant; new bare-`Identifier` arm in `recognize_body_arg` that accepts any free-fn call whose name is NOT marked `true` in `callee_network_yield_effect` (yielding callees stay on the state-machine intercept path; lowering them synchronously here would skip their yield); recursive arg recognition reuses the existing `BodyArg` recognised set. **Threading:** `recognize_body_arg` gained a `network_yield: &CalleeNetworkYieldEffectTable` parameter — all six existing call sites in the walker (let RHS, assign RHS, compound-assign RHS, free-fn-call args, method-call args, terminal final-expression) updated to pass `&program.callee_network_yield_effect`. The recognition extension applies in ALL `BodyArg` positions (not just terminal) — a `let x = helper()` between yields, or `take(helper())` as a call arg, now lower the same way; the conservative-skip discipline (any unrecognised nested shape → whole call skipped) carries through unchanged. `materialize_body_arg` arm for `BodyArg::Call`: `module.get_function(name)?` → materialise args via the same helper → `build_call` → `try_as_basic_value().basic()` for the `Option<BasicValueEnum>` return (None for void callees, falling the caller through to the conservative skip — terminal field keeps `i64 0`). **3 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ah` section: tail `other_fn()` returning i64 (no args) emits `%other_fn.return = call i64 @other_fn()` + stores the result into `%kara.return.field_ptr`; tail `ident(n)` where `n` is a captured local emits a slot-load + the call (regression pin that the arg-materialisation path threads through); tail call to a yielding callee (`remote_fetch() -> i64 with sends(Network)`) falls back to the `i64 0` placeholder (network-yield filter at recognition time prevents the synchronous-call shortcut). **2 existing tests updated:** `test_body_splitting_8k_skips_unrecognised_arg_shape` + `test_body_splitting_8l_skips_method_with_unrecognised_arg` previously used `ident(n)` as the "unrecognised" arg shape; with slice 8ah that's now recognised, so both tests switched to an `if`-expression arg (still unrecognised) to keep the conservative-skip-discipline guard intact. **1 existing test removed:** `test_terminal_return_8o_unrecognised_final_expr_keeps_zero_fallback` documented the old "Identifier-callee user-fn calls remain unrecognised" gap which slice 8ah closes — replaced by the new slice-8ah test for the same source asserting the now-correct emission. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen 776 → 778, all other binaries unchanged). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (~50 lines net — new `BodyArg::Call` variant + threaded `network_yield` arg through `recognize_body_arg` + new bare-`Identifier` recognition arm + new materialisation arm), `tests/codegen.rs` (3 new tests + 2 existing rewrites + 1 removal). **Cross-refs:** Slice 8i terminal-field ABI at line 127; line 50 parent's `[~]` clears once slice 8ai (line 129) also ships.

[x] **Slice 8ai — return-type widening beyond `i64` for state-machine transform shipped 2026-05-26.** **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** plan item (c) — "update the slice-8d / 8g caller-side intercepts to load through the correct LLVM type rather than assuming `i64`" — turned out to already be done. The slice-8d / 8g / per-mono intercepts already load through `state_machine_return_types.get(key)`'s typed entry (the hardcoded `i64 0` only appears in the unit-return fallback branch when there's NO entry for the key). So the actual code surface was (a) widen the registration helper, (b) update the registration call site, and (d) tests per type class. Plan's "by-pointer through a pre-allocated slot" scheme for user structs was not needed — the inline anonymous-struct shape (codegen registers user structs via `context.struct_type(..., false)`, not `opaque_struct_type`) lowers cleanly through the terminal field as a structural value with `zeroinitializer` as the placeholder. **Fix:** new module-level helper `state_machine_return_type_for(cg, ty) -> Option<BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>` in `src/codegen/declarations.rs` recognises the full v1 set: integer / float primitives (`i8`/`i16`/`i32`/`i64`, `u8`/`u16`/`u32`/`u64`, `usize`/`isize`, `f32`/`f64`, `bool`, `char`), `Vec[T]` / `VecDeque[T]` / `String` / `str` (inline `{ptr, i64, i64}` slice descriptor — independent of `T`), `Slice[T]` (`{ptr, i64}`), and concrete (non-shared) user structs declared in the program (via `struct_types`). Tuples, refs / mut-refs, shared structs, opaque user types, and unknown name shapes return `None` (callee stays on the unit-return path). Registration site in `emit_state_struct_type_for_key` swaps `is_i64_return_type(ret_te)` for `state_machine_return_type_for(self, ret_te)` and pushes the returned LLVM type as the terminal field. **Typed placeholder:** the terminal-arm fallback (when the body-splitting walker can't recognise the user's final expression) was a hardcoded `self.context.i64_type().const_int(0, false)` — width-mismatched for the widened set. New module-level helper `basic_zero_for_type(ty) -> BasicValueEnum<'ctx>` matches across the `BasicTypeEnum` variants (IntType / FloatType / PointerType / StructType / ArrayType / VectorType / ScalableVectorType) and returns the corresponding `const_zero()`. The terminal-arm now reads `state_machine_return_types[emit_key]` once into `ret_ty`, threads it into the fallback as `basic_zero_for_type(ret_ty)`, and stores well-typed zero. **`is_i64_return_type` removed** — the only call site was the registration helper, now subsumed by the widened lookup. **6 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 26 slice 8ai` section: i32 return (state struct + typed slot-load through the slice-8ah `BodyArg::Slot` path — `x: i32` parameter form sidesteps the integer-literal inference gap where `0` doesn't narrow to i32 in return-context); bool return (`{ i32, i1 }` state struct + `store i1 false` placeholder); Vec[i64] return (`{ptr, i64, i64}` descriptor + `store ... zeroinitializer`); String return (same descriptor as Vec); user struct return (`Hub { count: i64 }` lowers to anonymous `{ i64 }` + `zeroinitializer`); caller-side load through the widened type (`load i32` for an i32 callee). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries (codegen 778 → 823 — the +45 reflects 6 new slice-8ai + several tests previously skipped vacuously when the runtime crate wasn't built; the slice 8ah work in this session's earlier worktree, not just slice 8ai, also contributed; importantly zero failures). Files: `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (~55 lines net — new `state_machine_return_type_for` helper + new `basic_zero_for_type` helper + registration-site swap + terminal-arm typed-zero fallback; `is_i64_return_type` removed), `tests/codegen.rs` (6 new tests + section comment). **Cross-refs:** Slice 8i `state_machine_return_types` field at line 127; with slice 8ah (line 152) also shipped, line 50 parent's `[~]` flips to `[x]`.

- [~] **P0 — RAII-across-yield as compile error.** Implements the spec from the design audit (2) above. New typechecker pass: walk every network-boundary function's body; for each suspension point (every call to a function carrying network effects), check the live set of resources at that point; reject if any resource's type is not `CancelSafe`. Define the `CancelSafe` marker in stdlib; seed the v1 implementations (file handles after flush, well-defined RC types, etc.). Diagnostic + fix-it shape per spec.

[x] **Slice 1 — closed-enumeration shared-struct / shared-enum detection shipped 2026-05-18.** New `src/raii_check.rs` module + `RaiiAcrossYieldError { fn_key, binding_name, type_name, yield_span }` diagnostic + `check_raii_across_yield(program, types) -> Vec<RaiiAcrossYieldError>` entry point exported as `karac::raii_across_yield_check`. v1 detection runs the closed-enumeration approach: walks every entry in `program.state_struct_layouts` (slice-4 output — the per-function union of captured locals across yield points) and, for each field whose `type_name` resolves to a `shared struct N` or `shared enum N` (via `TypeCheckResult.struct_info[name].is_shared == true` or the `enum_info` analog), emits one `RaiiAcrossYieldError` anchored at the function's first yield-point span. Diagnostic body: `holding \`<name>\` (type \`<T>\`) across a suspension point in \`<fn_key>\` is not cancel-safe`; `help`: `release \`<name>\` before the yield, or \`impl CancelSafe for <T>\` once the type's Drop impl is audited to be safe under cancellation` — surfaces the two fix-its from the design audit up front (slice 2 will add the marker trait itself). Pipeline wiring in `src/cli.rs`: new `Pipeline.raii_errors: Option<Vec<RaiiAcrossYieldError>>` field, new `Pipeline::raii_check()` phase invoked from `run_all_checks` after `provider_escape_check`, counted in `total_errors`, surfaced through plain output (`error[E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD]: ... help: ...`), JSON `DiagEntry` collection (`phase: "raii_check"`, `code: "E_RAII_ACROSS_YIELD"`), JSONL phase events + `diagnostic` events, and the `cmd_run` hard-error short-circuit (mirrors the provider-escape contract — RAII violations would let cancel-leaked resources reach the interpreter, so the run path exits 1 rather than proceed). **8 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs`: shared-struct `self` held across yield → rejected (binding_name=`self`, type_name=`Hub`, fn_key=`Hub.run`); regular (non-shared) struct `self` → accepted; shared-enum `self` → rejected (symmetric rule); shared-struct param `h: Hub` in a free function → rejected (pins that the check fires regardless of param vs. self origin); `Vec[i64]` param → accepted (cancel-safe surface); primitive `i64` param → accepted (no recorded `type_name` so the check skips per-spec); pure function (no yield-points) → no entry, no errors; `None` types arg → empty errors (defensive contract — never spuriously fires without typecheck data). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 41 test binaries (8 new in `raii_check`; 496 codegen, 1064 typechecker, 250 effectchecker, ... all green). Files: `src/raii_check.rs` (new), `src/lib.rs` (module + `raii_across_yield_check` entry point), `src/cli.rs` (`Pipeline.raii_errors` field + `raii_check` phase + text/JSON/JSONL emission + `cmd_run` short-circuit), `tests/raii_check.rs` (new, 8 tests + `run_raii_check` driver). **What slice 1 does NOT cover:** see follow-on entries 2–5 below — `CancelSafe` marker trait + user-extensible opt-in (slice 2); flow-sensitive detection (slice 3); raw-pointer detection (slice 4); precise binding-construction span anchoring (slice 5). **Unblocks** slice 6 of line 26 (the codegen state-machine transform): the typechecker now rejects programs that the state-machine transform couldn't soundly lower — codegen never has to defensively handle non-cancel-safe bindings in the poll-fn lowering path.

[x] **Slice 2 — `CancelSafe` marker trait + user-extensible opt-in shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the gap where slice 1's diagnostic promised `impl CancelSafe for <T>` as a fix-it but the trait did not yet exist (following the help text got the user a "trait CancelSafe not found" resolver error). **Fix:** new `collect_cancel_safe_opt_ins(program) -> HashSet<String>` in `src/raii_check.rs` walks `program.items` for `Item::ImplBlock { trait_name: Some(p), target_type, .. }` whose `p.segments.last() == "CancelSafe"`, extracts the single-segment `target_type` name via the `TypeKind::Path(p) if p.segments.len() == 1` pattern (mirrors the opaque-type check in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs:1334`), and accumulates target names into the set. `is_not_cancel_safe_v1` renamed to `is_not_cancel_safe` and gained a `cancel_safe_opt_ins: &HashSet<String>` parameter — the set is consulted before the closed-enumeration check, so a `shared struct H` with `impl CancelSafe for H` in scope no longer fires. **Marker-trait infrastructure** already existed (`Item::MarkerTrait`, `env.marker_traits`, `parse_marker_trait`, the `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD` body-empty check) — the trait declaration itself is the existing `marker trait CancelSafe;` form. v1 keeps the trait *user-declared*: programs (and tests) declare `marker trait CancelSafe;` inline alongside the opt-in impl. **Discovered constraint during test authoring:** the parser requires `impl Trait for T { }` (braces) even for empty marker-trait impls — there is no `impl Trait for T;` short form. Tests use the `{ }` form. **4 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 2` section: shared struct + `impl CancelSafe for Hub { }` opt-in → accepted; shared enum + `impl CancelSafe for Status { }` opt-in → accepted (symmetric); shared struct without opt-in → still rejected (slice 1 contract preserved); typo'd impl (`impl CancelSafeButTypo for Hub { }`) → opt-in NOT applied (path-segment-equality is strict, regression guard against any contains / prefix / case-insensitive walker). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (raii_check 8 → 12; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `src/raii_check.rs` (new walker + predicate signature change), `tests/raii_check.rs` (4 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 2 does NOT cover:** stdlib `CancelSafe` seeding (deferred until stdlib infrastructure lands — track separately when that surfaces); generic-parameter-bounded opt-ins (`impl[T: CancelSafe] CancelSafe for Vec[T]` — needs bound-resolution wiring beyond a syntactic name walk); negative impls or coherence checks across opt-ins (v1 accepts any well-formed impl regardless of audit; the diagnostic's `help` text says "once the type's Drop impl is audited" — auditing is on the user, not the compiler); multi-segment target paths (e.g. `impl CancelSafe for module::Foo`) — the v1 walker silently skips them.
  3. [~] **Slice 3 — flow-sensitive detection.** Slice 1 detects by surface-type identity (shared struct / shared enum); slice 3 detects by *binding state* at the yield point — `File` held with unflushed writes, `BufReader` with a non-empty buffer, database transaction handles before commit. Spec settled (the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "<name>")]` attribute landed in slice 3a as the v1 declaration surface; flow-walker infrastructure is type-agnostic so each stdlib type lights up by adding the attribute to its soiling methods). Carry parent open while remaining stdlib prereqs (`BufReader[R]`) ship; sub-slices break out per stdlib type as it lands.
     1. [x] **Slice 3a — flow-sensitive infrastructure + File seeding shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the design.md "File before fsync" pattern for the v1 `File` handle (phase-8 line 87, shipped 2026-05-26). **Attribute:** new `cancel_unsafe_until` bare-name registered in `attribute_validator::RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`. Shape: `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "<clear>")]` on an impl method declares "calling this method on a receiver flips the receiver to a cancel-unsafe state until `<clear>` is called on the same receiver". Stdlib seeding: `File.write` in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` carries `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` — clear method is `flush` (also `sync_all` once that ships; only `flush` is in the v1 surface). **Walker (`src/raii_check.rs`):** new `collect_cancel_unsafe_annotations` walks both user `program.items` AND every program in `crate::prelude::STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (the baked stdlib's impl blocks don't get spliced into `program.items` — `synthetic_prelude_items` clones the StructDef only, so the walker reaches into STDLIB_PROGRAMS explicitly to pick up `File.write`). Returns `HashMap<type_name, HashMap<soiling_method, clear_method>>`. **New `StateFlowWalker`** mirrors `cli::YieldPointWalker`'s structure — same scope-discipline (push on let / pattern binding, truncate on block exit), same network-yield detection via `method_callee_types` lookup, plus a per-binding-name `state: HashMap<String, BindingState>` threaded linearly through the walk. At each `MethodCall(object=Identifier(n)|SelfValue, method, ...)`, looks up `annotations[type_of(n)][method]` — if Some(clear_name), flips `state[n] = Soiled { soiling_method, soil_span, clear_method_name }`; if `state[n]` is `Soiled` and the called method matches the recorded `clear_method_name`, flips back to `Clean`. At each yield-point call site (Call or MethodCall where the resolved callee_key is in `callee_network_yield_effect`), iterates `state` and emits one `RaiiAcrossYieldError { state_violation: Some(_) }` per Soiled binding. **Diagnostic extension:** new `state_violation: Option<StateViolation>` field on `RaiiAcrossYieldError` (`StateViolation { soiling_method, soil_span, clear_method_name }`). `message()` / `help()` branch on `state_violation.is_some()`: message names the soiling method and the remediation call shape (`call `f.flush` before yielding...`); help points at the literal clear method (`call `f.flush()` before the suspension point...`) rather than the slice-1 `impl CancelSafe` fix-it. **cli.rs emission (three output paths):** plain text adds `note: soiled by `.write()` here at <span>` between the binding-declaration note and the help line when `state_violation` is `Some`; JSON `DiagEntry.extra_json` accumulates a `"state_violation":{"soiling_method":...,"clear_method_name":...,"soil_span":{...}}` block alongside the existing `"binding_span":{...}`; JSONL `diagnostic` event appends the same structured payload. **v1 implementation shape — linear forward flow, no branch merging:** every soiling call met in source-traversal order soils; every clearing call clears; irrespective of whether the call was in an `if` / `match` arm / loop body. Biased toward false positives over false negatives — a soil reachable in any walked branch propagates to the yield. Precise branch-merging is a follow-on sub-slice; the v1 surface catches the design.md flagship case and unblocks BufReader by plug-and-play attribute annotation. **Dedup contract:** one `RaiiAcrossYieldError` per `(binding, fn_key)` pair, even when the binding is held Soiled across multiple yield points — matches slice 1's per-binding emission shape (`emitted: HashSet<String>` in the walker). **8 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 3a` section: `file_write_then_yield_rejected` (linear shape, asserts `state_violation.soiling_method == "write"` + `clear_method_name == "flush"`); `file_write_then_flush_then_yield_accepted` (clear closes the soil); `file_param_without_write_held_across_yield_accepted` (File alone is cancel-safe — soiling requires the call); `file_write_violation_carries_state_help_text` (pins the help text branching: contains `f.flush()`, contains `pending `write``, does NOT contain `impl CancelSafe` — guards against slice-3 errors regressing to the slice-1 help shape); `file_two_writes_then_one_flush_then_yield_accepted` (one clear closes all preceding soils — the OS flush semantic); `file_write_flush_write_then_yield_rejected` (re-soil after a clear triggers detection); `file_two_yields_emit_one_error_per_binding` (dedup contract); `user_annotated_type_participates` (user-defined `struct Tx { } impl Tx { #[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "commit")] fn put(...); fn commit(...); }` triggers the same diagnostic, pins the user-extensibility surface so future stdlib types plug in by annotation alone). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (raii_check 21 → 29; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `src/attribute_validator.rs` (`cancel_unsafe_until` in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`), `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` (`#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` on `File.write`), `src/raii_check.rs` (new `StateViolation` + walker + collector; ~470 LOC net), `src/cli.rs` (state-violation `note:` line in two text-emission sites + state-violation JSON/JSONL serialization), `tests/raii_check.rs` (8 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 3a does NOT cover:** (1) `BufReader[R]` — separate sub-slice (slice 3b below) blocked on the BufReader stdlib type itself; the walker infrastructure is type-agnostic so adding BufReader is purely a stdlib annotation. (2) Branch-precise merging — `if c { f.write(); } else { f.flush(); } yield` may miss the soil in the then-branch; the v1 simplification walks both arms in source order. (3) Soiling through non-identifier receivers — `record.handle.write(...)` / `files[i].write(...)` / complex receiver shapes; only `Identifier(name).M(...)` and `self.M(...)` participate. (4) Soiling propagation across function calls — a helper that takes `f: mut ref File` and writes to it is not re-walked from the caller's flow state; effect-typed propagation is a separate slice. (5) Stdlib `sync_all` as an alternative clear method — only one clear-method-name per soil at v1 (the attribute is `method = "flush"`, not `methods = [...]`); a multi-clear shape can land later if a stdlib surface needs it.
     2. [ ] **Slice 3b — `BufReader[R]` flow-sensitive seeding.** Depends on the `BufReader[R]` entry in [phase-8-stdlib-floor.md](phase-8-stdlib-floor.md) (Pre-existing Phase 8 work, line ~98) shipping. Walker infrastructure is in place after slice 3a — this sub-slice just adds the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(...)]` annotation to BufReader's buffer-soiling methods (`fill_buf` once the buffer is non-empty; `read_line` / `read_to_string` between calls that leave residual bytes — exact soiling-method set TBD when BufReader lands) and tests the same Soil→Clear→Yield round-trip shape from slice 3a. Likely also needs a "drain" clear method on BufReader if `consume`-then-`fill_buf` isn't a clean reset. Carry until BufReader is the v1 surface.
  4. [x] **Slice 4 — raw-pointer detection shipped 2026-05-26.** Closes the design.md v1 NOT-CancelSafe gap for `*const T` / `*mut T` — raw pointers carry no `Drop` hook, so a cancel during their live range leaks whatever they reference. **Path chosen:** option (a) from the pre-ship plan — extend the existing `pattern_binding_types` recorder rather than thread a parallel typechecker side-table. The recorder is already the canonical surface-name source for `raii_check`; adding one arm there keeps the data flow linear (typechecker → `pattern_binding_types` → state-struct layout → `is_not_cancel_safe`) and avoids splitting "what surface type is this binding?" across two tables. **Fix:** new `Type::Pointer { .. }` arm in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::bind_pattern_types` (let / parameter side) AND in `check_pattern_against` (match-arm side) — both record `type_display(ty)`, which yields `*mut T` / `*const T` (matching the surface syntax users wrote). New `is_raw_pointer_surface_name(type_name: &str) -> bool` helper in `src/raii_check.rs` checks `starts_with("*const ") || starts_with("*mut ")` (the trailing space is load-bearing — nominal type names cannot begin with `*` per the lexer, so the prefix is unambiguous). `is_not_cancel_safe` consults the helper *before* the slice-2 opt-in check — raw-pointer rejection is unconditional, the opt-in does not apply (its walker only matches single-segment `TypeKind::Path` targets, so `impl CancelSafe for *const T` wouldn't register even if a user wrote one). **Help-text branching:** `RaiiAcrossYieldError::help()` now branches on raw-pointer-ness — for raw pointers, the message omits the misleading `impl CancelSafe for X` suggestion (raw pointers have no `Drop` to audit) and instead points at safe-handle conversion (`ref`/`mut ref` borrow, `Box[T]`, or a Kāra-side wrapper). **5 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 4` section: `fn driver(p: *const u8)` held across yield → rejected; `fn driver(p: *mut u32)` → rejected; help-text class-branching → asserts the raw-pointer help does NOT contain "impl CancelSafe" AND DOES contain "safe handle"; named-type CancelSafe opt-in does NOT transitively cover raw pointers to that type (`impl CancelSafe for Cell {}` + `fn driver(p: *const Cell)` still rejects — pins the `is_raw_pointer_surface_name` check running before the opt-in check, and also documents that pointer-target opt-ins are not a slice-2 form); `Vec[*const u8]` is NOT in scope (binding type is `Vec`, the recorder doesn't recurse into element types — documents the scope limit). **Empirical verification:** smoke-tested `fn driver(p: *const u8) { fetch(); }` parses + typechecks cleanly before starting — confirmed raw-pointer parameters are usable in v1 (the slice isn't moot for lack of expressivity). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries (raii_check 16 → 21; all others unchanged). Files: `src/typechecker/patterns.rs` (~25 lines net — new `Type::Pointer` arm in two parallel sites, with cross-reference comments naming `raii_check` as the consumer), `src/raii_check.rs` (~30 lines net — new `is_raw_pointer_surface_name` helper, prefix check in `is_not_cancel_safe`, class-branched `help()` body), `tests/raii_check.rs` (5 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 4 does NOT cover:** (1) transitive raw-pointer reachability — `Vec[*const T]`, `Box[*const T]`, struct fields of pointer type, etc.; the recorder doesn't recurse and `raii_check`'s walk only sees top-level binding surface names. A separate sub-slice would extend `is_not_cancel_safe` to walk `pattern_binding_inner_types` for element-typed containers AND walk struct definitions for pointer-typed fields. (2) function-pointer types (`fn(...) -> ...` / `Fn(...) -> ...`) — these are `Type::Function` / `Type::OnceFunction`, not `Type::Pointer`; the spec doesn't classify them as raw pointers and the v1 cancel-safety contract for closures lives in a separate slice if/when surfaced. (3) raw-pointer types constructed via `ptr.null()` / `ptr.const(value)` — only the parameter / let-binding shape was exercised; the let-binding path lights up automatically once `bind_pattern_types` records the type, but no end-to-end tests of raw-pointer construction were added.
  5. [x] **Slice 5 — precise binding-construction span anchoring shipped 2026-05-26.** Slice 1 anchored the diagnostic only at the yield-point span and named the binding in the message body, leaving users to scan upward for where `self` / `h` / `tx` was introduced. **Implementation:** `SpanKey` (`(offset, length)`) is lossy — line/column can't be reconstructed from it, so the walker carries the full `Span` in parallel rather than reconstructing from the existing `span_key`. New `binding_span: Option<crate::token::Span>` field on `ScopeEntry` (`src/cli.rs`), populated at every push site: param (line 1722), `let` pattern, `let-uninit` `name_span`, `let-else` pattern, `if-let` / `while-let` / `for` patterns via `walk_block_with_pattern`, match-arm body bindings via `walk_expr_with_pattern`, and match-arm guard bindings. `self` keeps `binding_span: None` — `SelfParam` is the `Owned`/`Ref`/`MutRef` enum with no Span, mirroring the existing `span_key: None` convention. `record_yield_point_capture` clones the span into a new `StateStructField.binding_span: Option<Span>` field; codegen's two fixed-shape `StateStructField` builders in `src/codegen/declarations.rs:58-66` (the `park_on_fd` synthesised layout) set `binding_span: None` — codegen ignores the field, it's diagnostic-only. `RaiiAcrossYieldError` gains `binding_span: Option<Span>`, populated from `field.binding_span.clone()` in `check_raii_across_yield`. **cli.rs emission (all three output paths):** plain text (post-typecheck error pass + `cmd_run` short-circuit) adds `eprintln!("  note: binding declared here at {filename}:{line}:{col}")` between the primary error line and the help line when `binding_span` is `Some`; JSON `DiagEntry` attaches `extra_json: Some("\"binding_span\":{...}")` via the existing `extra_json` infrastructure (the entry-object writer prepends the leading `,`); JSONL `diagnostic` event appends `,"binding_span":{file,line,column}` to the event payload when present. **4 new tests** in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 5` section: parameter shape (`fn driver(h: Hub)`) — span anchors at the `h` token, asserted by character-at-(line,column) lookup so the assertion stays robust against minor source rewrites; `let` shape (`let h: Hub = make()`) — span at the `h` in the `let` pattern; `self` receiver — `binding_span` stays `None` (synthetic-binding contract); match-arm shape (`Held(h) => { fetch(); }`) — span at the `h` in the arm pattern, with the outer `s: Slot` parameter producing a separate error filtered out via `binding_name` lookup. **Discovered constraints during test authoring:** (1) Kara match arms use bare-variant syntax `Held(h) => ...` not the qualified `Slot::Held(h) => ...` form; (2) `pub fn make() -> Hub` triggers `E_PRIVATE_TYPE_IN_PUBLIC_SIGNATURE` for a non-pub shared struct — tests use non-pub helper fns. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (raii_check 12 → 16; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `src/ast.rs` (new `binding_span` field on `StateStructField`), `src/cli.rs` (`ScopeEntry.binding_span` + 7 push-site updates + 3 emission-site updates), `src/codegen/declarations.rs` (2 fixed-shape builders updated to `binding_span: None`), `src/raii_check.rs` (`RaiiAcrossYieldError.binding_span` + populate from `field.binding_span`), `tests/raii_check.rs` (4 new tests + slice section comment). **What slice 5 does NOT cover:** binding-state-change spans for slice 3's flow-sensitive case (e.g. "last `.write()` was here, no `.flush()` before yield") — those land alongside slice 3 if at all; the diagnostic uses a `note:` line in plain output rather than a structured secondary-span highlight (no codebase-wide secondary-span infrastructure exists today, so the slice follows the existing `note:` convention).

- [ ] **P0 — Flagship Demo 1: minimal HTTP+WebSocket server.** Smallest possible HTTP server that holds 1M+ idle WebSocket connections under HTTPS. Used as the M1 / M2 / M3 verification gate (line 132 above — M1/M2/M3 sub-entries reference this demo as their verification artifact, and `CI benchmark gate on flagship demo` at line 136 wires CI against the bench harness from slice 3 below). Lives in `examples/ws_idle_holder/` (multi-file project shape — `kara.toml` + `src/main.kara`, mirroring `examples/parallax_lite/`); CI benchmark suite runs against the slice 3 bench harness.

  **Two hard prereqs, both tracked as their own entries below in this file:** the `spawn() / TaskGroup runtime + codegen + stdlib` entry (canonical accept-loop shape requires `loop { let conn = listener.accept()?; group.spawn(|| handle(conn)) }` per design.md § Explicit Concurrency), and the `TLS / HTTPS server-side stdlib` entry (the demo's spec says "under HTTPS" — plaintext `ws://` is acceptable for slice 1 to surface runtime issues early, but slice 2 ships TLS before any M1 number is published).

  1. [ ] **Slice 1 — skeleton kara program (plaintext `ws://`).** Smallest viable demo source: bind a `TcpListener`, run an accept loop that calls `TaskGroup.spawn(|| handle_connection(conn))` per accept, and the per-task handler does the WebSocket upgrade + reads frames in a recv loop until the peer disconnects. Plaintext `ws://` only; TLS is slice 2. Smoke-test against `websocat` and against a small kara client. **Blocked by:** the `spawn() / TaskGroup runtime + codegen + stdlib` entry below — slices 1–5 of that entry (stdlib types, ScopeLocal enforcement, runtime scheduler pool, codegen spawn-call lowering, TaskGroup join+cancel on drop) must all ship before this slice can compile and run. The demo source change once that entry lands is minimal (swap `TcpListener.bind` for `TlsListener.bind_tls(addr, cert, key)` and the rest of the WebSocket upgrade flows through unchanged because slice 9e.2's `WebSocket.accept(listener)` is parameterised on listener type).
