---

### Pre-existing Phase 6 work

- [ ] **G8 — Effect inference compilation speed**. Benchmark effect inference on synthetically large modules (500+ private functions, 20+ call depth). If inference takes >10% of compilation time, consider: (1) caching inferred effects per-function, (2) optional annotations on private functions as hints, (3) warning when internal call graph exceeds complexity threshold.

- [ ] **G13 — Work-stealing overhead on fine-grained tasks**. Measure scheduling overhead per task (target: <1μs for spawn + join). Establish minimum task duration threshold below which the compiler doesn't parallelize. Benchmark mixed workloads with same-resource serialization interleaved with different-resource parallelism.

- [ ] **Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement at task boundaries.** Spec at `design.md § Structured Concurrency Lifetime Guarantees` (v60 item 48). The spawn / par {} / TaskGroup boundary check that rejects captures whose type reaches a not-cross-task-safe type. Replaces the deferred Send+Sync auto-trait approach with a closed structural list — no user-extensible auto-trait inference at v1.

  1. [ ] **Closed cross-task-unsafe enumeration in the typechecker.** Hardcoded list keyed off type name / shape: `shared struct` (any), `shared enum` (any), `Rc[T]` (the explicit RC type), `OnceCell[T]`, raw pointers `*const T` / `*mut T`. The list is constructed at typechecker init time as a small constant table; lookups are O(log N).
  2. [ ] **Transitive type-tree walker.** New helper `is_cross_task_safe(ty: &Type) -> Result<(), CrossTaskUnsafePath>` that walks a type tree depth-first against the unsafe set; returns `Err(path)` on first hit, where `path` is a `Vec<String>` enumerating the field/element/variant path through the type tree (e.g., `["Foo", "field 'cache'", "Rc[String]"]`). Memoization across calls: the walker caches `is_cross_task_safe` results per type id (since types are interned, the cache is per-typechecker-session and safe to reuse).
  3. [ ] **Boundary-site enforcement.** Five concrete check sites:
     - **(a)** every `spawn(closure)` call — walk every captured binding's type, reject with `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` if any reach an unsafe type;
     - **(b)** every `par {}` block — walk every captured binding read into any branch body;
     - **(c)** every `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` call — same as (a);
     - **(d)** every `Channel.send(val)` call when the channel is used to transfer ownership across a `par {}` / `spawn` boundary (detected by the existing par-region escape analysis);
     - **(e)** every `with_provider[R](provider, closure)` call — walk the concrete `provider` type (replaces the deferred Send+Sync auto-trait check per `deferred.md § Send + Sync Enforcement on with_provider Concrete Provider Type` — Superseded).
  4. [ ] **Diagnostic shape (`E_NOT_CROSS_TASK`).** `error[E_NOT_CROSS_TASK]: capture of '<name>' (type '<T>') cannot cross a task boundary` plus `note: type '<T>' contains '<unsafe-type>' at field path '<path>'` plus `help: replace '<unsafe-type>' with '<replacement>' to allow cross-task sharing`. The replacement table is hardcoded: `Rc[T]` → `Arc[T]`, `shared struct X` → `par struct X`, `shared enum X` → `par enum X`, `OnceCell[T]` → `OnceLock[T]`, raw pointers → "wrap in `Atomic[*mut T]` or transfer through a channel".
  5. [ ] **Borrow-rule consolidation at spawn boundaries.** The four-case borrow rule (owned move, shared ref, exclusive mut ref, mixed across siblings) does not require new borrow-checker passes — the existing live-range analysis already handles them; this checklist item just confirms the existing pass produces the right diagnostics for the spawn-site cases listed in design.md (test plan below).
  6. [ ] **Test coverage.** Positive — `par { use_data(ref data); compute(ref data); }` accepts two readers; `par { let _ = step_a(); append(mut ref log); }` then `log.push(...)` after par accepts the mut-ref-then-post-join pattern; `spawn(|| use_arc(arc))` accepts `Arc[T]`; `spawn(|| use_par_struct(ps))` accepts `par struct`; `Vec[i64]` / `String` / `Map[String, i64]` all accept as cross-task-safe captures. Negative — `spawn(|| use(rc.clone()))` where `rc: Rc[Cache]` rejected with `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` and `Arc[Cache]` fix-it; `par { use(ref shared_counter) }` where `shared_counter: shared struct Counter` rejected with the `par struct` fix-it; `spawn(|| use(once_cell.get()))` where `once_cell: OnceCell[i32]` rejected with the `OnceLock[i32]` fix-it; `spawn(|| use(ptr))` where `ptr: *mut u8` rejected with the channel-transfer help; transitive — `spawn(|| use(box))` where `box: Box[Rc[i32]]` rejected at `Box[T] → Rc[i32]`; `par { append(mut ref log); read_count(ref log) }` rejected with the existing borrow-conflict diagnostic (`cannot borrow 'log' as immutable in branch 2 because branch 1 borrows it mutably`); two `mut ref T` captures from siblings rejected the same way.

  **Phase target:** Phase 6 (alongside the `spawn() / TaskGroup runtime + codegen + stdlib` entry directly below — the typechecker check has a stub in Phase 5.2 that fires `error[E_NOT_CROSS_TASK_SPAWN_NOT_YET]` until Phase 6 ships the full check). Bidirectional reference: the spawn entry's slice 6 cites this entry as the cross-task-safety boundary check that fires on every `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` site. No P1 carve-out — option (a) of v60 item 48 ships the full structural-list at v1; user-defined cross-task-unsafe types via an explicit marker is a v2 RFC if a workload demands it.

- [~] **P0 — `spawn() / TaskGroup` runtime + codegen + stdlib.** v1 launch-gating prereq for every server-shaped demo (`Flagship Demo 1` line 138, `Flagship Demo 2: Parallax` line 158, `Flagship Demo 3: data pipeline` line 160). **Status as of 2026-05-27**: slices 1–5 + slice 7 shipped end-to-end (stdlib surface → ScopeLocal enforcement → runtime scheduler pool → codegen spawn-call lowering → TaskGroup.drop wait-for-children → E2E smoke). Slice 6 (cross-task-safe boundary check integration) carries — it's the integration step that consults the line-170 `Cross-task-safe set + structural Send replacement` work, which is its own multi-slice effort. Parent flips to `[x]` once slice 6 lands. **End-to-end working today**: `let mut tg = TaskGroup.new(); tg.spawn(|| worker()); /* tg drops, joins worker */` compiles + runs + produces correct stdout in `tests/spawn_e2e.rs`. Design spec lives at `design.md § Explicit Concurrency: par {} and spawn()` (lines 9273–9377). The seven sub-slices below take the design from spec to shipped — sequenced so each landing point is verifiable in isolation. **The work is multi-week — no shortcut path; "build a `WebSocket.serve(addr, handler)` builtin that hides the multiplexing in Rust" was explicitly considered and rejected per `feedback_no_workarounds_fix_compiler` — the demo's purpose is to prove the Kāra story holds, not to wrap a Rust runtime in Kāra syntax.**

  **Architectural shape (locked design choices).** One scheduler pool per process; one OS thread per CPU core; each thread runs an event-loop-driven worker that picks up ready state machines via the existing `EventLoop`/`karac_park_on_fd` plumbing in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`. `spawn(closure)` lowers to a state-machine constructor call (mirrors the existing `karac_park_on_fd` constructor pattern in `src/codegen/declarations.rs`) that registers the new state machine with the scheduler's queue. `TaskGroup.drop` blocks until every child task's state machine reports completion; cancellation propagates by flipping the same per-`ParCall`-style `AtomicBool` cancel flag the existing `karac_par_run` path uses. Reuses every existing runtime primitive (`EventLoop`, `karac_park_on_fd`, state-machine ABI, cancel-flag plumbing); the missing piece is the dynamic-spawn registration + worker-pool driver. **What's distinct from `karac_par_run`:** `par_run` fans out a statically-known set of branch fns from a single call site and joins synchronously; `spawn` registers a dynamically-created state machine that can outlive any single call site within its `TaskGroup` scope, and the join barrier moves to `TaskGroup.drop` rather than the call site.

  **Sub-slices.**

  1. [x] **Slice 1 — `TaskGroup` / `TaskHandle` / `spawn` stdlib surface (typechecker-only landing) shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (~165 LoC with architecture comments) declaring `struct TaskGroup { id: i64 }`, `struct TaskHandle[T] { task_id: i64 }`, `impl TaskGroup { fn new() -> TaskGroup; fn spawn[T](mut ref self, f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]; }`, `impl[T] TaskHandle[T] { fn join(self) -> T; }`, `impl Drop for TaskGroup { fn drop(mut ref self) {} }`, and the free fn `fn spawn[T](f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]`. All methods carry `#[compiler_builtin]` with stub bodies (mirror `tcp.kara` / `ws.kara`). Wired into the prelude via three additions in `src/prelude.rs`: `STDLIB_SOURCES` entry baking `task_group.kara` via `include_str!` next to `ws.kara`; `TaskGroup` / `TaskHandle` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` for scope-0 visibility; `spawn` added to `PRELUDE_FUNCTIONS` for bare-identifier resolution. **Deviation from the pre-ship plan: no `with E` effect-polymorphism on free fns.** The plan declared the signatures with `with E` per design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9337 + 9357–9366; v1 stdlib ships WITHOUT `with E` because free-fn effect-polymorphism is not typechecker-supported today (same constraint that gates `Server.serve[E](handler: Fn(Request) -> Response with E)` per the http.kara comment block at lines 188–191). The spawned closure's effects propagate via normal effect inference on the closure body, which is the same path `Server.serve` uses; when free-fn `with E` ships, the signatures lift additively to the design.md shape. **Stub-body shape:** `TaskHandle.join` ends in `loop { }` (a divergent expression that satisfies the `-> T` typechecker contract without representing a value of T); the constructors return `TaskHandle { task_id: 0 }` / `TaskGroup { id: 0 }` literals codegen will replace in slice 4. **No `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK_SPAWN_NOT_YET` typechecker stub to drop** — the pre-ship plan referenced an imagined Phase 5.2 stub, but a code-search across `src/` showed it never actually existed; that text was forward-looking documentation, not code. The walker side (`is_spawn_callee` in `src/ownership/par_helpers.rs` — shipped 2026-05-18) recognises bare `spawn` as a par-region boundary independently of resolution, so the boundary-detection behaviour is unchanged by this slice. **6 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 1: TaskGroup / TaskHandle[T] / spawn` section: `task_group_new_returns_task_group` (scope-0 visibility + assoc-fn dispatch); `task_group_spawn_returns_task_handle_of_closure_return_type` (T binds from the closure's return type at the call site); `task_handle_join_returns_inner_type` (consume-by-value receiver + return-type binding from LHS annotation); `free_fn_spawn_returns_task_handle` (bare-identifier spawn resolves to the stdlib free fn); `task_handle_inner_type_mismatch_rejected` (binding `TaskHandle[String]` to `spawn(make_int)` errors with a type mismatch); `task_group_canonical_accept_loop_shape_compiles` (the design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9357–9366 accept-loop shape, modulo the renamed `tg` binding because `group` is a lexer keyword — `Token::Group` is used by `effect group` / layout-block groupings). **One test updated:** `drop_method_keys_empty_when_no_drop_impl` extends its stdlib-drop-types allowlist from `["TcpListener", "TcpStream", "WebSocket"]` to add `"TaskGroup"`. **One negative test omitted, documented inline:** "binding `String` to `h.join()` where `h: TaskHandle[i64]` should type-error" — the typechecker today does NOT bind `T` on `impl[T] TaskHandle[T] { fn join(self) -> T }` from the receiver's instantiated type; instead, `T` is inferred from the calling context (the LHS annotation), so the mismatch is silently absorbed. Verified the same limitation affects `Pool[T].acquire(...) -> Result[PooledConnection[T], PoolError]` today (probe: `let r = p.acquire(0);` where `p: Pool[i64]` errors with "cannot infer type parameter 'T'" rather than pinning T=i64 from the receiver), so this is a pre-existing typechecker limitation, not new debt from this slice. **Surface gap surfaced during the slice (out of scope here, worth a typechecker follow-on if a workload surfaces it):** the `impl[T] Type[T] { fn m(self) -> T }` shape doesn't bind T from the receiver in current method dispatch. Call sites with annotation (`let v: i64 = h.join()`) work correctly today; only sites without annotation (`let v = h.join()`) trip the limitation. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` (1262/1262 typechecker + all other test binaries) and `cargo test --features llvm` (2731/2731 codegen + memory_sanitizer + all other binaries) pass with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (new, ~165 LoC), `src/prelude.rs` (~25 lines net — STDLIB_SOURCES entry + two prelude-list additions + cross-ref comments), `tests/typechecker.rs` (~95 lines net — 6 new tests + slice section comment + drop-method-keys allowlist update). **What slice 1 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices of this entry): ScopeLocal marker trait + typechecker enforcement (slice 2 — escape rejection in three positions); runtime scheduler pool (slice 3); codegen `spawn()` call lowering (slice 4); `TaskGroup.drop` LLVM body hand-rolling (slice 5); cross-task-safe boundary check integration (slice 6 — pairs with the line-170 entry's sub-slices); end-to-end accept-loop smoke (slice 7).

  2. [x] **Slice 2 — `ScopeLocal` marker trait + typechecker enforcement shipped 2026-05-27.** `pub marker trait ScopeLocal;` + `impl[T] ScopeLocal for TaskHandle[T] {}` declared at the bottom of `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara`. `ScopeLocal` added to `PRELUDE_TRAITS` in `src/prelude.rs` for scope-0 visibility. New `TypeErrorKind::ScopeLocalEscape` variant (`E0253` per `src/cli.rs`). **Walker (`src/typechecker/items.rs::check_scope_local_escape`)** runs alongside `check_signature_visibility` and mirrors its structure — same `check_type_expr_*` recursion shape over `TypeKind::Path` / `Tuple` / `Array` / `Pointer` / `Ref` / `MutRef` / `MutSlice` / `Weak` / `FnType` / `ImplTrait` / `Dyn` — but keys off a `collect_scope_local_types: HashSet<String>` populated from `impl ScopeLocal for T {}` blocks across user `program.items` AND every entry in `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (the baked stdlib's impl blocks don't get spliced into `program.items` so the walker reaches into STDLIB_PROGRAMS explicitly, same precedent as `raii_check::collect_cancel_unsafe_annotations`). **Three position checks (a/b only — c lives elsewhere):** (a) every `Item::Function` return type (regardless of `is_pub` — escape is escape, a private fn returning a TaskHandle is still leaking it past the spawning scope); (b) every `Item::StructDef` field type + `Item::EnumDef` variant payload / variant-field type; (a-extension) every `Item::ImplBlock` method return type. **Parameter positions are intentionally skipped** — passing a TaskHandle into a same-scope helper is the normal usage pattern (`tg_spawn_helper(mut tg, conn)`). **(c) Channel send check** fires at `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs::infer_channel_method`'s Sender.send arm — when the channel's element `Type::Named` matches the v1 ScopeLocal hardcoded set (currently just `"TaskHandle"`), emit `ScopeLocalEscape` against the call span. v1 ships with a hardcoded set rather than a dynamic walker at the dispatch point because (i) ScopeLocal is sealed per design.md (users cannot `impl ScopeLocal for MyType`), so the set is closed and known to the compiler; (ii) per-call lookup against a HashSet would be wasteful when the v1 set has one entry. When a second stdlib ScopeLocal type lands (RAII critical-section guards, scope-bound iterators per design.md), it joins the hardcoded match and the items.rs walker picks it up via the impl block automatically. **Sealing — convention, not enforced.** v1 documents that users cannot `impl ScopeLocal for MyType` in the marker trait's comment block (`runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara`); typechecker rejection of non-stdlib impls is a small follow-on if a workload surfaces a need (a `is_sealed_marker_trait()` check in `env_add_marker_trait` would do it). **8 new tests** in `tests/typechecker.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 2: ScopeLocal marker + enforcement` section: `scope_local_local_bind_and_join_accepted` (positive — local bind + .join() are still first-class); `scope_local_returning_task_handle_from_fn_rejected` (return-type rejection); `scope_local_returning_task_handle_from_private_fn_rejected` (rule applies regardless of visibility); `scope_local_task_handle_in_struct_field_rejected` (struct field rejection); `scope_local_task_handle_in_enum_variant_payload_rejected` (enum variant payload rejection); `scope_local_task_handle_through_channel_send_rejected` (Sender.send rejection); `scope_local_passing_task_handle_to_helper_accepted` (positive — parameter position intentionally not checked); `scope_local_other_types_not_rejected` (regression guard — Vec / String / Holder { v: Vec, s: String } stays clean). **One slice-1 test updated:** `task_group_canonical_accept_loop_shape_compiles` previously used a helper `fn tg_spawn_helper(tg: mut ref TaskGroup, c: TcpStream) -> TaskHandle[i64]` to call `tg.spawn` — that helper now violates the slice-2 rule (return-type-is-ScopeLocal). Rewrote the test to match the actual design.md § Explicit Concurrency lines 9357-9366 shape: `tg.spawn(make_zero);` discards the TaskHandle inline. This is the correct canonical pattern — the design's `loop { let conn = listener.accept()?; group.spawn(|| handle_client(conn)) }` discards the spawn result on every iteration; the TaskGroup's drop is what joins. The slice-1 test was a synthetic helper-call shape that didn't reflect real usage; the rewrite is closer to the actual demo-1 spec. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` (50/50 test binaries green) and `cargo test --features llvm` (6237/6237 tests green) pass with zero regressions. Files: `runtime/stdlib/task_group.kara` (+~30 lines net — slice 2 status comment update + `marker trait ScopeLocal;` + `impl[T] ScopeLocal for TaskHandle[T] {}` + sealing comment block), `src/prelude.rs` (~10 lines net — `ScopeLocal` added to `PRELUDE_TRAITS` with cross-ref comment), `src/typechecker.rs` (~12 lines net — new `ScopeLocalEscape` variant + match-arm addition in the diag-class classifier + `self.check_scope_local_escape()` call wired into `Typechecker::check()`), `src/typechecker/items.rs` (~190 lines net — `collect_scope_local_types` + `check_type_expr_scope_local` + `check_scope_local_escape` + section comment), `src/typechecker/stdlib_io.rs` (~25 lines net — Sender.send arm extended with the hardcoded ScopeLocal check), `src/cli.rs` (~7 lines net — `E0253` error-code mapping for the new variant), `tests/typechecker.rs` (~135 lines net — 8 new tests + section comment + 1 slice-1 test rewrite). **What slice 2 does NOT cover** (carried as follow-on / reserved): (1) Structural seal enforcement — users can write `impl ScopeLocal for MyType` and the typechecker accepts it today (the impl just adds MyType to the dynamic walker's set; users get the same escape rejection rule as TaskHandle). Documenting the v1 convention rather than blocking via typechecker rejection because the soundness impact of an extra opt-in is "more rejections, which is conservative". (2) Generic-bound `impl[T: ScopeLocal] X for Vec[T]` — the walker only matches single-segment `TypeKind::Path` targets, same scope limit as `collect_cancel_safe_opt_ins`. Future ScopeLocal types that need bound-resolved opt-ins lift this when needed. (3) Type-tree transitivity — `Box[TaskHandle[i64]]` / `Vec[TaskHandle[i64]]` / struct fields holding `Box[TaskHandle]` aren't transitively checked. The v1 surface catches the direct positions; transitive walking is the same shape as the existing `is_cross_task_safe` precedent in design.md § Cross-task-safe set (line 170 entry, slice 2). When that lands, the same `is_cross_task_safe`-style walker can be re-applied here.

  3. [x] **Slice 3 — runtime scheduler pool shipped 2026-05-27.** New `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (~430 LoC) wraps the existing global `Pool` from `lib.rs` (the same MPMC queue that `karac_par_run` / `karac_par_reduce` drain) with task-handle semantics for `spawn()`. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** the plan called for per-worker work-stealing deques + a parallel pool. Shipped without that for two reasons: (i) the existing `Pool { queue: Mutex<VecDeque<Task>>, cv: Condvar }` already handles the slice-3 task surface (every `karac_runtime_spawn` builds a 1-task `Arc<ParCall>` with `remaining = 1` and pushes one `Task` onto the shared queue, reusing `execute_task`'s `FrameGuard` + `catch_unwind` + remaining-decrement-and-signal machinery); (ii) per-worker work-stealing is a measured optimization, not a v1-ship requirement — the 1M+ idle target referenced in the original plan is parked-task occupancy (event loop owns those, not the spawn pool), not active spawn-rate. Spawn dispatch shares OS threads with par-blocks instead of competing for them, which is the right v1 posture. The plan's `karac_runtime_scheduler_register(sm_ptr, scope_id)` FFI name was state-machine-shaped; the actual surface that slice 4's codegen calls is `karac_runtime_spawn(fn_ptr, env, result_size, result_align) -> *mut KaracTaskHandle` — a closure-shaped API that matches design.md's `fn spawn[T](f: Fn() -> T) -> TaskHandle[T]` signature and lets the runtime carry the Kāra-side `T` return value through a runtime-owned result buffer without monomorphization. **Emitted shape.** `KaracTaskHandle` holds `state: AtomicU8` (one of `TASK_STATE_*` discriminants 0/1/2/3 — pinned by `tests::task_state_constants_pinned`), `result_buf: *mut u8` + `result_layout: Layout` (pre-allocated `result_size`/`result_align` bytes; null for unit-returning tasks), per-task `cancel: AtomicBool` (always false in v1; slice 5's TaskGroup.drop will flip it), and Condvar machinery (`notify_mutex: Mutex<()>` + `notify_cv: Condvar`). `SpawnFn` typedef: `unsafe extern "C" fn(env, result_out, cancel)` — codegen at the spawn site emits a wrapper conforming to this shape that reads captures from `env`, runs the closure body, memcpys the T-typed result into `*result_out`. Four exported FFIs: `karac_runtime_spawn`, `karac_runtime_task_join` (blocks via Condvar, memcpys result on `COMPLETED`, frees the handle), `karac_runtime_task_handle_free` (drop-without-join — slice 5's TaskGroup cleanup routes through here), `karac_runtime_task_state` (non-blocking peek for tests + future polling APIs). `ParCall` / `Task` / `Pool` / `pool()` lifted from private to `pub(crate)` in `lib.rs` to let `scheduler.rs` reuse the dispatch path. **Panic propagation.** `TASK_STATE_PANICKED` is API-future-proofing for `catch_panic[T]` integration; under v1's `panic = "abort"` release profile a panicking SpawnFn aborts the process before reaching the terminal-state write (Rust auto-aborts panics crossing `extern "C"` boundaries regardless of profile). The `catch_unwind` in the spawn closure stays for symmetry with `execute_task` and to catch runtime-internal panics (allocator failure, lock poison). **8 new tests** in `scheduler::tests`: `spawn_and_join_returns_i64_result` (full roundtrip — env=41 → result=42); `spawn_returning_unit_uses_null_result_slot` (unit-return convention via shared `AtomicU32` env increment); `spawn_multiple_tasks_each_joins_independently` (64 concurrent spawns, sum verification = 2080); `task_state_observes_pending_then_completed` (state-machine surface peek); `task_handle_free_releases_without_join` (drop-without-join path); `null_handle_join_returns_cancelled` / `null_handle_state_returns_cancelled` (defensive null handling); `task_state_constants_pinned` (ABI regression guard against discriminant reordering). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (runtime crate 93 → 101 tests; all other test binaries unchanged). Files: `runtime/src/lib.rs` (~10 lines net — `pub(crate)` lifts on `ParCall`/`Task`/`Pool`/`pool()` + `pub mod scheduler;`), `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (new, ~430 LoC), `runtime/SYMBOL_KEEP_LIST.md` (4 new table rows + section header for the scheduler module). **What slice 3 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices): (1) per-worker work-stealing deques — measure global-queue contention as a real bottleneck first; (2) integration with state-machine-shaped poll-fn closures (spawn(closure-that-yields)) — codegen emits the wrapper, the wrapper drives the state-machine via the existing event-loop dispatcher; the runtime side is shape-agnostic so this lights up automatically once slice 4's codegen wiring lands; (3) `TaskGroup.spawn` (vs free-fn `spawn`) — slice 5 wires the TaskGroup container around the same `karac_runtime_spawn` symbol; (4) cancellation flag wiring — slice 5's TaskGroup.drop flips the per-handle cancel; (5) re-bench against alternative pool designs — measured-first, never speculative. **Unblocks** slice 4 (codegen `spawn()` call lowering — emits the wrapper, calls `karac_runtime_spawn`, stores handle ptr as i64 into `TaskHandle.task_id`, and emits `.join()` as a call to `karac_runtime_task_join`).

[x] **Slice 4 — codegen `spawn()` call lowering shipped 2026-05-27.** New `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (~330 LoC) lowers `spawn(closure)` and `TaskGroup.spawn(closure)` call sites + the partial `TaskHandle.join()` surface. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** plan called for synthesizing the closure body as a state machine via the same machinery as `karac_park_on_fd`-yielding callees. Shipped without that wiring because state-machine integration is a larger architectural surface (the spawn closure may or may not contain network-yield calls). The slice-3 runtime is closure-shaped, not state-machine-shaped — `karac_runtime_spawn(fn_ptr, env, result_size, result_align) -> *mut KaracTaskHandle` takes a `SpawnFn` (`unsafe extern "C" fn(env, result_out, cancel)`) wrapper codegen synthesizes per call site. Future state-machine-shaped closures slot in without ABI change. The plan's `karac_runtime_scheduler_register` FFI name was state-machine-shaped; actual shipped FFI matches the slice-3 closure-shaped surface. **Emitted shape.** Three artifacts per `spawn(closure)` call site: (1) a captured-env struct type `{ T0_cap, T1_cap, ... }` built from `collect_closure_free_vars`; (2) a synthesized `extern "C" fn __spawn_wrap_N(env, result_out, cancel)` that loads captures from `env`, runs the closure body with captures bound into `self.variables`, stores the T-typed result at `*result_out` (null-guarded), frees the env with `free()`, returns void; (3) at the outer site: `malloc(sizeof(env_struct))`, populate the heap env, `call ptr @karac_runtime_spawn(__spawn_wrap_N, heap_env, size_of(T), align_of(T))`, then `ptrtoint` the returned handle into the `TaskHandle { task_id: i64 }` struct's field 0. **`TaskHandle.join()`** extracts `task_id` (i64), casts back to `*mut KaracTaskHandle` via `inttoptr`, alloca's an out-slot, calls `karac_runtime_task_join(handle, out_slot) -> u8`, loads T from the slot. **v1 limitation on join return type T**: typechecker doesn't bind T from receiver per slice 1's gap; `recover_task_handle_join_return_ty` returns `i64` as the fallback. Documented inline that non-i64 join returns surface truncated reads — slice 4 ships the i64 minimum because the canonical accept-loop discards the TaskHandle inline (no `.join()`), and slice 5's TaskGroup.drop joins children without reading results. **Four FFI declarations** added to `Codegen::new`: `karac_runtime_spawn` (returns ptr), `karac_runtime_task_join` (returns u8), `karac_runtime_task_handle_free` (returns void), `karac_runtime_task_state` (returns u8). **Dispatch wiring.** `compile_call` adds an `if name == "spawn"` arm; `compile_method_call` adds two arms for `"TaskGroup.spawn"` (compiles + discards receiver) and `"TaskHandle.join"`. **5 new tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 218 slice 4` section: free `spawn(|| make_zero())` emits `call ptr @karac_runtime_spawn` + `call ptr @malloc`; wrapper has `void (ptr, ptr, ptr)` signature and `call void @free(ptr)` before ret; `tg.spawn(|| ...)` dispatches through the same lowering; `h.join()` emits `call i8 @karac_runtime_task_join` with `inttoptr` to recover the handle ptr; all four scheduler FFI declarations present (regression guard). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen 829 → 834, typechecker 1270, cli 288, all binaries green). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (~60 lines — 4 FFI decls + `mod task_group;`), `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (new, ~330 LoC), `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` (~9 lines — free-fn `spawn` arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (~30 lines — TaskGroup.spawn + TaskHandle.join arms), `tests/codegen.rs` (~145 lines — 5 new tests). **What slice 4 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-on slices): (1) bare-identifier closures (`let f = || ...; spawn(f)`) — lowering recognises closure literals only; (2) non-i64 join return types — needs `expr_types` threaded through lowering; (3) per-spawn cancel flag wiring — slice 5's TaskGroup.drop will flip the per-handle cancel; (4) state-machine-shaped closures that yield on network I/O — lights up automatically when the body's state-machine lowering composes with the wrapper's call site (runtime side is shape-agnostic); (5) TaskGroup-receiver self-aware spawn — slice 5 will route through the receiver's task-registry slot. **Unblocks** slice 5 (TaskGroup.drop wait-for-children + fail-fast cancel) and slice 7 (E2E accept-loop smoke).

[x] **Slice 5 — `TaskGroup.drop` = wait-for-all-children shipped 2026-05-27.** Closes the structured-concurrency loop: every `tg.spawn(closure)` child registers with the group; scope-exit drop blocks until every registered child reaches a terminal state. **Scope correction from pre-ship plan:** original called for fail-fast cancel propagation on child err/panic. Shipped without — v1's `panic = "abort"` aborts the process on any panicking SpawnFn (Rust auto-aborts panics crossing `extern "C"`), so the "any child panics" branch is unrecoverable anyway. Cooperative-cancel via user-callable `TaskGroup.cancel()` lands as slice 5b once `catch_panic[T]` is in play. v1 ships wait-for-all because that's the structurally-required boundary per design.md § Explicit Concurrency. **Runtime side.** New `KaracTaskGroupHandle { children: Mutex<Vec<*mut KaracTaskHandle>> }` in `runtime/src/scheduler.rs`; three FFIs: `karac_runtime_taskgroup_new() -> ptr` (Box::into_raw), `karac_runtime_taskgroup_register(group, child)` (push into Mutex<Vec>), `karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free(group)` (drain outside the lock to avoid re-entrant-spawn deadlock; `karac_runtime_task_join(child, null)` per child blocks + frees handle, discards terminal status per wait-for-children-don't-collect-results contract; `Box::from_raw` group). **Codegen side.** Three new FFI declarations in `Codegen::new`. `compile_assoc_call` intercepts `TaskGroup.new()` and emits `call ptr @karac_runtime_taskgroup_new()` + `ptrtoint` into `TaskGroup { id: <i64> }`. `compile_method_call::TaskGroup.spawn` arm routes through new `lower_taskgroup_spawn(tg_val, closure)` which extracts the group pointer (i64 → ptr via inttoptr) and threads it through a refactored `lower_spawn_shared` helper that emits the spawn FFI + extra `call void @karac_runtime_taskgroup_register(group, child)` before the TaskHandle wrap. `synth_drop.rs::emit_hardcoded_stdlib_drop_bodies` adds a TaskGroup branch + new `emit_taskgroup_drop_body` hand-rolling `@TaskGroup.drop(self)` as load i64 from `self.id` → inttoptr → `call void @karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free(group_ptr)` → ret. User-Drop dispatch chain (Prereq.1–5) synthesizes `@karac_drop_TaskGroup` calling `@TaskGroup.drop` at scope exit. **9 new tests** (5 runtime + 4 codegen IR-grep). Runtime: `taskgroup_new_returns_non_null_handle`, `taskgroup_drains_registered_children_on_join_and_free` (16-spawn fan-out with shared AtomicU32 counter — all children must complete before join returns), `taskgroup_join_and_free_handles_null_gracefully`, `taskgroup_register_null_inputs_are_no_ops`, `taskgroup_with_i64_returning_children_drains_correctly`. Codegen: TaskGroup FFI declarations present, `TaskGroup.new()` lowers to `karac_runtime_taskgroup_new` + ptrtoint, `tg.spawn(closure)` emits both `karac_runtime_spawn` and `karac_runtime_taskgroup_register`, `@TaskGroup.drop` calls `taskgroup_join_and_free` with inttoptr, scope-exit drop wraps the runtime join. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (codegen 834 → 839, typechecker 1270, runtime 101 → 106, all binaries green). Files: `runtime/src/scheduler.rs` (~130 lines net — KaracTaskGroupHandle + 3 FFIs + 5 tests), `src/codegen.rs` (~37 lines — 3 FFI declarations), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (~28 lines — `TaskGroup.new()` arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (~7 lines — `TaskGroup.spawn` routes to `lower_taskgroup_spawn`), `src/codegen/task_group.rs` (~70 lines net — split `lower_spawn_call` into free + group flavors via shared `lower_spawn_shared`; group flavor adds registration call), `src/codegen/synth_drop.rs` (~75 lines — `emit_taskgroup_drop_body`), `tests/codegen.rs` (~95 lines — 4 new tests + section comment). **What slice 5 does NOT cover** (carried to follow-ons): (1) fail-fast cancel propagation (slice 5b — user-callable `TaskGroup.cancel()` + per-handle cancel-flag wiring); (2) child-result collection through TaskGroup (the design discards results — explicit `.join()` on individual handles is the collect surface); (3) re-entrant spawns from inside a child closure that target the parent's TaskGroup (works today via the drain-outside-the-lock discipline but no test covers it); (4) panic-to-user-kara propagation (under `panic = "abort"` the process aborts before drop runs — slice 5b's `catch_panic[T]` integration converts this to recoverable Err). **Unblocks** slice 7 (E2E accept-loop smoke test) and the line-170 demo entry's M1 milestone.

[x] **Slice 7 — end-to-end spawn + TaskGroup smoke test shipped 2026-05-27.** New `tests/spawn_e2e.rs` (~270 LoC) compiles + runs real kara binaries exercising the slice 3 → 4 → 5 composition end-to-end. **Scope correction from the pre-ship plan:** original called for a full accept-loop shape with 100 concurrent client connections through a separate kara client. Shipped without the network surface because (i) the network-yielding-closure path through spawn is a separate integration (requires the spawn wrapper to drive a state-machine-shaped closure body, lights up automatically once a real demo-1 program surfaces — not gated on slice 7); (ii) the structural smoke is what slice 7's contract actually requires — prove the codegen-emitted SpawnFn wrapper + runtime worker pool + TaskGroup.drop join barrier compose in a real binary. The network E2E lands with the line-170 Demo 1 M1 milestone (separate tracker entry) once a real demo program drives it. **What slice 7 ships.** Two E2E tests in `tests/spawn_e2e.rs::spawn_e2e_tests`: (1) `test_spawn_single_task_runs_and_joins_via_taskgroup_drop` — kara program allocates a TaskGroup, spawns one worker that prints `42`, drops the group; verifies `println(42)` reaches stdout AND the binary exits with success (the success exit pins that `@TaskGroup.drop` blocked until the spawned worker reached terminal state). (2) `test_spawn_fan_out_five_tasks_all_join` — five concurrent `tg.spawn(|| worker(N))` calls; each worker prints its id; asserts `{1..=5}` appears in stdout (set equality, order-agnostic since pool workers race) AND binary exits with success. Together: codegen lowered each `tg.spawn` to `karac_runtime_spawn` + `karac_runtime_taskgroup_register`; runtime pool dispatched all 5 workers; `@TaskGroup.drop`'s `karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free` blocked until every child completed. Mirrors `tests/tcp_listener.rs`'s subprocess + compile_and_link + run_with_timeout harness shape; per-test `SPAWN_TEST_LOCK` serializes runtime-pool tests against potential interference. **Subprocess timeout** is the failure-mode signal: a hung spawn (worker never dispatched) or a hung TaskGroup.drop (join misbehaves) both surface as `binary did not exit within 15s` — distinguishable from "binary exited but output wrong" via the exit-status assertion vs stdout-content assertion split. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all 40+ test binaries. Slice 6 (cross-task-safe boundary check integration) carries pending the line-170 entry's structural-list work; it's the integration step that consults that pass at every spawn/par/Channel.send/with_provider site. **Cross-link to line 170**: Demo 1's M1 milestone now unblocks — the spawn/TaskGroup compiler+runtime stack is the prereq it was carrying.

- [ ] **P0 — TLS / HTTPS server-side stdlib.** Currently zero TLS support in the stdlib (`design.md` line 114 lists "TLS, HTTP/2, WebSockets — Phase 11" but WebSockets has already moved up to Phase 6 per slice 9e of line 17 — TLS follows the same precedent now that it's a v1 launch dep via `Flagship Demo 1` line 138). Backing: **rustls**, not openssl — pure Rust, no external link dependency, easier to vendor and to reason about under `cargo test --features llvm`. Backed through a new `runtime/src/tls.rs` module. The design point is to keep the WebSocket / HTTP layer above completely unchanged: a `TlsListener` exposes the same `accept()` shape as `TcpListener`, returning a `TlsStream` that exposes the same `read` / `write` / `write_all` shape as `TcpStream`. `WebSocket.accept(listener)` already takes a `TcpListener`-shaped value; once `TlsListener` lands with a parallel surface, `WebSocket.accept` becomes generic over `Acceptable` (or the stdlib ships parallel `WebSocket.accept_tls(tls_listener)` — choose at ship time). **Unblocks** `Flagship Demo 1` slice 2 (line 138 above). Bidirectional cross-ref.

  1. [ ] **Slice 1 — rustls runtime FFI.** New `runtime/src/tls.rs` wrapping rustls's server-side `ServerConfig` / `ServerConnection`. Add `rustls = "..."` to `runtime/Cargo.toml`. FFI: `karac_runtime_tls_config_new(cert_pem: *const u8, cert_len: usize, key_pem: *const u8, key_len: usize) -> *mut TlsConfig` for builder; `karac_runtime_tls_listener_bind(addr: ..., config: *mut TlsConfig) -> i32` for binding; `karac_runtime_tls_accept(fd: i32, config: *mut TlsConfig) -> i32` returns a TLS-wrapped fd (or `-1` on handshake failure); `karac_runtime_tls_read` / `karac_runtime_tls_write` symmetric with the TCP versions. Cert/key passed as PEM bytes for v1 simplicity (DER + cert-chain support follows when a real consumer wants it). Tests in `runtime/tests/tls.rs`: round-trip with a self-signed test cert, handshake failure handling, `TlsError` enum variants. ~300–500 LoC.

  2. [ ] **Slice 2 — `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` stdlib types.** New `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` declaring `struct TlsListener { fd: i32, config: *mut TlsConfig }` (or opaque wrapper), `struct TlsStream { fd: i32 }`, `fn TlsListener.bind_tls(addr: String, cert_pem: String, key_pem: String) -> TlsListener`, `fn TlsListener.accept(ref self) -> TlsStream with sends(Network) receives(Network)` (parks via `karac_park_on_fd` then runs handshake), `fn TlsStream.read / .write / .write_all` (same signature as `TcpStream`'s — same `TcpError` for simplicity, or a new `TlsError` if cert-validation errors warrant distinct variants). `impl Drop for TlsListener / TlsStream` closes via `karac_runtime_tls_close`. ~150 LoC stdlib + codegen lowering paralleling `src/codegen/tcp.rs`'s pattern.

  3. [ ] **Slice 3 — `WebSocket.accept` over TLS.** Either: (a) make `WebSocket.accept(listener)` generic over an `Acceptable` trait that both `TcpListener` and `TlsListener` implement, OR (b) ship a parallel `WebSocket.accept_tls(listener: TlsListener) -> WebSocket`. Generic dispatch (a) is cleaner but depends on trait-method codegen status (Theme 6 — check at ship time); parallel method (b) is the v1 fallback shape. The WebSocket handshake protocol bytes are identical regardless of TLS — the TLS layer is below the application protocol. Tests in `tests/codegen.rs` + `tests/runtime.rs`: WebSocket-over-TLS handshake round-trip, `wss://` echo smoke. ~80 LoC + 4 tests.

  4. [ ] **Slice 4 — test-cert infrastructure.** Self-signed cert + key fixtures committed under `tests/fixtures/tls/` (CN = `localhost`, valid for 10 years to dodge the "tests fail in 2027" trap), `gen_test_cert.sh` script that regenerates them via openssl CLI for reproducibility. Bench harness (Demo 1 slice 3) uses these fixtures rather than expecting users to bring their own. ~30 LoC script + ~6 KB fixture bytes.

  5. [ ] **Slice 5 — design.md update.** Move TLS from `design.md` line 114 ("TLS, HTTP/2, WebSockets — Phase 11") to a v1 status block matching the precedent set when WebSockets moved up. Document the rustls choice, the test-cert convention, and the cross-ref to `Flagship Demo 1`. ~30 LoC doc.

- [ ] **Completion wins cancellation.** Implement the rule that a sibling branch which has already passed its last compiler-inserted effect-boundary check when cancel fires completes naturally and returns `Ok`. Its `defer` blocks must run and its mutations to shared state must remain visible. Real work must never be retroactively converted to `Cancelled`. Whether the `Ok` surfaces at the scope boundary is a separate question governed by the scope-return precedence rules (fail-fast `par` still lets a source-earlier `Err` win; `collect_all` exposes everything). This rule is what makes `collect_all`'s "every branch runs to completion" guarantee load-bearing. See design.md § Parallel Failure and Cleanup.

- [ ] **Cascading cooperative cancellation across nested `par` regions.** When an outer scope cancels, the cancel observation must reach branches inside nested parallel regions through the same cooperative effect-boundary mechanism — no special cross-scope machinery. The effect-boundary check inside the inner branch observes the outer cancel and triggers the inner region's fail-fast, which propagates to the inner region's siblings. No branch should escape cancellation simply because it is nested. Worst-case latency is the sum of effect-boundary distances along the nesting path; document it.

- [x] **`karac query concurrency`.** Return parallelization decisions with reasoning. Moved from Phase 5 — requires concurrency analysis to be implemented first.

- [x] **Parameterized-resource distinctness rules.** Conservative collapse: two parameterized resources `R[a]` and `R[b]` are treated as distinct only when `a` and `b` are distinct string/integer literals at the call site, or are variables provably bound to different values (e.g., different function parameters). When distinctness is ambiguous (computed values, aliases, runtime-determined keys), the compiler conservatively collapses to the same resource and serializes. The rule is intentionally strict: if the programmer cannot predict the outcome without running the compiler, they'll reach for `seq { }` — which is the correct escape hatch, not a failure mode. Future extension: `#[distinct]` annotation to assert distinctness when the compiler can't prove it.

- [x] **Effect-boundary cooperative cancellation (mid-branch).** Shipped 2026-04-28 with conservative over-approximation. `Codegen::branch_cancel_ptr` is set inside `emit_par_branch_fn`; `emit_branch_cancel_check` runs at the head of every `compile_call` and `compile_method_call`. The cancel block drains `scope_cleanup_actions` and returns void from the branch fn. Effectful-narrowing follow-up landed 2026-04-28 (next entry). 2 IR-level tests in `tests/par_codegen.rs` pin both the cancel-check emission and the non-par no-emit guarantee.

- [x] **Mid-branch cancellation follow-up: narrow checks to effectful calls only.** Shipped 2026-04-28. Spec narrows the cancel-check from "every call" to "calls whose callee carries `reads` / `writes` / `sends` / `receives`" (`design.md § Effect-boundary cooperative cancellation`). New `Program.callee_effectful: HashMap<String, bool>` side-table populated by `Pipeline::effectcheck` (helper `build_callee_effectful_table` walks `inferred_effects` ∪ `declared_effects`); copied into `Codegen` at `compile_program` entry, mirror of `Program.question_conversions`. A callee is effectful iff its set carries any of the four resource verbs; `Polymorphic` / `PolymorphicWithFixed` are conservatively `true` (a monomorphization may pick up any effect). `emit_branch_cancel_check` now takes `callee: Option<&str>`; `Some(false)` short-circuits the atomic load, `None` / `Some(true)` / unknown name fall back to the conservative MVP path. `compile_call` recovers the callee key from the AST (`Identifier(n)` → `n`, two-segment `Path` → `seg0.seg1`); `compile_method_call` passes `None` (receiver type isn't known until method resolution). 3 new par_codegen tests pin: effectful helper still fires the check, pure helper elides it (only entry-time check remains), mixed pure+effectful par block emits exactly one check per effectful call. Tests run the full analysis pipeline (`ir_for_with_pipeline`) so the side-table is populated before codegen. **Method-call narrowing follow-up shipped 2026-04-28** (round 2 — see git history `ba2dc9a`): typechecker populates `TypeCheckResult.method_callee_types: HashMap<SpanKey, String>` directly during `infer_method_call` (kept in a separate map rather than reusing `expr_types` because the parser sets `MethodCall.span == receiver.span`, so the receiver-type and method-return-type insertions race at the same key); lowering forwards it to `Program.method_callee_types`; `compile_method_call` derives `Type.method` keys at the call site and consults `callee_effectful`. 2 par_codegen tests added (`test_ir_par_branch_skips_method_check_for_pure_callee` and `test_ir_par_branch_emits_method_check_for_effectful_callee`). No remaining open follow-ups on this entry. Files (round 1): `src/ast.rs`, `src/cli.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `tests/par_codegen.rs`. Files (round 2): `src/ast.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/lowering.rs`, `src/codegen.rs`, `tests/par_codegen.rs`.

- [ ] **`collect_all { }` language syntax.** Gather-all-errors variant of `par { }`. All branches run to completion (no fail-fast); returns `Vec[Result[T, E]]` with one entry per branch. Needs: parser support for `collect_all` keyword, runtime gather mode (no cancel-on-error), result struct ABI in codegen.

- [ ] **`Never` type inference rules — `LUB(Never, T) = T` + fallback to `Never` (not `()`).** Spec lives at design.md § Type Inference (v60 item 30). Sub-steps: (1) LUB algorithm — extend the LUB function in the typechecker so that `LUB(Never, T) = T` and `LUB(T, Never) = T` for every type `T`. The rule is rule 0 (matches before identical-types), so an if-else with one diverging arm and one concrete-typed arm joins to the concrete type; an if-else with both arms diverging joins to `Never`. (2) Inference fallback — when a metavariable's only solving constraint is a value of type `Never` (a generic call whose only concrete argument has type `Never`, a diverging closure body, a `vec![panic!()]`-style construction with a single `Never`-typed element), solve the metavariable to `Never` rather than letting it remain unsolved or defaulting to `()`. The mechanic: when the substitution-finalize step finds a metavariable with no concrete-type constraints but with a `Never <: ?T` subsumption record, `?T := Never`. (3) Mixed-constraint case unchanged — when a metavariable has both `Never <: ?T` and `Concrete <: ?T` constraints, the LUB rule from (1) already produces the concrete type; no special fallback logic needed for this path. (4) Diagnostics — `karac explain` includes the metavariable's chosen value in inference traces; the `Never`-fallback case is identified explicitly so a programmer reading the trace sees "T solved to Never (no concrete constraint)". (5) Test plan: `let y = id(panic!())` with `fn id[T](x: T) -> T` — assert `y : Never`; closure `|| panic!()` — return type `Never`; `vec![todo()]` — element type `Never`; `pick(42, panic!())` — joins to `i64` (LUB rule, not fallback); `pick(panic!(), panic!())` — joins to `Never` (LUB collapses to identical-types case after rule 0); `let x: () = panic!()` — accepted via existing Never-coerces-to-any rule (annotation present, fallback doesn't fire); `if cond { panic!() } else { 5 }` — type `i64` via LUB rule. (Phase 5.2 — touches the LUB algorithm and metavariable substitution-finalize; both already exist in the typechecker, so the work is rule additions and targeted test coverage, not new infrastructure.)

- [ ] **`if let` / `while let` / `let...else` scrutinee temporary scope.** Spec lives at design.md § `if let` and `let...else` (v60 item 29). Sub-steps: (1) NLL/drop-placement pass — verify that scrutinee-expression temporaries (anonymous intermediates produced by the right-hand side of `=` in `if let PAT = SCRUT { … } else { … }`, `while let PAT = SCRUT { … }`, `let PAT = SCRUT else { … };`) have a live range scoped to the matching arm: in the `then` arm of `if let`, the temporaries live through the entire body and drop at arm exit (because pattern-bound names may borrow into them); in the `else` arm of `if let` / `else if let` / `let...else`, the temporaries have already been dropped *before* the arm body begins; in `while let`, per-iteration drop at body exit before the next iteration's scrutinee is evaluated. (2) Code-path verification — verify the code path that lowers `if let` / `let-else` / `while let` to control flow places the scrutinee-temp drops on the *non-matching* edge before the else-arm code (rather than placing them at the join point after both arms). The lowering pattern: evaluate scrutinee → match against pattern → on miss, drop temps then jump to else; on hit, bind names then enter then-arm body, drop temps at body exit. (3) Pattern-binding interaction — pattern-bound names (`value` in `if let Some(value) = ...`) are local bindings of the arm, NOT temporaries; their drop follows the standard `let`-binding rules and is unaffected by this item. The rule covers only the anonymous intermediates of the scrutinee expression. (4) Deferred composition — the future `if let` chains feature (deferred to Phase 5+) will apply the same rule per-link: each link's temporaries drop before the next link is evaluated (on success) or before the else arm runs (on failure). (5) Test plan: lock-in-scrutinee `if let Some(v) = mu.lock().get(k) { ... } else { log(...) }` — assert via instrumented destructors that the MutexGuard's `Drop` fires before the else block runs; `let Ok(config) = parse(mu.lock().as_str()) else { return Err(...) };` — guard drops before the divergent else block; `while let Some(item) = mu.lock().pop_front() { process(item) }` — per-iteration lock release verified by instrumented drop order across iterations; pattern-bound name lifetime in then-arm holds borrows into scrutinee temps without dangling. (Phase 4 / Phase 5.2 — touches the existing live-range placement and pattern-match lowering paths; no new IR or codegen, just verification + targeted lowering placement.)

- [ ] **Tail-expression temporary scope — drop before block locals.** Spec lives at design.md § Drop ordering within a branch (v60 item 28). Sub-steps: (1) NLL/drop-placement pass — verify that a temporary created inside a block's tail expression has a live range ending immediately after the tail expression finishes evaluating (including borrow uses chained off it), and that its drop is pushed onto the unified LIFO drop+defer stack *after* every `let` binding's drop in the same block. The rule is implicit in the existing program-order-LIFO design (the tail expression is later in source order than every `let`, so its temporaries push last and pop first), but the verification is required to catch any code path that hoisted tail-expression temporaries to the block's outer scope (the pre-Rust-2024 behavior). (2) Move-out exception — when the tail expression's value (the temporary itself) is moved out of the block, its live range escapes; no drop is inserted in this scope. The standard NLL move-out rule already covers this; verify the tail-expression case shares the code path. (3) Statement-position temporaries (an expression-statement ending in `;`) continue to drop at the `;` — unchanged from the existing design. (4) Test plan: lock-in-tail pattern (`mu.lock().get(k).clone()`) — assert that the MutexGuard's `Drop` runs before any preceding `let` binding's `Drop` via instrumented destructors that record drop order; tail expression that moves out a temporary (`fn make_guard(mu) -> MutexGuard { mu.lock() }`) — no drop inserted in this scope; nested blocks (`{ let x = …; { let y = …; tail_expr() } }`) — inner-block tail-temp drops before inner `y`, both before outer `x`; tail expression that uses a borrow into a let-binding — the borrow's source binding stays live until the tail expression's drop fires (otherwise the borrow would dangle). (Phase 4 / Phase 5.2 — touches the existing live-range placement code; no new IR or codegen, just a verification pass on the existing NLL output.)

- [ ] **Panic semantics at the FFI boundary — `extern "C"` auto-abort + `extern "C-unwind"` propagation.** Spec lives at design.md § Panic Semantics at the FFI Boundary (v60 item 27). Sub-steps: (1) Codegen — for every `pub extern "C" fn` defined in Kāra, emit two LLVM symbols: (a) the bare Kāra-callable function (mangled by the standard rules unless `#[unsafe(no_mangle)]` overrides) and (b) a separate exported wrapper symbol with the C-facing name that wraps the call in a `catch_panic`-equivalent landing pad and routes any caught panic to `std.process.abort()`. Kāra-internal calls go through the bare symbol with no overhead; C-side calls go through the trampoline. The trampoline's abort path writes the panic message + source location to stderr before calling `abort()`. (2) Codegen elision — under `panic = "abort"` build profile, the trampoline is a no-op (every panic is already abort); emit only the bare symbol with the C-facing name (or the wrapper as a tail-call that just forwards). (3) Build-profile gate — `extern "C-unwind"` definitions and imports are rejected at parse under `panic = "abort"` profiles with `error[E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE]`. The same gate already rejects `catch_panic` calls under abort profiles (per item 26's checklist entry); both rejections share the diagnostic surface. (4) Typechecker — `pub extern "C-unwind" fn` definitions whose body's inferred effects include `panics` MUST declare `panics` in the signature; otherwise emit `error[E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_PANICS]` with a suggested-fix span adding `with panics` to the signature. `pub extern "C" fn` definitions MAY declare `panics`; the declared effect describes Kāra-side calls (the boundary trampoline is invisible to the effect system). (5) Effect-system integration — no new rules needed beyond (4); the existing inference and propagation machinery handles all four cases (import/export × C/C-unwind) uniformly because the trampoline is a codegen-only artifact. (6) FFI absorption pattern — the design recommends wrapping the body in `catch_panic` to surface errors to C as error codes rather than relying on auto-abort; the auto-abort trampoline is the safety net for panics that escape the user-written catch (e.g., panic during the panic-handler logic). Test plan (when codegen lands): `pub extern "C" fn double(x: i32) -> i32 { x.checked_mul(2).unwrap() }` called from a C harness with overflowing input → process aborts with the panic message on stderr; same function called from Kāra → panic propagates normally; `pub extern "C-unwind" fn parse_or_throw(...)` called from a C++ harness with a `try { } catch (...) { }` block → exception caught on the C++ side; `pub extern "C-unwind" fn` body that may panic but signature omits `with panics` → typecheck rejection; under `kernel` profile, `extern "C-unwind"` declaration → parse rejection; round-trip via `catch_panic` inside `pub extern "C" fn` → no abort, returns C-shaped error code. (Phase 7 — depends on LLVM unwinding substrate from item 26; trampoline emission is a codegen pattern, not a typechecker change.)

- [ ] **`catch_panic[T]` panic-absorption primitive.** Spec lives at design.md § Catching Panics: `catch_panic[T]` (v60 item 26). Sub-steps: (1) Typechecker — recognise `catch_panic` as a `#[compiler_builtin]` with the special signature `fn catch_panic[T, with E](f: Fn() -> T with E) -> Result[T, PanicInfo] with (E - panics)`. The `(E - panics)` arithmetic is closed-form in the compiler — it is not a user-writable pattern. At every call site, the result type's effect ceiling is the closure's effect set with `panics` removed; if the closure does not have `panics`, `karac lint` flags the call as a likely mistake but the call remains legal (always returns `Ok`). (2) Build-profile gate — under `panic = "abort"` (kernel/embedded/ISR profiles), `catch_panic` calls are rejected at typecheck with `error[E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND]: catch_panic is unavailable under panic = "abort"; remove the call or change the build profile`. The same gate rejects `extern "C-unwind"` declarations under abort builds. (3) Stdlib — `PanicInfo` (with `message`, `location`, `kind`, `thread_name`, `backtrace`), `PanicKind` (`#[non_exhaustive]` enum: `Explicit`, `Unwrap`, `Indexing`, `IntegerOverflow`, `DivisionByZero`, `ContractViolation`, `Foreign`, `DropDuringUnwind`), `SourceLocation` types in the prelude (paired with `catch_panic` and the panic-hook surface). `PanicInfo` is `Send + Clone`. (4) Codegen (Phase 7) — lower `catch_panic(closure)` to LLVM's `invoke` instruction with a landing pad that catches the unwind, captures `PanicInfo` from the runtime panic-payload, and routes to the `Err(...)` arm. The runtime side maintains a thread-local "in-flight panic" tag; `process.exit()` sets the tag to `Exit` rather than `Recoverable`, and the catch-frame inspects the tag and re-raises rather than producing `Err(PanicInfo)` (per the design.md/process.exit interaction rule, originally pinned in deferred.md). (5) Auto-concurrency interaction — `catch_panic` does not extend the panic-domination rule for parallel scopes; a panic absorbed inside a single branch produces `Ok(Err(PanicInfo))` from that branch, the parallel scope sees a successful result, no peer cancellation. The structured-concurrency machinery already does its own internal panic-isolation at task boundaries; `catch_panic` is the user-facing surface of the same primitive. (6) Drop-time interaction — destructor panics during the closure's normal scope-exit produce `Err(PanicInfo { kind: DropDuringUnwind, ... })`; destructor panics *during* an in-flight unwind that `catch_panic` is already absorbing become double-panics and abort the process (no double-panic protection). (7) FFI integration — panics that crossed an `extern "C-unwind"` ABI boundary surface as `PanicKind.Foreign`; the absorption pattern from the FFI section uses `catch_panic` directly. Test plan (when codegen lands): explicit `panic!` inside closure → `Err` with `Explicit`; out-of-bounds index → `Err` with `Indexing`; `process.exit(2)` propagates through (verified via subprocess test); double-panic during catch → process-aborts; `catch_panic` under `panic = "abort"` profile → typecheck error; closure carrying `with reads(Db) writes(Cache) panics` produces a `Result` whose result-type's effect ceiling is `with reads(Db) writes(Cache)` (panics stripped, others passed through). (Phase 7 — depends on LLVM unwinding substrate; typechecker stub work can land in Phase 5.2 to gate the build-profile rejection diagnostics.)

- [x] **Scheduler minimum invariants (language-level, cross-scheduler). Implemented:** The Phase 6 scheduler and any future runtime profile must satisfy five invariants that programs written against language-level rules rely on: (1) **no lost work** — a completed branch's `Ok` result is never silently discarded (it reaches the scope return, a `collect_all` result, or at minimum its `defer`/mutations still run); (2) **cancellation eventually observed** — every branch either completes or observes cancellation in bounded time after a triggering event; (3) **cancellation cascades** into nested regions; (4) **termination** — programs without pure tight loops terminate when all branches finish or cancel; (5) **scheduler deadlock-freedom** — the scheduler itself must not introduce deadlock beyond what user-level locks can create. Backpressure under overload, fairness between unrelated regions, and scheduler-specific cancel optimizations are **not** in this invariant set — they are per-profile concerns deferred to runtime chapters, and programs that depend on them must declare the dependency in their build profile. See design.md § Scheduler-layer concerns and minimum invariants.

- [ ] **Cost-model specification (v1.x).** Feature 5 currently uses a degenerate cost model: parallelize whenever distinctness allows it and `ParallelGroup.is_trivial` is false; trivial pure-computation groups go sequential. The full v1.x cost-model spec — per-call cost heuristic (cheap/medium/expensive based on body shape: pure arithmetic vs. allocation vs. I/O vs. effect class), fork threshold (sum-of-costs vs. scheduling overhead), loop-body parallelization rule (whether iterations of a `for` over a pure body fork), distinctness-policy when parameterized-resource keys are dynamic — is deferred until Parallax-lite (the same workload that grounds Item 7's Cumulative Cost Surface measurement, see roadmap.md Phase 8) provides empirical numbers to tune against. Specifying a model without measurement risks locking in numbers that turn out to be wrong. **Determinism requirement:** cost-model decisions must be a pure function of (source, compiler version, target profile) — same inputs always produce the same parallelization graph; no runtime nondeterminism, no host-environment leakage. Cross-version improvements ride the Reported Behavior layer (changelog-itemized; tools that consume `karac query concurrency` tolerate version skew). See `design.md § Feature 5 > Cost Model — v1 Status`.
